(2 Kings 1:1) 
After Ahab died, the nation of Moab revolted against Israel.

(2 Kings 1:2) 
Ahaziah fell through the lattice of his upper chamber, which he had in Samaria, and he became very ill. He then sent messengers, telling them: "Go, consult Beelzebub, the idol-god of Ekron, to see if I will recover from this sickness."

(2 Kings 1:3) 
However, the Angel of the Lord spoke to Elijah the Tishbite, saying: "Get up and go meet the messengers of the king of Samaria. Then you shall say to them: 'Is there truly no God in Israel that you must go to consult Beelzebub, the idol-god of Ekron?'"

(2 Kings 1:4) 
Therefore, this is what the Lord says: 'You will not leave the bed upon which you have climbed, but you will surely die.' And Elijah then departed.

(2 Kings 1:5) 
And the messengers returned to Ahaziah. He asked them: "Why have you returned?"

(2 Kings 1:6) 
They answered him: "A man met us and spoke to us, saying: 'Go, and return to the king who sent you, and speak to him: Thus says the Lord: "Is there truly no God in Israel that you send to consult Beelzebub, the idol-god of Ekron? Therefore, from the bed upon which you have climbed, you shall not descend, but you will surely die."'

(2 Kings 1:7) 
Ahaziah asked them: "What was the appearance and manner of that man who met you and spoke these words to you?"

(2 Kings 1:8) 
And they told him: "He was a hairy man, with a leather belt wrapped around his waist." The king immediately knew and said: "It is Elijah the Tishbite!"

(2 Kings 1:9) 
So the king sent a captain of fifty soldiers with his fifty men to Elijah. The captain went up to him, and Elijah was sitting on the top of a mountain. And the captain spoke to him: "Man of God, the king commands that you come down!"

(2 Kings 1:10) 
And Elijah responded, saying to the captain of fifty: "If I am a man of God, then let fire descend from the sky and consume you and your fifty men." And immediately fire descended from the sky, and it consumed him and the fifty men who were with him.

(2 Kings 1:11) 
Again, the king sent to him a second captain of fifty soldiers with his fifty men. He spoke to Elijah: "Man of God, this is what the king says: 'Hurry, come down!'"

(2 Kings 1:12) 
And Elijah responded, saying: "If I am a man of God, then let fire descend from the sky and consume you and your fifty men." And immediately fire descended from the sky, and it consumed him and the fifty men who were with him.

(2 Kings 1:13) 
Again, the king sent a third captain of fifty soldiers with his fifty men. When he came, he knelt before Elijah and pleaded with him, saying: "Man of God, please do not despise my life, nor the lives of these fifty servants of yours."

(2 Kings 1:14) 
He continued: "Behold, fire has descended from the sky and consumed the first two captains of fifty and the fifty men who were under each of them. But now, I beg you, have mercy on my life!"

(2 Kings 1:15) 
And the Angel of the Lord spoke to Elijah, saying: "Go down with him, do not be afraid." So Elijah rose up and went down with him to the king.

(2 Kings 1:16) 
And Elijah spoke to the king: "Thus says the Lord: 'Because you sent messengers to consult Beelzebub, the idol-god of Ekron, as if there were no God in Israel whose word could be inquired of, therefore you will not leave the bed upon which you have climbed, but you will surely die.'"

(2 Kings 1:17) 
So Ahaziah died according to the word of the Lord which Elijah had spoken. And Joram, his brother, reigned in his place in the second year of Jehoram, son of Jehoshaphat, king of Judah, because Ahaziah had no son.

(2 Kings 1:18) 
As for the rest of the deeds of Ahaziah, and what he accomplished, are these not written in the book of the chronicles of the kings of Israel?

(2 Kings 1:1) 
After King Ahab died, the kingdom of Moab rebelled against the kingdom of Israel.

(2 Kings 1:2) 
Now King Ahaziah fell through the lattice of his upper chamber, which he had in Samaria, and he became very sick. He then sent messengers, telling them, 'Go, inquire of Baal-Zebub, the god of Ekron, whether I will recover from this illness.'

(2 Kings 1:3) 
But the Angel of the Lord spoke to Elijah the Tishbite, saying, 'Arise, and go up to meet the messengers of the king of Samaria, and you shall say to them: Is there no God in Israel, that you go to inquire of Baal-Zebub, the god of Ekron?'

(2 Kings 1:4) 
Therefore, this is what the Lord says: 'From the bed upon which you have climbed, you shall not descend, but you will surely die.' And Elijah went away to deliver this message.

(2 Kings 1:5) 
So the messengers returned to King Ahaziah. And he said to them, 'Why have you returned so quickly?'

(2 Kings 1:6) 
And they answered, 'A man met us and said to us: 'Go, and return to the king who sent you, and you shall tell him: This is what the Lord says: Is there no God in Israel, that you send to inquire of Baal-Zebub, the god of Ekron? Therefore, from the bed upon which you have climbed, you shall not descend, but you will surely die.''

(2 Kings 1:7) 
And the king said to them, 'What kind of man was he who met you and spoke these words?'

(2 Kings 1:8) 
And they described him, saying, 'He was a hairy man, with a leather belt fastened around his waist.' And the king immediately realized, 'It is Elijah the Tishbite.'

(2 Kings 1:9) 
So the king sent a captain of fifty men, with his fifty soldiers who were under him, to Elijah. The captain went up to Elijah; and behold, Elijah was sitting on the top of a mountain. And the captain spoke to him, saying, 'Man of God, the king commands that you come down.'

(2 Kings 1:10) 
And Elijah answered the captain of fifty, 'If I am a man of God, let fire come down from the sky and consume you and your fifty men.' So fire came down from the sky and consumed him and the fifty men who were with him.

(2 Kings 1:11) 
Again, King Ahaziah sent another captain of fifty men and fifty with him. And that captain spoke to Elijah, 'Man of God, the king says this: 'Hurry, come down!''

(2 Kings 1:12) 
And Elijah answered him, 'If I am a man of God, let fire come down from the sky and consume you and your fifty men.' Therefore, fire came down from the sky and consumed that captain and the fifty men who were with him.

(2 Kings 1:13) 
Again, King Ahaziah sent a third captain of fifty men, with the fifty who were with him. When this captain came, he knelt down before Elijah, and pleaded with him, and spoke: 'Man of God, please do not despise my life, nor the lives of these fifty servants of yours.'

(2 Kings 1:14) 
'For behold, fire has come down from the sky and consumed the two former captains of fifty and the fifty men who were with them. But now, I beg you, have mercy on my life.'

(2 Kings 1:15) 
Then the Angel of the Lord spoke to Elijah, saying, 'Go down with him; do not be afraid.' So Elijah arose and went down with the captain to the king,

(2 Kings 1:16) 
and he spoke to King Ahaziah: 'This is what the Lord says: 'Because you sent messengers to inquire of Baal-Zebub, the god of Ekron, as if there were no God in Israel whose word you could inquire of, therefore, from the bed upon which you have climbed, you shall not descend, but you will surely die.''

(2 Kings 1:17) 
So King Ahaziah died according to the word of the Lord which Elijah had spoken. And his brother Jehoram (Joram) reigned in his place in the second year of Jehoram, the son of King Jehoshaphat of Judah, because Ahaziah had no son.

(2 Kings 1:18) 
Now the rest of the acts of Ahaziah, all that he did, are they not written in the book of the chronicles of the kings of Israel?

(2 Kings 1:19) 
Now it came to pass, when the Lord was about to take Elijah up to the sky in a whirlwind, that Elijah and Elisha were going from Gilgal.

(2 Kings 1:20) 
And Elijah said to Elisha, 'Please stay here, for the Lord has sent me as far as Bethel.' Elisha replied to him, 'As the Lord lives, and as your soul lives, I will not leave you.' And when they had gone down to Bethel,

(2 Kings 1:21) 
the sons of the prophets who were in Bethel came out to Elisha and said to him, 'Do you know that today the Lord is taking your master from you?' And Elisha responded, 'Yes, I know; be silent about it.'

(2 Kings 1:22) 
And Elijah said to Elisha, 'Elisha, please stay here, for the Lord has sent me as far as Jericho.' And Elisha replied, 'As the Lord lives, and as your soul lives, I will not leave you.' And when they had come to Jericho,

(2 Kings 1:23) 
the sons of the prophets who were in Jericho approached Elisha and said to him, 'Do you know that today the Lord is taking your master from you?' And Elisha replied, 'Yes, I know; be silent about it.'

(2 Kings 1:24) 
And Elijah said to him, 'Please stay here, for the Lord has sent me as far as the Jordan River.' Elisha replied, 'As the Lord lives, and as your soul lives, I will not leave you.' So both of them continued on their journey.

(2 Kings 1:25) 
Furthermore, fifty men from the sons of the prophets followed them; and they stood facing them, from a distance, while Elijah and Elisha both stood by the Jordan.

(2 Kings 1:26) 
Then Elijah took his mantle, rolled it up, and struck the waters of the Jordan, which then divided to both sides. And both Elijah and Elisha crossed over on dry ground.

(2 Kings 1:27) 
When they had crossed, Elijah said to Elisha, 'Ask what you desire for me to do for you, before I am taken from you.' And Elisha said, 'I beg you, let a double portion of your spirit be upon me.'

(2 Kings 1:28) 
Elijah answered, 'You have asked a difficult thing. Nevertheless, if you see me when I am taken from you, it shall be granted to you as you have asked; but if you do not see me, it will not be granted.'

(2 Kings 1:29) 
As they walked on and talked together, behold, a fiery chariot and fiery horses appeared and separated the two of them. And Elijah ascended by a whirlwind into the sky.

(2 Kings 1:30) 
But Elisha, seeing this, cried out, 'My father, my father! The chariot of Israel and its horsemen!' And he saw Elijah no longer. Then Elisha took hold of his own clothes and tore them into two pieces.

(2 Kings 1:31) 
And Elisha picked up the mantle of Elijah that had fallen from him. Then he returned and stood by the bank of the Jordan River.

(2 Kings 1:32) 
And with the mantle of Elijah, which had fallen from him, Elisha struck the waters, but they did not divide. Then he said, 'Where is the God of Elijah now?' And again he struck the waters, and they divided to one side and to the other; and Elisha crossed over.

(2 Kings 1:33) 
Now when the sons of the prophets who were in Jericho saw him from a distance, they said, 'The spirit of Elijah rests upon Elisha.' And coming to meet him, they bowed down to the ground before him,

(2 Kings 1:34) 
and they said to him, 'Behold, we have fifty strong men with us who can go and search for your master. Perhaps the Spirit of the Lord has taken him up and cast him upon one of the mountains, or into one of the valleys.' But Elisha replied, 'Do not send them.'

(2 Kings 1:35) 
But they urged him until he consented, saying, 'Send them.' So they sent fifty men, who searched for three days but did not find Elijah.

(2 Kings 1:36) 
When they returned to Elisha, who was still waiting in Jericho, he said to them, 'Did I not tell you: 'Do not send them?'

(2 Kings 1:37) 
Now the men of the city of Jericho also said to Elisha, 'Behold, the dwelling place of this city is excellent, as you yourself, our lord, perceive. But the waters are very bad, and the land is barren.'

(2 Kings 1:38) 
And Elisha said, 'Bring me a new jar and put salt in it.' So when they brought it to him,

(2 Kings 1:39) 
he went out to the spring of the waters, and cast the salt into it, and said: 'This is what the Lord says: 'I have healed these waters, and there shall be no more death or barrenness in them from now on.''

(2 Kings 1:40) 
So the waters were healed to this very day, according to the word of Elisha, which he had spoken.

(2 Kings 1:1) 
But after King Ahab died, the kingdom of Moab rebelled against Israel.

(2 Kings 1:2) 
But King Ahaziah fell through the lattice of his upper room, which he had in Samaria, and became gravely ill. So he sent messengers, telling them, 'Go, consult Beelzebub, the pagan god of Ekron, to see if I will recover from this illness.'

(2 Kings 1:3) 
However, the Angel of the Lord spoke to Elijah the Tishbite, instructing him: 'Go now, ascend to meet the messengers of the king of Samaria, and say to them: "Is there no God in Israel, that you must go and consult Beelzebub, the pagan god of Ekron?"'

(2 Kings 1:4) 
Therefore, the Lord declares this: 'You shall not get up from the sickbed you are on; instead, you will certainly die.' With this message, Elijah departed.

(2 Kings 1:5) 
When the messengers returned to King Ahaziah, he asked them, 'Why have you come back?'

(2 Kings 1:6) 
They answered him, 'A man met us and told us, "Go back to the king who sent you, and tell him: 'This is what the Lord says: Is there no God in Israel, that you must send to consult Beelzebub, the pagan god of Ekron? Because of this, you will not get up from the sickbed you are on; instead, you will certainly die.'"'

(2 Kings 1:7) 
He then asked them, 'What kind of man was it who met you and spoke these words to you?'

(2 Kings 1:8) 
They replied, 'He was a man dressed in a rough, hairy garment, with a leather belt around his waist.' The king then realized, 'It is Elijah the Tishbite!'

(2 Kings 1:9) 
So the king sent to him a captain of fifty men with his fifty soldiers. The captain went up to Elijah, who was sitting on the top of a mountain, and addressed him, 'Man of God, the king commands you: "Come down!"'

(2 Kings 1:10) 
Elijah answered the captain of fifty, 'If I am a man of God, then let fire come down from the sky and consume both you and your fifty men.' Immediately, fire descended from the sky and consumed him and all fifty of his soldiers.

(2 Kings 1:11) 
Again, the king sent another captain of fifty with his fifty soldiers. This captain addressed Elijah, 'Man of God, this is what the king says: "Hurry, come down!"'

(2 Kings 1:12) 
Elijah answered him, 'If I am a man of God, then let fire come down from the sky and consume both you and your fifty men.' Immediately, fire descended from the sky and consumed him and his fifty soldiers.

(2 Kings 1:13) 
Once more, the king sent a third captain of fifty with his fifty soldiers. When this captain arrived, he humbly knelt before Elijah and pleaded with him, saying, 'Man of God, please do not disregard my life, nor the lives of these fifty servants of yours.'

(2 Kings 1:14) 
Behold, fire has already come down from the sky and consumed the first two captains of fifty with their fifty men. Now, I beg you, spare my life.

(2 Kings 1:15) 
Then the Angel of the Lord spoke to Elijah, saying, 'Go down with him; do not be afraid.' So Elijah rose, and went down with the captain to the king.

(2 Kings 1:16) 
Elijah then spoke to the king, saying, 'This is what the Lord declares: Because you sent messengers to consult Beelzebub, the pagan god of Ekron, as if there were no God in Israel from whom you could seek a prophetic word, you will not get up from the sickbed you are on; instead, you will certainly die.'

(2 Kings 1:17) 
So King Ahaziah died according to the word of the Lord that Elijah had spoken. His brother Joram then reigned in his place, because Ahaziah had no son. This occurred in the second year of Joram, son of King Jehoshaphat of Judah.

(2 Kings 1:18) 
As for the rest of the acts of King Ahaziah, and all that he did, are they not indeed written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?

(2 Kings 2:1) 
Now it came about, when the Lord was about to take Elijah up into glory by means of a whirlwind, that Elijah and Elisha departed from Gilgal.

(2 Kings 2:2) 
And Elijah said to Elisha: 'Stay here, I beg you, because the Lord has sent me on a mission to Bethel.' And Elisha replied: 'As the Lord lives, and as your soul lives, I will not leave you.' So they both went down to Bethel.

(2 Kings 2:3) 
Then the sons of the prophets who were in Bethel came out to Elisha and said to him: 'Do you know that today the Lord is taking your master from you?' And he answered: 'Yes, I know; be silent.'

(2 Kings 2:4) 
And Elijah said to Elisha: 'Stay here, I beg you, because the Lord has sent me on a mission to Jericho.' But he replied: 'As the Lord lives, and as your soul lives, I will not leave you.' So they both went to Jericho.

(2 Kings 2:5) 
Then the sons of the prophets who were in Jericho approached Elisha and said to him: 'Do you know that today the Lord is taking your master from you?' And he replied: 'Yes, I know; be silent.'

(2 Kings 2:6) 
And Elijah said to him: 'Stay here, I beg you, because the Lord has sent me on a mission as far as the Jordan River.' But he replied: 'As the Lord lives, and as your soul lives, I will not leave you.' So they both continued on their way.

(2 Kings 2:7) 
And fifty men from the sons of the prophets followed them and stood at a distance, watching them. But Elijah and Elisha both stood by the Jordan River.

(2 Kings 2:8) 
Then Elijah took his cloak, rolled it up, and struck the waters of the river. And the waters divided to both sides, so that both of them crossed over on dry ground.

(2 Kings 2:9) 
And when they had crossed over, Elijah said to Elisha: 'Ask what you wish me to do for you before I am taken from you.' And Elisha replied: 'I beg that a double portion of your spiritual power may come upon me.'

(2 Kings 2:10) 
He answered: 'You have asked a difficult thing. Nevertheless, if you see me when I am taken from you, then what you have asked will be granted to you. But if you do not see me, it will not be.'

(2 Kings 2:11) 
And as they continued on their way, speaking together as they walked, behold, a chariot of fire and horses of fire separated the two of them. And Elijah ascended into glory by means of a whirlwind.

(2 Kings 2:12) 
But Elisha saw it, and he cried out: 'My father, my father! The chariot of Israel and its horsemen!' And he saw him no more. Then he took hold of his own clothes and tore them into two pieces.

(2 Kings 2:13) 
And he picked up the cloak of Elijah, which had fallen from him. Then he returned and stood on the bank of the Jordan River.

(2 Kings 2:14) 
And with the cloak of Elijah, which had fallen from him, he struck the waters, but they did not divide. Then he said: 'Where is the God of Elijah now?' And he struck the waters again, and they divided to both sides. So Elisha crossed over.

(2 Kings 2:15) 
Now when the sons of the prophets who were in Jericho saw him from across the river, they said: 'The spiritual power of Elijah rests upon Elisha.' And they came to meet him, bowing down to the ground before him.

(2 Kings 2:16) 
And they said to him: 'Behold, there are fifty strong men among your servants, who could go and search for your master. Perhaps the Spirit of the Lord has taken him up and cast him upon one of the mountains or into one of the valleys.' But he said: 'Do not send anyone.'

(2 Kings 2:17) 
But they urged him until he consented and said: 'Send them.' So they sent fifty men, and after they had searched for three days, they did not find him.

(2 Kings 2:18) 
And when they returned to Elisha, who was sitting in Jericho, he said to them: 'Did I not tell you, 'Do not send anyone?'

(2 Kings 2:19) 
Then the men of the city said to Elisha: 'Behold, the situation of this city is excellent, as you yourself, my master, can see. But the waters are bad, and the land is barren.'

(2 Kings 2:20) 
And he said: 'Bring me a new bowl and put salt in it.' And when they had brought it to him,

(2 Kings 2:21) 
he went to the spring of waters and cast the salt into it, and said: 'Thus says the Lord: I have healed these waters. From now on, there will be no more death or barrenness in them.'

(2 Kings 2:22) 
So the waters were healed to this very day, according to the word of Elisha, which he had spoken.

(2 Kings 2:23) 
And from there he went up to Bethel. And as he was going up by the way, some small boys came out of the city and mocked him, saying: 'Go up, you bald head! Go up, you bald head!'

(2 Kings 2:24) 
When he looked back, he saw them and cursed them in the name of the Lord. And two she-bears came out of the forest and mauled forty-two of the boys.

(2 Kings 2:25) 
And he went from there to Mount Carmel, and from there he returned to Samaria.

(2 Kings 2:1) 
When the Lord was about to take Elijah up into the heavens by means of a whirlwind, Elijah and Elisha were traveling from Gilgal.

(2 Kings 2:2) 
And Elijah said to Elisha, 'Please, stay here, because the Lord has sent me as far as Bethel.' To which Elisha replied, 'As the Lord lives, and as your very self lives, I will not leave you.' So they both went down to Bethel.

(2 Kings 2:3) 
Then the company of prophets who were in Bethel came out to meet Elisha, and they asked him, 'Do you know that today the Lord is taking your master from you?' And he replied, 'Yes, I know that also; be silent.'

(2 Kings 2:4) 
Then Elijah said to Elisha again, 'Elisha, please stay here, because the Lord has sent me as far as Jericho.' But Elisha insisted, 'As the Lord lives, and as your very self lives, I will not leave you.' So they both went on to Jericho.

(2 Kings 2:5) 
And the company of prophets who were in Jericho came to Elisha and asked him, 'Do you know that today the Lord is taking your master from you?' He replied, 'Yes, I know that also; be silent.'

(2 Kings 2:6) 
Then Elijah said to him, 'Please, cross the Jordan, and stay here, because the Lord has sent me as far as the Jordan River.' But Elisha affirmed again, 'As the Lord lives, and as your very self lives, I will not leave you.' So both of them continued on their way.

(2 Kings 2:7) 
And fifty men from the company of prophets followed them and stood watching from a distance, directly opposite them. But Elijah and Elisha themselves stood by the Jordan River.

(2 Kings 2:8) 
Then Elijah took his mantle, rolled it up, and struck the waters of the Jordan. The waters parted to both sides, and both Elijah and Elisha crossed over on dry ground.

(2 Kings 2:9) 
When they had crossed over, Elijah said to Elisha, 'Ask what you wish for me to do for you, before I am taken from you.' Elisha then replied, 'I beg you, let a double portion of your prophetic spirit be upon me.'

(2 Kings 2:10) 
Elijah responded, 'You have asked a difficult thing. Nevertheless, if you see me when I am taken from you, then what you have asked will be granted to you. But if you do not see me, it will not be.'

(2 Kings 2:11) 
And as they continued on their way, still talking, behold, a chariot of fire and horses of fire appeared and separated the two of them. Then Elijah went up into the heavens by means of a whirlwind.

(2 Kings 2:12) 
But Elisha saw it, and he cried out, 'My father, my father! The chariot of Israel and its horseman!' —a declaration of Israel's strength and Elijah's importance. And he saw Elijah no more. Then, in his grief, Elisha took hold of his own clothes and tore them into two pieces.

(2 Kings 2:13) 
Then Elisha picked up Elijah’s mantle, which had fallen from him. He turned back and stood by the bank of the Jordan River.

(2 Kings 2:14) 
And with Elijah’s mantle, which had fallen from him, he struck the waters of the Jordan, but they did not part. So Elisha cried out, 'Where is the Lord, the God of Elijah, now?' He then struck the waters again, and they parted to both sides, and Elisha crossed over.

(2 Kings 2:15) 
When the company of prophets from Jericho, who had been watching from across the river, saw this, they declared, 'The spirit of Elijah rests upon Elisha!' And they came to meet him, bowing down before him with their faces to the ground.

(2 Kings 2:16) 
And they said to him, 'Behold, your servants have fifty strong men with us who could go and search for your master. Perhaps the Spirit of the Lord has taken him up and cast him upon one of the mountains or into one of the valleys.' But Elisha said, 'Do not send them.'

(2 Kings 2:17) 
But they urged him so persistently that he finally gave in and said, 'Send them.' So they sent fifty men, who searched for three days but did not find him.

(2 Kings 2:18) 
When they returned to Elisha — for he was staying in Jericho — he said to them, 'Did I not tell you, 'Do not send them?'

(2 Kings 2:19) 
Then the men of the city of Jericho said to Elisha, 'Behold, the situation of this city is excellent, as you yourself, our master, can see. But its waters are very bad, and the land is unproductive.'

(2 Kings 2:20) 
But Elisha said, 'Bring me a new jar, and put salt in it.' So they brought it to him.

(2 Kings 2:21) 
Then Elisha went out to the spring of the waters, and he cast the salt into it, declaring, 'Thus says the Lord: 'I have now healed these waters. From this moment on, there will be no more death nor barrenness from them.'' 

(2 Kings 2:22) 
And the waters have remained healed to this very day, according to the prophetic word that Elisha spoke.

(2 Kings 2:23) 
From there, Elisha went up towards Bethel. As he was going up by the road, some young lads came out from the city and began to mock him, shouting, 'Go up, bald head! Go up, bald head!' — a taunt challenging his authority and connection to Elijah's ascent.

(2 Kings 2:24) 
And when Elisha turned and looked at them, he saw them and cursed them in the name of the Lord. Immediately, two she-bears came out of the nearby forest and attacked them, tearing apart forty-two of the boys.

(2 Kings 2:25) 
Then Elisha went from there to Mount Carmel, and from Mount Carmel, he returned to Samaria.

(2 Kings 3:1) 
Moab, however, rebelled against Israel after Ahab's death.

(2 Kings 3:2) 
And Joram, Ahab's son, became king over Israel in Samaria during the twelfth year of Jehoshaphat, who was king of Judah. Joram reigned for twelve years.

(2 Kings 3:3) 
He did what was evil in the Lord's sight, though not to the same extent as his father Ahab or his mother Jezebel. For Joram removed the stone pillars of Baal that his father had set up.

(2 Kings 3:4) 
Now Mesha, the king of Moab, was a sheep breeder, and he used to pay tribute to the king of Israel: a hundred thousand lambs and a hundred thousand rams with their wool.

(2 Kings 3:5) 
But after Ahab died, Moab broke the treaty they had with the king of Israel.

(2 Kings 3:6) 
So King Joram left Samaria that day and took a census of Israel's fighting men.

(2 Kings 3:7) 
He then sent a message to Jehoshaphat, the king of Judah, saying, 'The king of Moab has rebelled against me. Will you come with me to fight against Moab?' Jehoshaphat replied, 'I will go up with you. My forces are like your forces, my people like your people, and my horses like your horses.'

(2 Kings 3:8) 
Then Joram asked, 'By what route should we advance?' And Jehoshaphat answered, 'By way of the desert of Edom.'

(2 Kings 3:9) 
So the king of Israel, the king of Judah, and the king of Edom set out. They marched for seven days, but there was no water for their army or for the animals that followed them.

(2 Kings 3:10) 
Then the king of Israel cried out, 'Oh no! Has the Lord called these three kings together only to deliver them into the hand of Moab?'

(2 Kings 3:11) 
But Jehoshaphat asked, 'Is there no prophet of the Lord here through whom we might consult the Lord?' One of the servants of the king of Israel replied, 'Elisha, the son of Shaphat, is here. He used to pour water on Elijah's hands'—meaning he was Elijah's personal assistant and successor.

(2 Kings 3:12) 
Jehoshaphat then declared, 'The Lord's message is indeed with him.' So the king of Israel, Jehoshaphat, and the king of Edom went down to meet Elisha.

(2 Kings 3:13) 
Elisha said to the king of Israel, 'What business do you and I have together? Go to the prophets of your father and your mother!' The king of Israel answered him, 'No, for the Lord has called these three kings together to deliver them into the hand of Moab.'

(2 Kings 3:14) 
Elisha declared, 'As the Lord of hosts lives, before whom I stand, if I did not respect the presence of Jehoshaphat, the king of Judah, I would not even look at you or acknowledge you.'

(2 Kings 3:15) 
But now, bring me a harpist. And as the harpist played, the hand of the Lord came upon Elisha.

(2 Kings 3:16) 
And he said, 'Thus says the Lord: Dig many trenches in this dry streambed.'

(2 Kings 3:17) 
For thus says the Lord: 'You will neither see wind nor rain, yet this streambed will be filled with water, so that you, your troops, and your animals may drink.'

(2 Kings 3:18) 
And this is but a small thing in the Lord's sight. He will also deliver Moab into your hands.

(2 Kings 3:19) 
You will strike every fortified city and every excellent city. You will cut down every fruit tree, stop up every spring of water, and ruin every good field with stones.

(2 Kings 3:20) 
So it happened in the morning, at the time when the sacrifice was offered, that behold, water came by way of Edom, and the land was filled with water.

(2 Kings 3:21) 
Now all the Moabites, hearing that the kings had come up to fight against them, gathered everyone who could put on a belt for battle and stood at their border.

(2 Kings 3:22) 
When they rose early in the morning, and the sun was shining opposite them, the Moabites saw the water in the distance, appearing to them like blood.

(2 Kings 3:23) 
And they said, 'This is blood! The kings must have fought with their swords and killed each other. Now, Moab, to the plunder!'

(2 Kings 3:24) 
But when the Moabites came to the camp of Israel, the Israelites rose up and struck the Moabites, who fled before them. The Israelites pursued them and continued to strike Moab.

(2 Kings 3:25) 
They destroyed their cities and filled every good field with stones by throwing them. They stopped up every spring of water and cut down every fruit tree. So only the walls of stones were left in Kir-hareseth. Then the forces surrounded the city with slingers and attacked it.

(2 Kings 3:26) 
When the king of Moab saw that the battle was too fierce for him, he took with him seven hundred swordsmen to break through to the king of Edom's position, but they were unable.

(2 Kings 3:27) 
Then he took his eldest son, who was to succeed him as king, and offered him as a burnt offering upon the city wall. This act caused great wrath to fall upon Israel. Immediately, they withdrew from him and returned to their own land.

(2 Kings 3:1) 
Joram, the son of Ahab, began to rule over Israel in Samaria during the eighteenth year of Jehoshaphat, the king of Judah. He reigned for twelve years.

(2 Kings 3:2) 
He did evil in the sight of the Lord, but not to the extent of his father and mother, for he removed the stone column of Baal that his father had made.

(2 Kings 3:3) 
Nevertheless, he clung to the sins of Jeroboam, the son of Nabat, who had caused Israel to sin, and he did not turn away from them.

(2 Kings 3:4) 
Now Mesa, the king of Moab, was a sheep breeder. He used to pay the king of Israel a tribute of one hundred thousand lambs, and one hundred thousand rams with their wool.

(2 Kings 3:5) 
But when Ahab died, the king of Moab rebelled against the king of Israel.

(2 Kings 3:6) 
So King Joram left Samaria that very day and reviewed all the men of Israel.

(2 Kings 3:7) 
He went and sent a message to Jehoshaphat, the king of Judah, saying: 'The king of Moab has rebelled against me. Will you come with me to fight against Moab?' Jehoshaphat replied: 'I will go up with you. My people are like your people, and my horses are like your horses.'

(2 Kings 3:8) 
Joram then asked: 'By which way should we march up?' Jehoshaphat answered: 'Through the way of the desert of Edom.'

(2 Kings 3:9) 
So the king of Israel, the king of Judah, and the king of Edom went forth. They marched in a roundabout way for seven days, and there was no water for the army or for the animals that followed them.

(2 Kings 3:10) 
The king of Israel cried out: 'Alas, alas! Has the Lord called these three kings together only to deliver them into the hand of Moab?'

(2 Kings 3:11) 
Then Jehoshaphat asked: 'Is there no prophet of the Lord here, that we may inquire of the Lord through him?' One of the servants of the king of Israel answered: 'Elisha, the son of Shaphat, is here, he who poured water over the hands of Elijah.'

(2 Kings 3:12) 
And Jehoshaphat said: 'The word of the Lord is with him.' So the king of Israel, Jehoshaphat, and the king of Edom went down to him.

(2 Kings 3:13) 
Elisha said to the king of Israel: 'What concern have I with you? Go to the prophets of your father and your mother.' The king of Israel replied to him: 'No, because the Lord has called these three kings together to deliver them into the hand of Moab!'

(2 Kings 3:14) 
Then Elisha said: 'As the Lord of hosts lives, before whom I stand, if it were not for my respect for Jehoshaphat, the king of Judah, I would not even give you attention or look at you.'

(2 Kings 3:15) 
Now, bring me a harpist. And when the harpist played, the hand of the Lord came upon Elisha.

(2 Kings 3:16) 
And he said: 'Thus says the Lord: Make this valley full of ditches, dig many ditches.'

(2 Kings 3:17) 
For thus says the Lord: 'You will not see wind, nor will you see rain, yet this valley will be filled with water, and you, your livestock, and your flocks will drink.'

(2 Kings 3:18) 
And this is but a small thing in the sight of the Lord: He will also deliver Moab into your hands.

(2 Kings 3:19) 
You will strike every fortified city and every excellent city. You will cut down every fruitful tree, and you will stop up all springs of water, and you will ruin every good field with stones.

(2 Kings 3:20) 
So it came to pass in the morning, at the time when the sacrifice is usually offered, that suddenly water came by the way of Edom, and the land was filled with water.

(2 Kings 3:21) 
Now all the Moabites, hearing that the kings had come up to fight against them, gathered together everyone who could put on armor, from young men to old, and they stood at their borders.

(2 Kings 3:22) 
Rising early in the morning, as the sun rose opposite the water, the Moabites saw the water from afar, red like blood.

(2 Kings 3:23) 
And they said: 'This is the blood of the sword! The kings must have fought against each other and killed one another. Now, Moab, to the plunder!'

(2 Kings 3:24) 
But when they came to the camp of Israel, the Israelites rose up and struck the Moabites, who fled before them. They pursued them, striking down and devastating Moab.

(2 Kings 3:25) 
They also destroyed the cities, and every good field they filled with stones by each man throwing a stone. They stopped up all the springs of water and cut down every fruitful tree, so that only the walls of the city of Kir Haraseth remained. The slingers surrounded it and struck it.

(2 Kings 3:26) 
When the king of Moab saw that the battle was too fierce for him, he took with him seven hundred men who drew swords to break through to the king of Edom, but he could not.

(2 Kings 3:27) 
Then he took his firstborn son, who was to reign in his place, and offered him as a burnt offering upon the wall. And there was great indignation in Israel. Immediately, they withdrew from him and returned to their own land.

(2 Kings 3:1) 
Moab rebelled against Israel after King Achab died.

(2 Kings 3:2) 
Now Joram, son of Achab, began his reign over Israel in Samaria during the eighteenth year of Josaphat's kingship in Judah, and Joram reigned for twelve years.

(2 Kings 3:3) 
And he did what was evil in the sight of the Lord, yet not to the same degree as his father and mother had done, for he had removed the idols of Baal that his father had erected.

(2 Kings 3:4) 
Now Mesa, the king of Moab, was a wealthy sheep breeder, and he was required to pay the king of Israel a tribute of one hundred thousand lambs and one hundred thousand rams with their wool.

(2 Kings 3:5) 
But when King Achab had died, Mesa, the king of Moab, openly rebelled against the king of Israel.

(2 Kings 3:6) 
So King Joram marched out from Samaria at that time and mustered all the fighting men of Israel.

(2 Kings 3:7) 
And Joram sent a message to Josaphat, the king of Judah, saying: 'The king of Moab has rebelled against me. Will you come with me to Moab to wage war?' Josaphat replied: 'I will indeed go with you. My resources are entirely at your disposal, my people are your people, and my horses are your horses.'

(2 Kings 3:8) 
Then Joram asked, 'By what route should our army advance?' And Josaphat replied, 'We should go through the desert route of Edom.'

(2 Kings 3:9) 
So the king of Israel, the king of Judah, and the king of Edom began their march. After they had traveled for seven days, there was no water left for their army or for the animals that accompanied them.

(2 Kings 3:10) 
Then the king of Israel cried out, 'Oh no! Has the Lord truly brought these three kings together just to deliver us into the hand of Moab?'

(2 Kings 3:11) 
Then Josaphat asked, 'Is there no prophet of the Lord present here, through whom we might inquire of the Lord's will?' One of the servants of the king of Israel answered, saying: 'Elisha, the son of Saphat, is here. He is the one who used to pour water on Elijah’s hands, serving him as a disciple.'

(2 Kings 3:12) 
Josaphat then declared, 'The Lord's message is truly with him.' So the king of Israel, Josaphat, and the king of Edom went down to Elisha.

(2 Kings 3:13) 
Then Elisha said to the king of Israel, 'What business do I have with you? Go to the prophets of your father and your mother, the prophets of Baal!' But the king of Israel pleaded with him, 'It is because the Lord has truly called these three kings together only to deliver us into the hand of Moab!'

(2 Kings 3:14) 
Then Elisha declared: 'As the Lord of hosts lives, before Whom I stand in service, if it were not for my respect for Josaphat, the king of Judah, I would not even look at you nor acknowledge your presence!'

(2 Kings 3:15) 
Now, therefore, bring me a musician to play a stringed instrument.' And while the musician played, the power of the Lord came upon Elisha.

(2 Kings 3:16) 
And Elisha declared: 'Thus says the Lord: "Dig many ditches and trenches throughout this dry valley!"'

(2 Kings 3:17) 
For thus says the Lord: 'Even though you will see no wind or rain, this valley will be filled with water, so that you, your families, and your animals can drink.'

(2 Kings 3:18) 
And this miracle alone is but a small thing in the sight of the Lord; He will also deliver Moab, your enemy, into your hands.

(2 Kings 3:19) 
And you will conquer every fortified city and destroy every important town. You will cut down every fruit-bearing tree, stop up every spring of water, and ruin every fertile field by covering it with stones.

(2 Kings 3:20) 
So it came to pass the next morning, at the hour when the daily sacrifice was customarily offered, and behold, water began to flow from the direction of Edom, and the land was quickly filled with water.

(2 Kings 3:21) 
Now all the Moabites, hearing that the allied kings had come up to fight against them, called together every man who was able to bear arms, from the youngest to the oldest, and they took their stand at their borders.

(2 Kings 3:22) 
And they rose early in the morning, and when the sun had fully risen, shining on the water, the Moabites looked and saw the water appearing as red as blood.

(2 Kings 3:23) 
And they exclaimed, 'This is blood! The allied kings must have fought fiercely and slaughtered each other with their swords! Everyone must have slain his neighbor! Now, therefore, Moab, let us go for the plunder!'

(2 Kings 3:24) 
But when the Moabites approached the camp of Israel, the men of Israel suddenly rose up and struck down the Moabites, who then fled in panic before them. As the Israelites pursued and struck down the Moabites, they continued to lay waste to the entire region.

(2 Kings 3:25) 
And the allied armies continued to destroy the cities, filling every fertile field with stones. They stopped up every spring of water and cut down every fruit-bearing tree, leaving only the stone walls of the final stronghold. They surrounded this last remaining city with siege works and relentlessly attacked it with sling stones from above.

(2 Kings 3:26) 
Now when the king of Moab saw that the battle was completely lost to his enemies, he took with him seven hundred men who drew swords, hoping to break through the lines towards the king of Edom; but they were unable to succeed.

(2 Kings 3:27) 
Then, in a desperate act, he took his eldest son, who was destined to succeed him as king, and offered him as a burnt offering upon the city wall. This act caused great moral indignation among the allied forces, who immediately withdrew from the city and returned to their own land.

(2 Kings 4:1) 
A certain woman, one of the wives of your prophet-disciples, cried out to Elisha, saying: 'My husband, your servant, is dead. And you know that your servant was a man who truly feared the Lord—a devout man. But now, a creditor is coming to take my two sons to be his slaves, to settle their father's debt!'

(2 Kings 4:2) 
Elisha then asked her: 'What do you want me to do for you, my child? Tell me, what do you have in your house?' She replied: 'Your servant has absolutely nothing left in my house, except a tiny bit of oil, just enough for personal anointing.'

(2 Kings 4:3) 
And he said to her: 'Go now, and borrow empty vessels from all your neighbors—and make sure to get many of them, not just a few!'

(2 Kings 4:4) 
Then go inside, and close the door upon yourself and your sons. Begin to pour your existing oil into all these empty vessels. And as each vessel becomes full, set it aside.'

(2 Kings 4:5) 
So the woman went and did as Elisha commanded. She closed the door upon herself and her sons. Her sons began bringing her the empty vessels, and she continued pouring from her small jar.

(2 Kings 4:6) 
When all the vessels were full, she said to her son: 'Bring me another vessel.' But he responded: 'There are no more!' At that very moment, the flow of oil stopped completely.

(2 Kings 4:7) 
So she went and told the man of God what had happened. He said: 'Go, sell the oil, and repay your creditor. You and your sons can then live on the rest of the money.'

(2 Kings 4:8) 
It happened one day that Elisha was passing through Shunem. There was a prominent and wealthy woman there, who urged him to come and eat bread with her. So whenever he passed through, he would turn aside to her house to eat bread.

(2 Kings 4:9) 
She said to her husband: 'I perceive that this is a holy man of God who frequently passes by our house.'

(2 Kings 4:10) 
She continued: 'Let us make a small room on the roof for him, and furnish it with a bed, a table, a chair, and a lamp. Then, whenever he comes to us, he can stay there.'

(2 Kings 4:11) 
So it happened one day that when Elisha came, he went to that room and rested there.

(2 Kings 4:12) 
Then he said to Gehazi, his servant: 'Call this Shunammite woman.' When Gehazi called her, and she stood before Elisha,

(2 Kings 4:13) 
Elisha said to Gehazi: 'Speak to her and tell her: “Behold, you have diligently provided for us and shown us every kindness. What do you wish that I do for you in return? Do you want me to speak on your behalf to the king, or to the commander of the army?”' She replied: 'I dwell among my own people—I lack nothing.'

(2 Kings 4:14) 
And Elisha asked: 'What then can be done for her?' Gehazi replied: 'She has no son, and her husband is an old man.'

(2 Kings 4:15) 
So Elisha commanded that she be called again. When she was called, and stood in the doorway, he said:

(2 Kings 4:16) 
'At this very time, in this same season, in the coming year, you shall embrace a son.' But she exclaimed: 'No, my lord, man of God, do not lie to your handmaid!'

(2 Kings 4:17) 
And indeed, the woman conceived and bore a son at the very time and in the season that Elisha had promised her.

(2 Kings 4:18) 
The boy grew up. And it happened one day that he went out to his father, who was with the reapers in the field,

(2 Kings 4:19) 
and he cried out to his father: 'My head, my head aches! My head, my head aches!' His father then said to one of the servants: 'Carry him home, and take him to his mother.'

(2 Kings 4:20) 
So the servant carried him and brought him to his mother. She held him on her knees until midday, and then he died.

(2 Kings 4:21) 
Then she went up to the room, placed him on the bed of the man of God, closed the door, and left.

(2 Kings 4:22) 
She called her husband, saying: 'Please send me one of the young men and a donkey, so I can hurry to the man of God and return quickly.'

(2 Kings 4:23) 
He asked: 'For what reason are you going to him today? Is it the New Moon festival or the Sabbath day?' She replied, cryptically: 'It is well.' —meaning 'All is fine, I will explain later.'

(2 Kings 4:24) 
So she saddled the donkey and instructed her servant: 'Drive quickly; do not slow down the pace unless I tell you to.'

(2 Kings 4:25) 
Thus she went and arrived at the man of God, Elisha, on Mount Carmel. When the man of God saw her from a distance, he said to his servant Gehazi: 'Look, it is that Shunammite woman!'

(2 Kings 4:26) 
'Run now to meet her,' he instructed, 'and ask her: “Is all well with you? Is all well with your husband? Is all well with your son?”' She replied, again briefly: 'All is well.'

(2 Kings 4:27) 
But when she reached the man of God on the mountain, she grasped his feet. Gehazi approached to push her away. But the man of God said: 'Leave her alone, for her soul is in bitterness. The Lord has hidden it from me and has not revealed it to me.'

(2 Kings 4:28) 
And she cried out: 'Did I ask for a son from my lord? Did I not say to you: “Do not deceive me”?'

(2 Kings 4:29) 
Elisha then said to Gehazi: 'Gird up your loins, take my staff in your hand, and go. If you meet anyone on the way, do not greet them; and if anyone greets you, do not answer them. Place my staff upon the face of the boy.'

(2 Kings 4:30) 
But the mother of the boy declared: 'As the Lord lives, and as your soul lives, I will not leave you!' So Elisha arose and followed her.

(2 Kings 4:31) 
Meanwhile, Gehazi had gone ahead of them and had placed the staff upon the boy's face. But there was no voice, nor any sign of life. So he returned to meet Elisha and reported to him, saying: 'The boy has not awakened.'

(2 Kings 4:32) 
Then Elisha entered the house, and behold, the boy was lying dead on his own bed.

(2 Kings 4:33) 
He went in and closed the door behind himself and the boy, and he prayed to the Lord.

(2 Kings 4:34) 
Then he went up and lay upon the boy, putting his mouth upon his mouth, and his eyes upon his eyes, and his hands upon his hands. He stretched himself out upon him, and the boy's flesh began to grow warm.

(2 Kings 4:35) 
Elisha then went down and walked around in the house once more. Then he went up again and stretched himself out upon the boy once more. And the boy sneezed seven times, and then opened his eyes.

(2 Kings 4:36) 
Elisha called Gehazi and told him: 'Call this Shunammite woman.' When she was called, she came in to him. He said: 'Take up your son!'

(2 Kings 4:37) 
She came in, fell at his feet, and prostrated herself on the ground in worship. Then she took up her son and went out.

(2 Kings 4:38) 
Elisha then returned to Gilgal. There was a severe famine in the land, and the prophet-disciples were sitting before him. He said to one of his servants: 'Put a large pot on the fire, and cook a stew for the prophet-disciples.'

(2 Kings 4:39) 
One of them went out into the field to gather herbs. He found a wild plant and gathered enough of its fruit to fill his cloak, —like wild gourds—. He came back and chopped them into the pot of stew, for they did not know what it was.

(2 Kings 4:40) 
So they served it to the men to eat. But when they tasted the stew, they cried out, saying: 'There is death in the pot, O man of God! There is death in the pot!' And they could not eat it.

(2 Kings 4:1) 
A certain woman, one of the wives of the prophets, cried out to Elisha, saying: “Your servant, my husband, is dead. You know that your servant lived in holy fear of the Lord. And now a creditor has come to take my two sons to be his slaves to pay off the debt.”

(2 Kings 4:2) 
And Elisha said to her: “What do you want me to do for you? Tell me, what do you have in your house?” And she responded: “Your handmaid has nothing in my house, except a small amount of oil.”

(2 Kings 4:3) 
He said: “Go and borrow many empty vessels from all your neighbors. Make sure there are not just a few.”

(2 Kings 4:4) 
Then go inside and shut the door behind you and your sons. Pour the oil into all these vessels. And when they are full, set them aside.”

(2 Kings 4:5) 
So the woman went away and shut the door upon herself and upon her sons. They brought the vessels to her, and she kept pouring.

(2 Kings 4:6) 
And when all the vessels were full, she said to her son: “Bring me still another vessel.” He responded: “There are no more.”

(2 Kings 4:7) 
And at that moment, the oil stopped flowing.

(2 Kings 4:8) 
So she came and told the man of God. He said: “Go, sell the oil, and pay the creditor. You and your sons can then live on the rest of the money.”

(2 Kings 4:9) 
Now it happened that Elisha was passing through Shunem. And there was a wealthy and influential woman there, who urged him to eat bread with her. So whenever he passed by, he would turn aside to her house to eat bread.

(2 Kings 4:10) 
And she said to her husband: “I perceive that this man, who passes by us so frequently, is a holy man of God.”

(2 Kings 4:11) 
“Let us make a small upper room for him and put in it a small bed, and a table, and a chair, and a lamp. So that when he comes to us, he may stay there.”

(2 Kings 4:12) 
So it happened one day that Elisha came, and he turned aside to the upper room and rested there.

(2 Kings 4:13) 
And he said to Gehazi, his servant: “Call this Shunammite woman.” And when he had called her, and she stood before him,

(2 Kings 4:14) 
Elisha said to his servant: “What do you want me to do for her?” Gehazi responded: “Indeed, she has no son, and her husband is old.”

(2 Kings 4:15) 
So he commanded: “Call her.” And when he had called her, she stood in the doorway.

(2 Kings 4:16) 
And he said to her: “At this time next year, you will hold a son in your womb.” But she responded: “No, my lord, man of God, do not deceive your handmaid.”

(2 Kings 4:17) 
So the woman conceived and bore a son at that very time, and at the same hour, as Elisha had said.

(2 Kings 4:18) 
And the boy grew up. And it happened one day that he went out to his father among the reapers in the field.

(2 Kings 4:19) 
He said to his father: “My head hurts, my head hurts!” And his father said to a servant: “Take him and bring him to his mother.”

(2 Kings 4:20) 
And when the servant had taken him and brought him to his mother, the boy sat on her knees until midday, and then he died.

(2 Kings 4:21) 
But she went up and laid him upon the bed of the man of God, shut the door, and went out.

(2 Kings 4:22) 
And she called her husband, saying: “Send me one of the servants and one of the donkeys, so that I may quickly go to the man of God and return.”

(2 Kings 4:23) 
He said: “For what reason are you going to him? It is not the new moon, nor the Sabbath.” These were the customary times people visited prophets. She responded: “It is well.”

(2 Kings 4:24) 
So she saddled the donkey and sat upon it. And she said to her servant: “Drive fast and hurry. Do not speak to me unless I tell you.”

(2 Kings 4:25) 
So she went, and came to the man of God on Mount Carmel. And when the man of God saw her from a distance, he said to Gehazi, his servant: “Behold, there is that Shunammite woman!”

(2 Kings 4:26) 
“Go to meet her and ask: ‘Is all well? Is your husband well? Is your son well?’” And she responded: “All is well.”

(2 Kings 4:27) 
But when she came to the man of God on the mountain, she took hold of his feet. And Gehazi came near to push her away. But the man of God said: “Leave her alone, for her soul is in bitterness. The Lord has hidden it from me and has not revealed it to me.”

(2 Kings 4:28) 
And she said: “Did I ask for a son from my lord? Did I not say to you: ‘Do not deceive me?’”

(2 Kings 4:29) 
And Elisha said to Gehazi: “Gird up your loins and prepare for urgent travel. Take my staff in your hand and go. If you meet anyone, do not greet him. And if anyone greets you, do not answer him. Lay my staff upon the face of the boy.”

(2 Kings 4:30) 
And the mother of the boy said: “As the Lord lives, and as your soul lives, I will not leave you.” So he arose and went with her.

(2 Kings 4:31) 
But Gehazi had gone ahead of them and had laid the staff upon the face of the boy. And there was no voice, nor any sign of life. So he returned and met Elisha, and announced to him, saying: “The boy has not awoken.”

(2 Kings 4:32) 
So Elisha went into the upper room, and behold, the dead boy lay upon his own bed.

(2 Kings 4:33) 
And having entered, he shut the door upon himself and upon the boy, and prayed to the Lord.

(2 Kings 4:34) 
Then he went up and lay upon the boy. He put his mouth upon his mouth, and his eyes upon his eyes, and his hands upon his hands. And he stretched himself upon him, and the flesh of the boy grew warm.

(2 Kings 4:35) 
And he turned away and walked through the house once within, and then went up again. He stretched himself upon him, and the boy sneezed seven times, and then opened his eyes.

(2 Kings 4:36) 
And he called Gehazi, and said to him: “Call this Shunammite woman.” And when he had called her, and she had come in to him, Elisha said: “Take your son.”

(2 Kings 4:37) 
She came, and fell at his feet, and bowed deeply in reverence towards the ground. Then she took her son and went out.

(2 Kings 4:38) 
Now Elisha returned to Gilgal. There was a famine in the land, and the community of prophets were sitting before him. And he said to one of his servants: “Put on the large pot and cook stew for the community of prophets.”

(2 Kings 4:39) 
But one went out into the field to gather wild herbs. He found something like a wild vine and gathered wild gourds from it, filling his cloak. And when he returned, he cut them into the pot of stew, for they did not know what it was. These gourds were poisonous.

(2 Kings 4:40) 
And they poured it out for their companions to eat. But when they had eaten of that stew, they cried out, saying: “Death is in the pot, O man of God!” And they could not eat it.

(2 Kings 4:1) 
A certain woman, one of the wives of the prophets, cried out to Elisha, saying, "Your servant, my husband, has died, and you know that your servant truly feared the Lord. Now, look, a creditor has come to take my two sons as slaves for himself to settle the debt."

(2 Kings 4:2) 
Then Elisha said to her, "What do you want me to do for you? Tell me, what do you have in your house?" She answered, "Your maidservant has nothing at all in the house, except a single small jar of oil."

(2 Kings 4:3) 
He said, "Go now and borrow empty vessels from all your neighbors. Make sure there are not just a few of them, but many."

(2 Kings 4:4) 
Then, go inside and shut the door behind you and your sons. Pour the oil from your jar into all these borrowed vessels. When they are full, set them aside."

(2 Kings 4:5) 
So the woman went away and shut the door behind herself and her sons. They brought her the vessels, and she continued to pour the oil.

(2 Kings 4:6) 
When all the vessels were full, she said to her son, "Bring me another vessel." He responded, "There isn't another vessel left." And then the oil stopped flowing.

(2 Kings 4:7) 
Then she went and told the man of God what had happened. He said, "Go now, sell the oil, and pay your creditor. After that, you and your sons can live on the rest of the money."

(2 Kings 4:8) 
It came to pass one day that Elisha was passing through Shunem. There was a prominent woman there who urged him to eat bread. And whenever he passed by frequently, he would turn aside to her house to eat bread.

(2 Kings 4:9) 
She said to her husband, "Look, I perceive that this man who passes by us so often is a holy man of God."

(2 Kings 4:10) 
"Let us make a small room for him on the roof, and put a bed in it for him, and a table, and a chair, and a lampstand. Then, whenever he comes to us, he can stay there."

(2 Kings 4:11) 
So it came to pass one day that Elisha came, turned aside to the room on the roof, and rested there.

(2 Kings 4:12) 
He said to Gehazi, his servant, "Call this Shunammite woman." When Gehazi had called her, and she stood before Elisha,

(2 Kings 4:13) 
Elisha said to Gehazi, "Tell her: 'Behold, you have gone to great trouble for us with all your hospitality. What do you want me to do for you in return? Do you have any request you want me to speak to the king about, or to the commander of the army?'" She responded, "I live among my own people; I am content with my position in life and have no need of royal connections."

(2 Kings 4:14) 
Elisha then said, "What then can be done for her?" And Gehazi answered, "She has no son, and her husband is old."

(2 Kings 4:15) 
So he commanded that she be called. When she had been called and stood in the doorway, Elisha said,

(2 Kings 4:16) 
"At this same time next year, when life returns in its cycle, you will be holding a son in your arms." But she responded, "No, my lord, man of God, do not lie to your maidservant about such a hope."

(2 Kings 4:17) 
And indeed, the woman conceived and gave birth to a son at that very time, at the exact hour Elisha had told her.

(2 Kings 4:18) 
So the boy grew up. And it happened one day that he went out to his father among the reapers in the field.

(2 Kings 4:19) 
He said to his father, "My head hurts, my head hurts!" So his father said to a servant, "Carry him and take him to his mother."

(2 Kings 4:20) 
When the servant had carried him and brought him to his mother, she laid him on her lap until noon, and then he died.

(2 Kings 4:21) 
But she went up to the room on the roof and laid him on the bed of the man of God. Then she shut the door and went out.

(2 Kings 4:22) 
She called her husband, saying, "Send me one of the young men and a donkey, so I can ride quickly to the man of God and return."

(2 Kings 4:23) 
Her husband said to her, "Why are you going to him today? It is not the New Moon festival, nor is it the Sabbath day, when people typically seek out prophets." She responded, "All is well," keeping her son's death a secret.

(2 Kings 4:24) 
So she saddled the donkey and instructed her servant, "Drive steadily and hurry. Do not stop speaking to me on the way unless I tell you to."

(2 Kings 4:25) 
So she set out and came to the man of God on Mount Carmel. When the man of God saw her coming from a distance, he said to Gehazi, his servant, "Look, there is that Shunammite woman."

(2 Kings 4:26) 
"Therefore, go meet her and ask: 'Are you well? Is your husband well? Is the boy well?'" She responded, "All is well."

(2 Kings 4:27) 
When she came to the man of God on the mountain, she grasped his feet. And Gehazi came near to push her away. But the man of God said, "Leave her alone, for her soul is in bitterness and anguish, and the Lord has hidden it from me and not revealed it to me."

(2 Kings 4:28) 
And she said, "Did I ask my lord for a son? Did I not say to you, 'Do not deceive me with false hope' (by promising a son)?"

(2 Kings 4:29) 
Then Elisha said to Gehazi, "Gird up your loins and take my staff in your hand. Go quickly! If you meet anyone on the way, do not greet them with conversation, and if anyone greets you, do not answer them. Then, place my staff on the boy's face."

(2 Kings 4:30) 
But the boy's mother said, "As the Lord lives, and as your soul lives, I will not leave you and go without you." So Elisha rose and went with her.

(2 Kings 4:31) 
Meanwhile, Gehazi had gone ahead of them and had placed the staff on the boy's face. But there was no voice, and no sign of life or consciousness. So he returned to meet Elisha and reported to him, saying, "The boy has not awakened."

(2 Kings 4:32) 
Then Elisha entered the room on the roof, and behold, the dead boy was lying on his bed.

(2 Kings 4:33) 
So he went out, closed the door behind him, and prayed to the Lord.

(2 Kings 4:34) 
Then he went up onto the bed and lay stretched out over the boy. He put his mouth on the boy's mouth, his eyes on the boy's eyes, and his hands on the boy's hands. As he remained bowed over the boy, the boy's flesh grew warm.

(2 Kings 4:35) 
Then Elisha returned and walked around the house once or twice. After that, he went up again and stretched out over him. The boy then sneezed seven times, and he opened his eyes.

(2 Kings 4:36) 
Elisha called Gehazi and said to him, "Call that Shunammite woman." So she was called and came in to him. Elisha said, "Take up your son."

(2 Kings 4:37) 
She came, fell at his feet, and prostrated herself on the ground in worship and profound gratitude. Then she took up her son and went out.

(2 Kings 4:38) 
Elisha returned to Gilgal, as there was a severe famine in the land. The sons of the prophets were sitting before him for instruction. He said to one of his servants, "Put a large pot on, and boil some stew for the sons of the prophets."

(2 Kings 4:39) 
Then one of them went out into the field to gather herbs. He found a wild plant and gathered from it wild gourds, filling his cloak. He returned and cut them into the pot of stew, without anyone knowing what they were.

(2 Kings 4:40) 
When the stew was poured out for the men to eat, as they ate, they cried out, saying, "There is death in the pot, O man of God!" And they could not eat it.

(2 Kings 5:1) 
Naaman, the commander of the Syrian army, was a very rich, noble, and powerful man. However, he was a leper.

(2 Kings 5:2) 
Syrian raiders had previously gone out into Israel, and they had captured a young girl. This girl was now serving Naaman’s wife.

(2 Kings 5:3) 
The young girl said to her mistress, “If only my master Naaman would go to the prophet who lives in Samaria, he would certainly be cured of his leprosy.”

(2 Kings 5:4) 
Naaman then went to his king and reported what the girl from the land of Israel had said.

(2 Kings 5:5) 
The king of Syria told Naaman, “Go now, and I will send a letter to the king of Israel.” So Naaman departed, taking with him ten talents of silver, six thousand shekels of gold, and six changes of fine clothing as gifts.

(2 Kings 5:6) 
He brought the letter to the king of Israel. The letter read: “When you receive this letter, know that I have sent my servant Naaman to you so that you may cure him of his leprosy.”

(2 Kings 5:7) 
When the king of Israel read the letter, he tore his clothes and exclaimed, “Am I God, able to kill and to give life, that this man sends someone to me to be cured of leprosy? This is obviously a pretext; he is looking for a reason to attack me.”

(2 Kings 5:8) 
However, when Elisha, the man of God, heard that the king of Israel had torn his clothes, he sent a message to the king, saying: “Why have you torn your clothes? Let Naaman come to me, and he will know that there is a true prophet in Israel.”

(2 Kings 5:9) 
So Naaman came with his horses and chariots and stood at the entrance of Elisha’s house.

(2 Kings 5:10) 
Elisha sent a messenger out to Naaman, telling him, “Go and wash yourself seven times in the Jordan River. Your flesh will be restored, and you will be clean.”

(2 Kings 5:11) 
Naaman departed in anger, saying, “I thought he would come out to me personally, and stand, and call on the name of the Lord his God, and wave his hand over the place of my leprosy, and cure me.”

(2 Kings 5:12) 
He continued, “Are not the rivers of Damascus, Abana and Pharphar, better than all the waters of Israel? Could I not wash in them and be clean?” He then turned and went away in a rage.

(2 Kings 5:13) 
His servants approached him and reasoned with him, saying, “Father, if the prophet had commanded you to do some difficult thing, you would certainly have done it. How much more, then, when he simply tells you: ‘Wash, and you will be clean’?”

(2 Kings 5:14) 
So Naaman went down and washed himself seven times in the Jordan, just as the man of God had instructed. His flesh was restored, becoming like the flesh of a young child, and he was completely clean.

(2 Kings 5:15) 
Then Naaman returned to the man of God with all his company. He came and stood before Elisha and declared, “Now I truly know that there is no other God in all the earth except in Israel. Therefore, I beg you, please accept a gift from your servant.”

(2 Kings 5:16) 
Elisha replied, “As the Lord lives, before whom I stand, I will accept nothing from you.” Naaman urged him, but Elisha refused.

(2 Kings 5:17) 
Then Naaman said, “If you will not accept a gift, then please, let me, your servant, be given two mule-loads of this Israelite earth. For from now on, your servant will no longer offer burnt offerings or sacrifices to foreign gods, but only to the Lord.”

(2 Kings 5:18) 
Naaman continued, “But in this one thing, I ask the Lord to forgive your servant: when my king enters the temple of Rimmon to worship there, and he leans on my arm, and I bow down in the temple of Rimmon along with him, may the Lord forgive me, your servant, for this act of bowing.”

(2 Kings 5:19) 
Elisha said to him, “Go in peace.” So Naaman departed from him, and had traveled only a short distance.

(2 Kings 5:20) 
Gehazi, the servant of Elisha the man of God, said to himself, “Look, my master has spared this Naaman the Syrian, by not accepting from his hand what he brought. As the Lord lives, I will surely run after him and get something from him!”

(2 Kings 5:21) 
So Gehazi pursued Naaman. When Naaman saw him running after him, he quickly dismounted from his chariot to meet him and asked, “Is everything all right?”

(2 Kings 5:22) 
Gehazi replied, “Yes, everything is well. My master sent me, saying, ‘Look, two young men, members of the prophets’ community, have just arrived from the hill country of Ephraim. Please give them a talent of silver and two changes of clothing.’”

(2 Kings 5:23) 
Naaman said, “By all means, take two talents!” He urged Gehazi to accept them, and then tied up two talents of silver in two bags, along with two changes of clothing. He gave them to two of his servants, who carried them ahead of Gehazi.

(2 Kings 5:24) 
When Gehazi reached the hill, he took the gifts from their hands and put them away in the house. Then he sent the men away, and they departed.

(2 Kings 5:25) 
He then went in and stood before his master. Elisha asked him, “Where have you come from, Gehazi?” He answered, “Your servant has not been anywhere.”

(2 Kings 5:26) 
But Elisha replied, “Was not my spirit present when the man turned from his chariot to meet you? Is this the time to accept money, and to accept clothes, and olive groves, and vineyards, and sheep, and oxen, and male and female servants?” This rhetorical question from Elisha implies that it was a time of spiritual significance, not personal gain.

(2 Kings 5:27) 
Elisha concluded, “Therefore, the leprosy of Naaman will cling to you and to your descendants forever.” And immediately, Gehazi departed from Elisha, a leper, white as snow.

(2 Kings 5:1) 
Naaman was the commander of the Syrian king’s army. He was a great man and highly esteemed by his master, because the Lord had granted the Syrians victory through him. He was also a powerful and wealthy man, but he was suffering from leprosy.

(2 Kings 5:2) 
Now some raiders had gone out from the land of Syria, and they had taken captive a young girl from the land of Israel, who now served Naaman’s wife.

(2 Kings 5:3) 
She said to her mistress, 'If only my master would go to the prophet who is in Samaria, he would certainly cure him of the leprosy he has.'

(2 Kings 5:4) 
So Naaman went in and told his master, saying, 'The girl from the land of Israel said these things.'

(2 Kings 5:5) 
And the king of Syria said to him, 'Go, and I will send letters to the king of Israel.' When Naaman departed, he took with him ten talents of silver, six thousand shekels of gold, and six changes of garments.

(2 Kings 5:6) 
And he brought the letters to the king of Israel, saying, 'When you receive this letter, know that I have sent my servant Naaman to you, so that you may cure him of his leprosy.'

(2 Kings 5:7) 
When the king of Israel read the letters, he tore his clothes in grief and alarm, and said, 'Am I God, that I can kill and make alive, that this man sends to me to cure a person of his leprosy? Observe and see that he is seeking an opportunity for conflict against me.'

(2 Kings 5:8) 
When Elisha, the man of God, heard that the king of Israel had torn his clothes, he sent a message to the king, saying, 'Why have you torn your clothes? Let him come to me, and he will know that there is a prophet in Israel, a man of God who can intercede.'

(2 Kings 5:9) 
So Naaman came with his horses and chariots, and he stopped at the door of Elisha’s house.

(2 Kings 5:10) 
And Elisha sent a messenger to him, saying, 'Go, and wash seven times in the Jordan River, and your flesh will be restored to health, and you will be clean from your leprosy.'

(2 Kings 5:11) 
Naaman departed in anger, saying, 'I thought that he would surely come out to me, and stand and call on the name of the Lord his God, and wave his hand over the place of the leprosy, and cure me.'

(2 Kings 5:12) 
'Are not the rivers of Damascus, Abana and Pharpar, better than all the waters of Israel, that I might wash in them and be clean?' And when he had turned away and was going off in indignation, his servants approached him.

(2 Kings 5:13) 
His servants approached him and spoke to him, saying, 'My father, even if the prophet had told you to do something difficult, you would surely have done it. How much more now that he has said to you, ‘Wash, and you will be clean’?'

(2 Kings 5:14) 
So he went down and washed seven times in the Jordan, according to the word of the man of God. And his flesh was restored like the flesh of a little child, and he was made clean.

(2 Kings 5:15) 
And he returned to the man of God with all his company. He came and stood before him, and said, 'Now I truly know that there is no other God in all the earth, except only in Israel. Therefore, I beg you to accept a gift from your servant.'

(2 Kings 5:16) 
Elisha answered, 'As the Lord lives, before whom I stand, I will not accept it.' And though Naaman urged him, he refused to take the gift.

(2 Kings 5:17) 
Naaman then said, 'If you will not accept a gift, then please, let two mule-loads of earth be given to your servant. For your servant will no longer offer burnt offering or sacrifice to other gods, but only to the Lord, the one true God.'

(2 Kings 5:18) 
But for this one thing alone I pray to the Lord, that when my king enters the temple of Rimmon to worship there, and he leans on my arm, and I bow myself in the temple of Rimmon while he worships in that place — may the Lord forgive your servant for this action, understanding that it is out of duty to my king, not true worship of an idol.

(2 Kings 5:19) 
And Elisha said to him, 'Go in peace.' So Naaman had traveled only a short distance from him.

(2 Kings 5:20) 
But Gehazi, the servant of the man of God, said, 'Behold, my master has let this Naaman, this Syrian, depart without accepting from him what he brought. As the Lord lives, I will run after him and take something from him!'

(2 Kings 5:21) 
So Gehazi pursued Naaman. When Naaman saw him running after him, he dismounted from his chariot to meet him, and said, 'Is everything well?'

(2 Kings 5:22) 
And Gehazi said, 'All is well. My master sent me, saying: Behold, just now two young men from the hill country of Ephraim, from the sons of the prophets, have come to me. Please give them a talent of silver and two changes of garments.'

(2 Kings 5:23) 
Naaman said, 'No, rather take two talents of silver!' And he urged him to take it. Then Naaman tied up two talents of silver in two bags, along with two changes of garments, and put them on two of his servants, who then carried them ahead of Gehazi.

(2 Kings 5:24) 
When Gehazi arrived at the hill, he took the gifts from their hands and stored them in his house. Then he sent the men away, and they departed.

(2 Kings 5:25) 
And he went in and stood before his master. Elisha said to him, 'From where have you come, Gehazi?' He answered, 'Your servant went nowhere.' He was attempting to deceive his master.

(2 Kings 5:26) 
But Elisha said, 'Was not my spirit present when the man turned from his chariot to meet you? Is this the time now to receive money, and to receive garments, and to buy olive groves, and vineyards, and sheep, and oxen, and male servants, and female servants?'

(2 Kings 5:27) 
'Therefore, the leprosy of Naaman will cling to you and to your descendants forever.' And Gehazi went out from his presence, a leper, as white as snow.

(2 Kings 6:1) 
And the disciples of the prophets spoke to Elisha, saying, "Look, this place where we are living with you is too small for all of us."

(2 Kings 6:2) 
They continued, "Let's go down to the Jordan River, and each of us can cut down a tree trunk or log so we can build a larger dwelling place for ourselves there."

(2 Kings 6:3) 
And Elisha responded, "Go ahead."

(2 Kings 6:4) 
Then one of the prophets' disciples said to Elisha, "Please come with us, your servants."

(2 Kings 6:5) 
Elisha replied, "I will come with you." So he went with them. When they arrived at the Jordan, they began cutting down trees and logs.

(2 Kings 6:6) 
As one of them was cutting down a log, the iron axe-head flew off the handle and sank into the water. He cried out in dismay, "Oh no, my master! And I borrowed this axe!"

(2 Kings 6:7) 
The man of God, Elisha, asked, "Where did it fall?" The disciple showed him the exact spot. So Elisha cut off a small piece of wood, threw it into the water at that spot, and the iron axe-head immediately floated to the surface.

(2 Kings 6:8) 
At that time, the King of Syria was at war with Israel. He consulted with his military commanders, saying, "I will set up an ambush at this particular place."

(2 Kings 6:9) 
But the man of God, Elisha, sent a message to the King of Israel, warning him, "Be careful not to pass through that specific location, because the Syrian army has set an ambush there."

(2 Kings 6:10) 
So the King of Israel sent a scouting party to the place Elisha had warned him about and had already given him a heads-up. Because he took precautions, he and his army were saved from danger, not just once or twice, but many times.

(2 Kings 6:11) 
The King of Syria became greatly disturbed by these repeated failures. He called his military commanders together and demanded, "Why aren't you telling me which one of you is betraying us to the King of Israel?"

(2 Kings 6:12) 
One of his commanders answered, "It's not that at all, my Lord King. It is Elisha, the prophet in Israel, who reveals to the King of Israel every single word you speak, even those uttered in the privacy of your innermost chamber!"

(2 Kings 6:13) 
The King of Syria commanded, "Go and find out where he is, so I can send men to capture him!" His scouts reported back to him, saying, "He is in the city of Dothan."

(2 Kings 6:14) 
So the King of Syria dispatched a large army there, with horses and chariots, a truly powerful force. They marched all night and arrived at Dothan before dawn, completely surrounding the city.

(2 Kings 6:15) 
When Elisha's personal servant woke up early and went outside, he saw a vast army, with horses and chariots, completely surrounding Dothan. He rushed back to Elisha and cried out, "Oh no, my master! What are we going to do?"

(2 Kings 6:16) 
But Elisha replied, "Do not be afraid; for there are more with us than there are with them!"

(2 Kings 6:17) 
Then Elisha prayed, "O Lord, open his eyes so that he may see!" And the Lord immediately opened the servant's eyes, and he looked up and saw, and there, on the mountains surrounding Elisha, was a magnificent sight: the mountain was completely full of horses and chariots made of fire, encircling Elisha.

(2 Kings 6:18) 
As the Syrian soldiers came down the mountain toward Elisha, Elisha prayed to the Lord, "Please strike these people with blindness!" And the Lord struck them with complete blindness, just as Elisha had prayed.

(2 Kings 6:19) 
Then Elisha said to them, "This is not the right road, and this isn't the city you're looking for. Follow me, and I will lead you to the man you are searching for." So Elisha led them, still blind, all the way to Samaria—the capital city of Israel.

(2 Kings 6:20) 
Once they had entered Samaria, Elisha prayed, "O Lord, open the eyes of these men so they may see!" And the Lord opened their eyes, and they could see again. And they realized with shock that they were right in the middle of Samaria, surrounded by their enemies.

(2 Kings 6:21) 
When the King of Israel saw the Syrian army suddenly appear in the heart of his capital city, he asked Elisha, "Shall I kill them, my father?"

(2 Kings 6:22) 
Elisha answered, "No, do not kill them! Would you normally kill captives you have taken with your own sword and bow? Instead, give them food and water, so they can eat and drink, and then send them back to their master, the King of Syria."

(2 Kings 6:23) 
So the King of Israel prepared a magnificent feast for the Syrian soldiers. They ate and drank, and then he sent them away, and they returned to their master. After this event, the Syrian raiding parties stopped invading the land of Israel for a significant time.

(2 Kings 6:24) 
However, sometime later, after these events, Ben-Hadad, the King of Syria, gathered his entire army, marched to Samaria, and laid siege to the city.

(2 Kings 6:25) 
A terrible famine gripped Samaria during the siege. The siege lasted so long that a donkey's head, normally considered unclean food, was sold for eighty pieces of silver, and even a quarter-kab of dove's droppings, a truly repulsive and desperate measure, was sold for five pieces of silver.

(2 Kings 6:26) 
As the King of Israel was walking along the city wall to inspect the defenses, a woman cried out to him desperately, "Help me, my Lord King!"

(2 Kings 6:27) 
The king replied, "If the Lord won't help you, how can I possibly help you? Do I have grain from the threshing floor, or wine from the winepress to give you?"

(2 Kings 6:28) 
Then the king asked her, "What is your trouble?" She answered, "This woman here said to me: 'Give up your son, so we can eat him today,' and then tomorrow we will eat my son."

(2 Kings 6:29) 
So we cooked my son, and we ate him. But the next day, when I told her, 'Now it's your turn, give us your son so we can eat him!' she hid her son.

(2 Kings 6:30) 
When the king heard the woman's story, he tore his clothes in a powerful display of grief and repentance. As he continued along the wall, all the people saw that beneath his royal robes, he was wearing sackcloth against his skin—a sign of deep mourning and humility before God.

(2 Kings 6:31) 
He then swore an oath, saying, "May God punish me severely and even more if I allow Elisha, the son of Shaphat, to live through this day!"

(2 Kings 6:32)
