Elisha was sitting in his house at the time, and the elders of Israel were sitting with him. The King of Israel had sent an executioner to behead Elisha. But before the king's messenger arrived, Elisha, knowing by divine revelation, said to the elders, "Do you see how this son of a murderer—referring to the king—has sent someone to cut off my head? When he arrives, make sure the door is shut and hold him back with the doors! For listen, the sound of his master's footsteps—the king himself—is right behind him!"

(2 Kings 6:33) 
While Elisha was still speaking, the king's messenger arrived at the door. And immediately after him, the king himself ascended and began to speak, saying, "This terrible evil—this famine—comes directly from the Lord! Why should I continue to hope or wait for any help from the Lord?"

(2 Kings 6:1) 
Then the sons of the prophets said to Elisha, "Look, this place where we gather and stay with you is now too small for us."

(2 Kings 6:2) 
So let's go down to the Jordan River, and each of us will cut down a log there. Then we can build ourselves a larger place to live in. Elisha replied, "Go ahead."

(2 Kings 6:3) 
But one of them said, "Please, come with your servants." He answered, "I will come."

(2 Kings 6:4) 
So he went with them. When they arrived at the Jordan, they began to cut down trees.

(2 Kings 6:5) 
But as one of them was cutting down a log, the iron head of his axe fell into the water. He cried out, "Oh no, my master! And it was borrowed!"

(2 Kings 6:6) 
The man of God asked, "Where did it fall?" He showed him the place. So Elisha cut off a piece of wood and threw it into the water at that spot, and the axe head floated to the surface.

(2 Kings 6:7) 
Elisha said, "Pick it up." The man reached out his hand and took it.

(2 Kings 6:8) 
Now the King of Syria was at war with Israel. He consulted with his officers, saying, "I will set up an ambush at such and such a place."

(2 Kings 6:9) 
But the man of God — Elisha — sent a message to the King of Israel, saying, "Be careful not to pass through that specific place, because the Syrians are hiding there in ambush."

(2 Kings 6:10) 
So the King of Israel sent a warning to the place which the man of God had told him about and had forewarned him against. The king saved his army there not just once or twice.

(2 Kings 6:11) 
The King of Syria's heart was greatly troubled by this, so he called his officers together and asked them, "Why don't you tell me which of us is betraying us to the King of Israel?"

(2 Kings 6:12) 
One of his officers replied, "By no means, my lord and king. It is Elisha the prophet, who is in Israel, who tells the King of Israel all the words you speak even in your secret bedchamber."

(2 Kings 6:13) 
The king said to them, "Go and find out where he is, so I can send men to capture him." They reported to him, saying, "Look, he is in Dothan."

(2 Kings 6:14) 
So the king sent horses and chariots and a great army there. They arrived at night and surrounded the city.

(2 Kings 6:15) 
When the servant of the man of God rose early in the morning and went out, he saw an army surrounding the city with horses and chariots. The servant said to him, "Oh no, my master! What shall we do?"

(2 Kings 6:16) 
But Elisha said, "Do not be afraid. For there are more with us than there are with them."

(2 Kings 6:17) 
Then Elisha prayed and said, "Lord, open this young man's eyes so he may see." And the Lord opened the eyes of the young man, and he saw! Behold, the mountain was full of horses and chariots of fire all around Elisha.

(2 Kings 6:18) 
When the Syrians came down toward him, Elisha prayed to the Lord, saying, "Strike this nation with blindness, I beg You." And the Lord struck them with blindness, just as Elisha had requested.

(2 Kings 6:19) 
Then Elisha said to them, "This is not the right road, nor is this the city you're looking for. Follow me, and I will lead you to the man you seek." So he led them into Samaria, the capital of Israel.

(2 Kings 6:20) 
When they had entered Samaria, Elisha said, "Lord, open the eyes of these men so they may see." And the Lord opened their eyes, and they looked around. Behold, they realized they were in the middle of Samaria!

(2 Kings 6:21) 
When the King of Israel saw them, he asked Elisha, "My father, shall I strike them down? Shall I strike them down?"

(2 Kings 6:22) 
Elisha answered, "You must not strike them down. Do you strike down even those you have taken captive with your sword and bow? Set food and water before them, so they may eat and drink, and then return to their master, the King of Syria."

(2 Kings 6:23) 
So the King of Israel prepared a great feast for them. After they had eaten and drunk, he sent them away. They returned to their master, and the raiding parties of the Syrians did not come into the land of Israel again.

(2 Kings 6:24) 
However, after this, Ben-Hadad, the King of Syria, gathered his entire army, marched up, and besieged Samaria.

(2 Kings 6:25) 
There was a great famine in Samaria. The city was under such a long siege that a donkey's head was sold for eighty pieces of silver, and a quarter of a cab (a small measure) of dove's dung for five pieces of silver. People were desperate for any food.

(2 Kings 6:26) 
As the King of Israel was walking along the city wall, a woman cried out to him, saying, "Help me, my lord and king!"

(2 Kings 6:27) 
He replied, "If the Lord does not save you, where can I get help for you? From the threshing floor, or from the winepress? I have no food to give."

(2 Kings 6:28) 
Then the king asked her, "What is your trouble?" She answered, "This woman said to me, 'Give up your son so we can eat him today, and we will eat my son tomorrow.'"

(2 Kings 6:29) 
So we cooked my son and ate him. Then I said to her the next day, 'Give up your son so we can eat him.' But she hid her son away.

(2 Kings 6:30) 
When the king heard the woman's words, he tore his clothes. As he walked along the wall, all the people saw that he was wearing sackcloth underneath, against his skin.

(2 Kings 6:31) 
Then the king said, "May God do so to me, and even more, if the head of Elisha, the son of Shaphat, remains on his shoulders this very day!"

(2 Kings 6:32) 
Now Elisha was sitting in his house, and the elders were sitting with him. The king had sent a messenger to behead Elisha. But before the messenger arrived, Elisha said to the elders, "Do you see that this son of a murderer has sent someone to take off my head? Look, when the messenger comes, shut the door and hold it fast against him with the door bar. For indeed, the sound of his master's footsteps is right behind him!"

(2 Kings 6:33) 
While Elisha was still speaking with them, the messenger appeared. And the messenger said, "Look, this disaster is from the Lord! Why should I wait for the Lord any longer?"

(2 Kings 6:1) 
The sons of the prophets—that is, the disciples under Elisha's guidance—told Elisha: "Look, the place where we are staying with you is too small for us."

(2 Kings 6:2) 
"Let's go all the way to the Jordan River, and each of us will take a single log from the trees there, so we can build ourselves a new dwelling place." Elisha replied: "Go ahead."

(2 Kings 6:3) 
Then one of them said, "Please, come with your servants as well." He answered: "I will come."

(2 Kings 6:4) 
So he went with them. And when they arrived at the Jordan River, they began to cut down trees.

(2 Kings 6:5) 
It happened that as one of them was cutting down a tree, the iron axe-head fell into the water. He cried out in distress and said: "Oh no, my master! And I even borrowed this axe-head."

(2 Kings 6:6) 
And the man of God—that is, Elisha—asked: "Where did it fall?" The man showed him the spot. So Elisha cut off a piece of wood and threw it toward that place, and the axe-head floated to the surface.

(2 Kings 6:7) 
And Elisha said: "Pick it up." So he reached out his hand and took it.

(2 Kings 6:8) 
Now the king of Syria was making war against Israel, and after taking counsel with his servants, he said: "In such and such a place I will set an ambush."

(2 Kings 6:9) 
Therefore, the man of God—Elisha—sent word to the king of Israel, saying: "Be careful not to pass through that specific place, because the Syrians are lying in ambush there."

(2 Kings 6:10) 
And the king of Israel sent men to the place that the man of God had told him about and had warned him of. And the king of Israel took precautions there, not just once or twice.

(2 Kings 6:11) 
The heart of the king of Syria was greatly troubled by this matter. He called his servants together and said: "Why don't you tell me who among us is a traitor to the king of Israel?"

(2 Kings 6:12) 
And one of his servants said: "By no means, my lord king. It is not a traitor among us, but rather Elisha the prophet, who is in Israel, who tells the king of Israel all the words that you speak even in your private bedchamber."

(2 Kings 6:13) 
So the king said: "Go and see where he is, so that I may send and capture him." And it was reported to him by those who said: "Look, he is in Dothan."

(2 Kings 6:14) 
Therefore, he sent horses and chariots and a strong army there. When they arrived by night, they surrounded the city.

(2 Kings 6:15) 
So at dawn, the servant of the man of God arose and went out, and he saw the army encircling the city, with horses and chariots. And he reported to Elisha, saying: "Oh no, my master, what shall we do?"

(2 Kings 6:16) 
But Elisha answered: "Do not be afraid, for those who are with us are more numerous than those who are with them."

(2 Kings 6:17) 
And Elisha prayed and said: "Lord, open this young man's eyes so that he may see." And the Lord opened the eyes of the young man, and he saw, and behold, the mountain was full of horses and chariots of fire all around Elisha.

(2 Kings 6:18) 
Now as the Syrians came down toward him, Elisha prayed to the Lord, saying: "Please, strike this people with blindness." And the Lord struck them with blindness, according to Elisha's word.

(2 Kings 6:19) 
And Elisha said to them: "This is not the way, nor is this the city you're looking for. Follow me, and I will lead you to the man you are seeking." So he led them to Samaria.

(2 Kings 6:20) 
And when they had entered Samaria, Elisha said: "Lord, open the eyes of these men so that they may see." And the Lord opened their eyes, and they saw, and behold, they were in the middle of Samaria—the capital city of Israel, deep within enemy territory.

(2 Kings 6:21) 
And the king of Israel, seeing them, said to Elisha: "Should I strike them down, my father?"

(2 Kings 6:22) 
Elisha replied: "You shall not strike them down. For you would not strike down even those you captured with your sword and your bow in battle. Instead, set bread and water before them, so that they may eat and drink, and then return to their master."

(2 Kings 6:23) 
So the king prepared a great meal for them. And they ate and drank, and he sent them away, and they returned to their master. And the raiding parties of Syria did not come into the land of Israel any more.

(2 Kings 6:24) 
But it came to pass after these events that Ben-hadad, the king of Syria, gathered all his army, and marched up and besieged Samaria.

(2 Kings 6:25) 
And there was a great famine in Samaria. And it was besieged for so long that an ass's head was sold for eighty pieces of silver—an exorbitant price for an unclean animal—and a quarter of a measure of dove's dung was sold for five pieces of silver—a sign of extreme desperation.

(2 Kings 6:26) 
As the king of Israel was passing by on the wall, a woman cried out to him, saying: "Help me, my lord king!"

(2 Kings 6:27) 
And he said: "May the Lord help you! How can I help you? Is it from the threshing floor or from the winepress?"—implying he had no provisions from either.

(2 Kings 6:28) 
And the king asked her: "What is your trouble?" And she replied: "This woman said to me: 'Give your son, so that we may eat him today, and then tomorrow we will eat my son.'"

(2 Kings 6:29) 
"So we cooked my son and ate him. And the next day, I said to her: 'Give your son, so that we may eat him.' But she hid him."

(2 Kings 6:30) 
When the king heard the words of the woman, he tore his garments, and as he walked along the wall, all the people saw that he was wearing sackcloth underneath, next to his skin, as a sign of mourning and repentance.

(2 Kings 6:31) 
And he said: "May God do to me and add to it more punishment, if the head of Elisha, the son of Shaphat, remains on him this day!"—meaning he swore to execute Elisha.

(2 Kings 6:32) 
Elisha, however, was sitting in his house, and the elders were sitting with him. So the king sent a man from his presence. But before the messenger could arrive, Elisha said to the elders: "Do you see that this son of a murderer—meaning the king—has sent someone to take off my head? Look, when the messenger comes, shut the door and hold him back with it. For behold, the sound of his master's feet is right behind him."

(2 Kings 6:33) 
While he was still speaking—Elisha, that is—the messenger who was coming to him appeared. And the messenger said: "Behold, such great evil has come from the Lord! Why should I wait any longer for the Lord's help?"

(2 Kings 7:1) 
Then Elisha, the prophet, said: 'Listen now to the word of the Lord! This is what the Lord says: Tomorrow, at this same time of day, within the gates of Samaria, the famine will be over. Then, two measures of fine flour will be sold for just one silver coin, and four measures of barley will be sold for one silver coin.'

(2 Kings 7:2) 
But the royal officer, upon whose arm the king leaned (indicating his high trust and authority), answered the man of God, saying: 'Even if the Lord were to open floodgates in the sky and make food rain down, could this possibly happen?' And Elisha, the prophet, replied: 'You will see it with your own eyes, but you will not partake in the abundance that follows.'

(2 Kings 7:3) 
Now there were four men afflicted with leprosy near the entrance of the city gate. They said to one another, 'Why are we sitting here until we die?'

(2 Kings 7:4) 
If we decide to go into the city, we will die there from starvation. If we remain here, we will also die. So come, let us desert and go over to the camp of the Syrians. If they spare our lives, we will live. But if they kill us, then we will simply die.

(2 Kings 7:5) 
So they rose up in the evening to go to the camp of the Syrians. But when they came to the edge of the camp, they found no one there.

(2 Kings 7:6) 
For the Lord had caused the Syrian army in the camp to hear the sound of chariots and of horses, and the sound of a very large army approaching. And they had said to one another: 'Look! The king of Israel has hired the kings of the Hittites and the kings of the Egyptians to attack us and come against us.'

(2 Kings 7:7) 
Therefore, rising up, they fled in silence, abandoning their tents, their horses, their donkeys, and the entire camp, exactly as it was. They simply fled for their lives.

(2 Kings 7:8) 
So when those lepers came to the edge of the camp, they entered one tent, and they ate and drank. They took from there silver, gold, and clothing, and they went away and hid them. Then they returned to another tent, and from there they took more things and hid them too.

(2 Kings 7:9) 
Then they said to one another: 'What we are doing is not right. This is a day of good news, and if we remain silent and do not report it until morning, we will be found guilty of a terrible crime. Come, let us go and report it in the king's palace.'

(2 Kings 7:10) 
So when they arrived at the city gate, they called out, saying: 'We came to the camp of the Syrians, and we found no one there! There was no sound of people, but only horses and donkeys tied up, and the tents just as they were left.'

(2 Kings 7:11) 
Therefore, they reported it to the gatekeepers of the city, who immediately announced it in the king's palace.

(2 Kings 7:12) 
Then the king rose up in the night and said to his servants: 'I will tell you what the Syrians have done to us. They know that we are suffering from famine, and that is why they have left their camp and hidden themselves in the fields, thinking: When the people come out of the city looking for food, we will capture them alive, and then we will enter the city ourselves.'

(2 Kings 7:13) 
One of his servants answered him: 'Let us take five of the remaining horses in the city. Indeed, the entire multitude of Israel that remains here is already like those who have perished (meaning, they are near death from starvation). Let us send them out, and see what is happening.'

(2 Kings 7:14) 
So they sent two horses and chariots (presumably carrying men), and they went out after them, saying: 'Go and see!'

(2 Kings 7:15) 
They followed the Syrians all the way to the Jordan River. And behold, the entire road was full of clothing and equipment, which the Syrians had thrown away in their haste to flee. And returning, they reported it to the king.

(2 Kings 7:16) 
Then the people went out and plundered the camp of the Syrians. And just as the Lord had declared, two measures of fine flour were sold for one silver coin, and four measures of barley were sold for one silver coin.

(2 Kings 7:17) 
Now the king had appointed that very royal officer (who was his close advisor) to be in charge of the gate. But the crowd trampled him in the gateway as they rushed out, and he died, just as the man of God had prophesied when the king came to him (earlier, during the famine).

(2 Kings 7:18) 
For it happened exactly according to the word of the man of God, who had said to the king: 'Two measures of fine flour will be sold for one silver coin, and four measures of barley will be sold for one silver coin, by this time tomorrow in the gate of Samaria.'

(2 Kings 7:19) 
When that officer had also responded to the man of God, saying: 'Even if the Lord were to open floodgates in the sky, could this possibly happen?' And Elisha had said to him: 'You will indeed see it with your own eyes, but you will not partake in that abundance.'

(2 Kings 7:20) 
And it happened to him just as Elisha had foretold: for the people trampled him in the gateway, and he died there.

(2 Kings 7:1) 
It happened that the king was dwelling securely in his own house, and the Lord had given him rest on every side from all his enemies,

(2 Kings 7:2) 
he then said to Nathan the prophet: “Look, I am living in a house built with cedar wood, but the Ark of God, which represents the Lord's presence, is placed only inside curtains.”

(2 Kings 7:3) 
And Nathan said to the king: “Go and do everything that is in your heart, for the Lord is with you in this endeavor.”

(2 Kings 7:4) 
However, it happened that in that very night, behold, the word of the Lord came to Nathan, saying:

(2 Kings 7:5) 
“Go and speak to My servant David: ‘Thus says the Lord: Are you the one who will build a house for Me to dwell in?’”

(2 Kings 7:6) 
“For I have not lived in a permanent house from the day I brought the children of Israel out of the land of Egypt until this very day; instead, I have moved about in a tabernacle, which is a portable sanctuary, and in a tent.”

(2 Kings 7:7) 
“In all the places through which I have passed with all the children of Israel, did I ever speak a word to any one of the tribes of Israel, to whom I commanded to feed My people Israel, saying: ‘Why have you not built Me a cedar house?’”

(2 Kings 7:8) 
“And now, you shall say this to My servant David: ‘Thus says the Lord of hosts: I took you from the pastures, from following the flock, so that you would be a leader over My people Israel.’”

(2 Kings 7:9) 
“And I have been with you in all places wherever you have walked, and I have destroyed all your enemies from before you; and I have made for you a great name, like the name of the great ones who are on the earth.”

(2 Kings 7:10) 
“And I will appoint a place for My people Israel, and I will plant them there, and they will live securely under their own rule, and they will not be disturbed any longer; nor will the sons of wickedness oppress them again, as they did at the first,”

(2 Kings 7:11) 
“from the day that I appointed judges over My people Israel. And I will give you rest from all your enemies. Furthermore, the Lord proclaims to you that He Himself will make a house for you—a dynasty and a lasting lineage.”

(2 Kings 7:12) 
“And when your days are completed, and you sleep with your fathers, I will raise up your offspring after you, who will come from your body, and I will establish his kingdom firmly.”

(2 Kings 7:13) 
“He himself will build a house for My name, a temple of worship, and I will establish the throne of his kingdom forever.”

(2 Kings 7:14) 
“I will be to him a father, and he himself will be to Me a son. If he does anything wickedly, I will discipline him with the rod of men, and with the scourges of the sons of men, as a father would correct his child.”

(2 Kings 7:15) 
“But My mercy I will not take away from him, as I took it away from Saul, whom I removed from My presence.”

(2 Kings 7:16) 
“And your house shall be faithful, and your kingdom shall endure forever before you; and your throne shall be firm perpetually.”

(2 Kings 7:17) 
According to all these words, and according to all this vision, so Nathan spoke to David.

(2 Kings 7:18) 
Then King David entered and sat before the Lord, and he said: “Who am I, Lord God, and what is my house, that you have brought me to this point of favor?”

(2 Kings 7:19) 
“But even this is a small thing in Your sight, Lord God, unless You have also spoken concerning the house of Your servant for a long time to come; this is the law and decree of man, Lord God, that such a promise would be made.”

(2 Kings 7:20) 
“Therefore, what more can David add by speaking to You? For You know Your servant, Lord God, and all his thoughts.”

(2 Kings 7:21) 
“Because of Your word, and according to Your own heart's desire, You have done all these great things, so that You might make them known to Your servant.”

(2 Kings 7:22) 
“For this reason, You are magnified, Lord God, for there is none like You, nor is there any God besides You, in all that we have heard with our own ears.”

(2 Kings 7:23) 
“And what other nation on earth is like Your people Israel, whom You went to redeem for Yourself as a people, and to make a name for Yourself, and to perform great and terrible things for them on the earth, delivering them from the face of Your nation whom You redeemed for Yourself out of Egypt, from their peoples and their false worship?”

(2 Kings 7:24) 
“And You have established Your people Israel for Yourself as a people forever; and You, O Lord, have become their God.”

(2 Kings 7:25) 
“Now therefore, Lord God, the word that You have spoken concerning Your servant and concerning his house, fulfill it eternally; and do as You have spoken.”

(2 Kings 7:26) 
“So that Your name may be magnified forever, and people may say: ‘The Lord of hosts is God over Israel,’ and the house of Your servant David may be established before You.”

(2 Kings 7:27) 
“For You, Lord of hosts, God of Israel, have revealed to Your servant, by whispering in his ear, saying: ‘I will build a house for you.’ Because of this, Your servant has found the courage in his heart to pray this prayer to You.”

(2 Kings 7:28) 
“Now therefore, Lord God, You are God, and Your words will be true; for You have spoken these good things to Your servant.”

(2 Kings 7:29) 
“Begin therefore and bless the house of Your servant, so that it may be forever before You; for You, Lord God, have spoken, and with Your blessing, the house of Your servant will be blessed eternally.”

(2 Kings 7:1) 
Then Elisha said, "Hear the word of the Lord! This is what the Lord says: At this very hour tomorrow, a seah (a measure) of fine flour will be sold for three shekels (a unit of silver currency), and two seahs of barley for four shekels, right at the market gate of Samaria."

(2 Kings 7:2) 
However, one of the king's officers, who was responsible for the king's personal safety and whose arm the king leaned upon, answered the man of God, saying, "Even if the Lord were to open the floodgates of the sky, could such a thing actually happen?" And Elisha said, "You will see it with your own eyes, but you will not eat any of it."

(2 Kings 7:3) 
Now there were four men who had leprosy sitting near the entrance of the city gate. They said to each other, "Why are we sitting here until we die?"

(2 Kings 7:4) 
If we go into the city, we will die there because of the famine. If we stay here, we will surely die. So come on, let's desert to the camp of the Arameans (Syrians). If they spare our lives, we will live. If they kill us, then we will simply die.

(2 Kings 7:5) 
So they got up in the evening to go to the camp of the Arameans. When they came to the edge of the Aramean camp, they found no one there.

(2 Kings 7:6) 
For the Lord had made the Aramean army hear the sound of chariots, horses, and a very large army. So they said to one another, "Look, the king of Israel has hired the kings of the Hittites and the kings of Egypt to come and attack us!"

(2 Kings 7:7) 
Because of this, they got up and fled silently in the evening, abandoning their tents, their horses, their donkeys in the camp, and everything just as it was. They simply fled for their lives.

(2 Kings 7:8) 
So when those men with leprosy came to the edge of the camp, they went into one tent and ate and drank. They took silver, gold, and clothing from there, and went and hid them. Then they returned to another tent and likewise took things from there and hid them.

(2 Kings 7:9) 
Then they said to one another, "What we are doing is not right. This is a day of good news, and if we keep silent and do not report it until morning, we will be held accountable for our wickedness. Come now, let's go and report it to the king's palace."

(2 Kings 7:10) 
So they went and called out to the gatekeepers of the city, saying, "We went to the camp of the Arameans, and we found no one there, nor any sound of a human, but only horses and donkeys tied up, and the tents just as they were left."

(2 Kings 7:11) 
The gatekeepers then went and announced the news inside the king's palace.

(2 Kings 7:12) 
The king rose up in the night and said to his servants, "I will tell you what the Arameans have done to us. They know that we are suffering from famine, and that is why they have left their camp and hidden themselves in the fields. They are thinking, 'When they come out of the city, we will capture them alive and then enter the city.'"

(2 Kings 7:13) 
One of his servants answered him and said, "Let's take five of the remaining horses in the city, because the entire population of Israel remaining in it will be like those who are already dead. Indeed, the entire population of Israel is almost consumed by the famine. Let us send them out and see what is happening."

(2 Kings 7:14) 
So they took two chariots with horses, and the king sent them to the Aramean camp, saying, "Go and see."

(2 Kings 7:15) 
They went after them as far as the Jordan River. And behold, the entire road was full of garments and equipment that the Arameans had thrown away in their haste when they were in a panic. The messengers returned and reported this to the king.

(2 Kings 7:16) 
Then the people went out and plundered the camp of the Arameans. So a seah of fine flour was sold for three shekels, and two seahs of barley for four shekels, exactly as the Lord had spoken.

(2 Kings 7:17) 
Now the king had put that officer, on whose arm he leaned, in charge of the city gate. But the crowd trampled him in the gate, and he died, just as the man of God had prophesied when the king came down to speak with him.

(2 Kings 7:18) 
So it happened exactly according to the word of the man of God, which he had spoken to the king when he said: "Two seahs of barley will be sold for four shekels, and a seah of fine flour for three shekels, tomorrow at the gate of Samaria."

(2 Kings 7:19) 
And when that officer had answered him and said, "What if the Lord were to open the floodgates of the sky, could such a thing actually happen?" Elisha had said to him, "You will see it with your own eyes, but you will not eat any of it."

(2 Kings 7:20) 
And it happened to him just as it had been said, because the people trampled him in the gate, and he died.

(2 Kings 8:1) 
Eliseus then spoke to the woman whose son he had restored to life, telling her: 'Get up, and go, you and your entire household, and reside as a foreigner wherever you can; for the Lord has commanded a devastating famine upon this land, and it will last for seven years.'

(2 Kings 8:2) 
So the woman got up, and she left with all of her household, and they resided as foreigners in the land of the Philistines for the entire seven years.

(2 Kings 8:3) 
And when the seven years were finished, the woman returned from the land of the Philistines. And she went to appeal to the king about her house and her fields, which had likely been taken by others.

(2 Kings 8:4) 
Now, the king was speaking with Giezi, the servant of the man of God, Eliseus. The king was saying: 'Tell me all the great things Eliseus has done.'

(2 Kings 8:5) 
As Giezi was telling how Eliseus had raised the dead boy back to life, the very woman whose son Eliseus had restored to life appeared, crying out to the king concerning her house and her fields. Then Giezi said: 'My lord the king, this is the woman, and this is her son, whom Eliseus brought back to life.'

(2 Kings 8:6) 
And the king questioned the woman, and she told him her story. Then the king gave her an official, saying: 'Restore to her all that is hers, and all the income from her fields, from the day she left the land until now.'

(2 Kings 8:7) 
Eliseus also went to Damascus, and Benadad, the king of Syria, was sick. And it was announced to him, with people saying: 'The man of God has come here!'

(2 Kings 8:8) 
And the king said to Hazaël, one of his officials: 'Take gifts with you, and go to meet the man of God, and consult the Lord through him, asking: "Will I recover from this illness?"'

(2 Kings 8:9) 
So Hazaël went to meet him, bringing gifts with him—all the good things of Damascus, a load for forty camels. And when he arrived, he stood before Eliseus and said: 'Your son Benadad, the king of Syria, has sent me to you, asking: "Will I recover from this illness?"'

(2 Kings 8:10) 
And Eliseus said to him: 'Go, tell him: "You will surely recover"— but the Lord has shown me that he will certainly die.'

(2 Kings 8:11) 
And Eliseus stood with him, staring intently. Hazaël became troubled and embarrassed, and then the man of God, Eliseus, wept.

(2 Kings 8:12) 
To him, Hazaël said: 'Why is my lord weeping?' Eliseus answered: 'Because I know what evils you will inflict upon the children of Israel: you will set their fortified cities on fire, you will kill their young men with the sword, you will dash their little ones to pieces, and you will rip open their pregnant women.'

(2 Kings 8:13) 
And Hazaël said: 'What is your servant, a mere dog, that I should do such a great evil?' And Eliseus said: 'The Lord has shown me that you will be king over Syria.'

(2 Kings 8:14) 
And when he had departed from Eliseus, he came to his master. Who said to him: 'What did Eliseus say to you?' And he answered: 'He told me: "You will surely recover."

(2 Kings 8:15) 
But the very next day, Hazaël took a thick cloth, soaked it in water, and spread it over Benadad’s face, smothering him. And when he was dead, Hazaël reigned in his place.

(2 Kings 8:16) 
In the fifth year of Joram, son of Achab, king of Israel, while Josaphat was king of Juda, Joram, son of Josaphat, king of Juda, began to reign.

(2 Kings 8:17) 
He was thirty-two years old when he began to reign, and he reigned for eight years in Jerusalem.

(2 Kings 8:18) 
And he walked in the ways of the kings of Israel, just as the house of Achab had walked, because a daughter of Achab was his wife. And he did evil in the sight of the Lord.

(2 Kings 8:19) 
However, the Lord would not destroy Juda, for the sake of David, His servant, just as He had promised him by speaking, and by giving him a lamp—a continuous line of descendants—and to his sons for all days.

(2 Kings 8:20) 
In his days, Edom revolted so that it would no longer be under the rule of Juda, and it appointed a king for itself.

(2 Kings 8:21) 
So Joram went to Seira, and all the chariots with him. And he rose up in the night and attacked the Idumeans who had surrounded him, along with the commanders of their chariots; but the people fled to their tents.

(2 Kings 8:22) 
Therefore Edom revolted from being under Juda, and it remains so to this present day. At that same time, Libna also revolted.

(2 Kings 8:23) 
Now, the rest of the acts of Joram, and all that he did, are these not written in the book of the chronicles of the kings of Juda?

(2 Kings 8:24) 
And Joram slept with his fathers, and he was buried with them in the City of David. And Ochozias, his son, reigned in his place.

(2 Kings 8:25) 
In the twelfth year of Joram, son of Achab, king of Israel, Ochozias, son of Joram, king of Juda, began to reign.

(2 Kings 8:26) 
Ochozias was twenty-two years old when he began to reign, and he reigned for one year in Jerusalem. His mother’s name was Athalia, daughter of Amri, king of Israel.

(2 Kings 8:27) 
And he walked in the ways of the house of Achab, and he did evil in the sight of the Lord, just like the house of Achab, for he was a son-in-law of Achab.

(2 Kings 8:28) 
He also went with Joram, son of Achab, to war against Hazaël, king of Syria, in Ramoth Galaad; and the Syrians wounded Joram.

(2 Kings 8:29) 
So Joram returned to be healed in Jezraël because of the wounds that the Syrians had inflicted on him in Ramoth, when he fought against Hazaël, the king of Syria. And Ochozias, son of Joram, king of Juda, went down to visit Joram, son of Achab, who was sick in Jezraël.

(2 Kings 8:1) 
But Elisha spoke to the woman whose son he had restored to life, saying, "Rise up, you and your household, and go live as a foreigner wherever you can; for the Lord has called a famine upon the land, and it will last for seven years."

(2 Kings 8:2) 
So she rose up and went with all her household, and lived as a foreigner in the land of the Philistines for seven years.

(2 Kings 8:3) 
When the seven years were finished, the woman returned from the land of the Philistines, and she went out to appeal to the king concerning her house and her fields.

(2 Kings 8:4) 
Now the king was speaking with Gehazi, the servant of the man of God, saying, "Tell me all the great works that Elisha has done."

(2 Kings 8:5) 
As Gehazi was telling the king how Elisha had raised the dead, the very woman whose son Elisha had restored to life appeared, crying out to the king concerning her house and her fields. And Gehazi said, "My lord king, this is the woman, and this is her son whom Elisha raised from the dead!"

(2 Kings 8:6) 
The king then questioned the woman, and she told him her story. So the king gave her an official, saying, "Restore to her all that belonged to her, and all the income from her fields, from the day she left the land until now."

(2 Kings 8:7) 
Now Elisha came to Damascus, and Ben-hadad king of Syria was sick. They reported to him, saying, "The man of God has come here!"

(2 Kings 8:8) 
And the king said to Hazael, "Take gifts with you, and go meet the man of God, and inquire of the Lord through him, saying, 'Will I recover from this sickness?'"

(2 Kings 8:9) 
So Hazael went to meet Elisha, carrying gifts with him, all the good things of Damascus, a load for forty camels. When he came, he stood before him and said, "Your son Ben-hadad, king of Syria, has sent me to you, saying, 'Will I recover from this sickness?'"

(2 Kings 8:10) 
And Elisha said to him, "Go, tell him, 'You will certainly recover.' However, the Lord has shown me that he will surely die a different death."

(2 Kings 8:11) 
Then Elisha stared fixedly until Hazael was confused and ashamed; and the man of God wept.

(2 Kings 8:12) 
And Hazael said, "Why does my lord weep?" He answered, "Because I know the evil that you will do to the children of Israel: you will burn their fortified cities with fire, and you will kill their young men with the sword, and you will dash their little ones to pieces, and rip open their pregnant women."

(2 Kings 8:13) 
To which Hazael said, "Who is your servant, my lord, but a dog, that I should do this great evil?" And Elisha said, "The Lord has shown me that you will be king of Syria."

(2 Kings 8:14) 
So he departed from Elisha and came to his master. And Ben-hadad said to him, "What did Elisha say to you?" And Hazael answered, "He told me, 'You will recover your health.'"

(2 Kings 8:15) 
But the next day, Hazael took a thick blanket, soaked it in water, and spread it over Ben-hadad's face, so he suffocated. When Ben-hadad was dead, Hazael reigned in his place.

(2 Kings 8:16) 
In the fifth year of Joram, son of Ahab, king of Israel—while Jehoshaphat was still king of Judah—Jehoram, son of Jehoshaphat, began to reign as king of Judah.

(2 Kings 8:17) 
He was thirty-two years old when he began to reign, and he reigned for eight years in Jerusalem.

(2 Kings 8:18) 
And he walked in the ways of the kings of Israel, just as the house of Ahab had walked, for the daughter of Ahab was his wife; and he did evil in the sight of the Lord.

(2 Kings 8:19) 
However, the Lord was unwilling to destroy Judah for the sake of David His servant, just as He had promised him that He would give him a lamp, a line of descendants, for all days.

(2 Kings 8:20) 
In his days, Edom revolted from being under the rule of Judah and appointed a king for themselves.

(2 Kings 8:21) 
So Jehoram went to Zair, and all his chariots with him; and he rose up by night and struck the Edomites who had surrounded him and the captains of the chariots. Then the people fled to their tents.

(2 Kings 8:22) 
Thus Edom revolted from being under Judah to this present day. At that time, Libnah also revolted.

(2 Kings 8:23) 
Now the rest of the acts of Jehoram, and all that he did, are they not written in the Book of the Annals of the Kings of Judah?

(2 Kings 8:24) 
And Jehoram rested with his fathers and was buried with them in the City of David; and Ahaziah, his son, reigned in his place.

(2 Kings 8:25) 
In the twelfth year of Joram, son of Ahab, king of Israel, Ahaziah, son of Jehoram, king of Judah, began to reign.

(2 Kings 8:26) 
Ahaziah was twenty-two years old when he began to reign, and he reigned for one year in Jerusalem. The name of his mother was Athaliah, the daughter of Omri, king of Israel.

(2 Kings 8:27) 
And he walked in the ways of the house of Ahab, and did evil in the sight of the Lord, just like the house of Ahab, for he was a son-in-law of Ahab's house.

(2 Kings 8:28) 
He also went with Joram, son of Ahab, to fight against Hazael, king of Syria, in Ramoth-gilead; and the Syrians wounded Joram.

(2 Kings 8:29) 
So Joram returned to Jezreel to recover from the wounds with which the Syrians had struck him at Ramoth, when he fought against Hazael, king of Syria. And Ahaziah, son of Jehoram, king of Judah, went down to visit Joram, son of Ahab, in Jezreel, because he was sick.

(2 Kings 8:1) 
Elisha had spoken to the woman whose son he had brought back to life, saying: "Get up and leave, you and your household, and find a place to live as a foreigner wherever you can, because the Lord has called for a famine to come upon the land, and it will last for seven years."

(2 Kings 8:2) 
So she got up and left with all her household, and lived as a foreigner in the land of the Philistines for seven years.

(2 Kings 8:3) 
And when the seven years were completed, the woman returned from the land of the Philistines. She went out to appeal to the king concerning her house and her fields, seeking their restoration.

(2 Kings 8:4) 
Meanwhile, the king was speaking with Gehazi, the servant of the man of God, saying: "Tell me all the great and powerful things that Elisha has done."

(2 Kings 8:5) 
And just as Gehazi was telling how Elisha had brought a dead person back to life, the very woman appeared, whose son Elisha had restored to life, crying out to the king about her house and her fields. Gehazi then said: "My lord king, this is the woman, and this is her son whom Elisha restored to life."

(2 Kings 8:6) 
And the king questioned the woman, and she told him her story. So the king gave her an official, saying: "Restore to her all that belongs to her, and all her fields from the day she left the land until now."

(2 Kings 8:7) 
Elisha also came to Damascus, when Ben-Hadad, the king of Syria, was sick. And they announced to the king, saying: "The man of God has come here."

(2 Kings 8:8) 
And the king said to Hazael: "Take gifts with you, and go to meet the man of God. Consult the Lord through him, saying: 'Will I be able to recover from this illness?'"

(2 Kings 8:9) 
So Hazael went to meet Elisha, carrying gifts with him, and all the good things of Damascus, a load for forty camels. And when he stood before him, he said: "Your son Ben-Hadad, the king of Syria, has sent me to you, saying: 'Will I be able to recover from this illness?'"

(2 Kings 8:10) 
And Elisha said to him: "Go and tell him: 'You will certainly recover.' However, the Lord has shown me that he will nevertheless surely die by other means."

(2 Kings 8:11) 
And the man of God stood there, troubled, and then wept.

(2 Kings 8:12) 
Hazael said to him: "Why does my lord weep?" And Elisha said: "Because I know the evils you will inflict upon the children of Israel: you will burn their strongholds with fire, you will kill their young men with the sword, you will dash their little ones to pieces, and you will rip open their pregnant women."

(2 Kings 8:13) 
And Hazael said: "But what am I, your servant, a mere dog, that I should do such a great deed?" And Elisha said: "The Lord has shown me that you will be king of Syria."

(2 Kings 8:14) 
And when he had departed from Elisha, he came to his master, who asked him: "What did Elisha say to you?" And Hazael responded: "He told me: 'You will certainly recover.'"

(2 Kings 8:15) 
However, the next day, Hazael took a thick cloth, soaked it in water, and spread it over Ben-Hadad's face, so that he suffocated and died. And Hazael reigned in his place.

(2 Kings 8:16) 
In the fifth year of Joram, son of Ahab, king of Israel, and while Jehoshaphat was king of Judah, Joram, son of Jehoshaphat, became king of Judah.

(2 Kings 8:17) 
He was thirty-two years old when he began to reign, and he reigned for eight years in Jerusalem.

(2 Kings 8:18) 
And he walked in the ways of the kings of Israel, just as the house of Ahab had walked, for the daughter of Ahab was his wife. And he did evil in the sight of the Lord.

(2 Kings 8:19) 
Yet the Lord was unwilling to destroy Judah, for the sake of His servant David, just as He had promised him that He would always give him and his sons a lamp, meaning a perpetual lineage on the throne.

(2 Kings 8:20) 
In those days, Edom revolted and separated from the control of Judah, and set up a king for themselves.

(2 Kings 8:21) 
So Joram went to Zair, and all his chariots with him. And he rose up by night and struck the Edomites who had surrounded him; but the rest of the Edomite people had already fled to their tents.

(2 Kings 8:22) 
And Edom remained separate from the control of Judah until this present day. At that time, Libnah also revolted.

(2 Kings 8:23) 
The rest of the acts of Joram, and all that he did, are they not written in the Book of the Annals of the Kings of Judah?

(2 Kings 8:24) 
And Joram rested with his ancestors and was buried with them in the City of David. Then Ahaziah, his son, reigned in his place.

(2 Kings 8:25) 
In the twelfth year of Joram, son of Ahab, king of Israel, Ahaziah, son of Joram, king of Judah, began to reign.

(2 Kings 8:26) 
Ahaziah was twenty-two years old when he began to reign, and he reigned for one year in Jerusalem. His mother's name was Athaliah, daughter of Omri, king of Israel.

(2 Kings 8:27) 
And he walked in the ways of the house of Ahab, and did evil in the sight of the Lord, just as the house of Ahab did; for he was allied by marriage to the house of Ahab.

(2 Kings 8:28) 
He also went with Joram, son of Ahab, to fight against Hazael, king of Syria, in Ramoth-Gilead. And the Syrians wounded Joram.

(2 Kings 8:29)

(2 Kings 9:1) 
Elisha the prophet called one of the disciples of the prophets and said to him, 'Prepare yourself for travel, and take this small jar of oil with you in your hand, then go to Ramoth Gilead.'

(2 Kings 9:2) 
When you arrive there, find Jehu, the son of Jehoshaphat, who is the son of Nimshi. When you find him, take him away from his companions and lead him into a hidden private chamber.

(2 Kings 9:3) 
Then, take the jar of oil and pour it over his head, saying: 'This is what the Lord says: I have anointed you to be king over Israel.' After you have done this, open the door, flee immediately, and do not delay.

(2 Kings 9:4) 
So the young man, the prophet's disciple, went to Ramoth Gilead.

(2 Kings 9:5) 
When he arrived, behold, the commanders of the army were sitting together. He said, 'I have a message for you, commander.'

(2 Kings 9:6) 
Jehu asked, 'Which of us are you speaking to?'
He replied, 'To you, commander.'

(2 Kings 9:7) 
So Jehu got up and went into the private chamber. The young man poured the oil over his head and said to him, 'This is what the Lord, the God of Israel, says: I have anointed you king over the Lord's people, Israel.'

(2 Kings 9:8) 
'You are to strike down the household of Ahab your master, so that I may avenge the blood of My servants, the prophets, and the blood of all the Lord's servants, at the hand of Jezebel.'

(2 Kings 9:9) 
'I will destroy the house of Ahab. I will cut off from Ahab every male, both slave and free, in Israel.'

(2 Kings 9:10) 
'I will make the house of Ahab like the house of Jeroboam, the son of Nebat, and like the house of Baasha, the son of Ahijah.'

(2 Kings 9:11) 
'As for Jezebel, dogs will devour her body in the field of Jezreel, and no one will bury her.'

(2 Kings 9:12) 
Then he opened the door and fled, just as Elisha commanded.

(2 Kings 9:13) 
When Jehu came out to the servants of his master, they asked him, 'Is everything all right? What did that madman want with you?'

(2 Kings 9:14) 
He answered them, 'You know the man and what he said.'

(2 Kings 9:15) 
But they insisted, 'That's not true! Tell us what he said!'
He then told them, 'He said such and such to me, saying: 'This is what the Lord says: I have anointed you king over Israel.''

(2 Kings 9:16) 
They quickly took off their cloaks, and each man spread his own under Jehu's feet, forming an impromptu royal carpet. Then they sounded the trumpet and shouted, 'Jehu is king!'

(2 Kings 9:17) 
So Jehu plotted against Joram. Now Joram, along with all of Israel, was guarding Ramoth Gilead against Hazael, the king of Syria.

(2 Kings 9:18) 
King Joram had returned to Jezreel to recover from the wounds the Arameans had inflicted upon him when he fought against Hazael, the king of Syria.
Jehu then said, 'If you are with me, let no one escape from the city to go and report this news in Jezreel.'

(2 Kings 9:19) 
So Jehu mounted his chariot and rode to Jezreel, for Joram was lying there wounded. Ahaziah, the king of Judah, had also come down to visit Joram.

(2 Kings 9:20) 
Now the watchman was standing on the tower in Jezreel. He saw Jehu approaching with his company and exclaimed, 'I see a chariot approaching!'

(2 Kings 9:21) 
Joram said, 'Harness my chariot!' So they harnessed his chariot, and King Joram of Israel, along with King Ahaziah of Judah, each in their own chariots, went out to meet Jehu. They encountered him in the field of Naboth the Jezreelite.

(2 Kings 9:22) 
When Joram saw Jehu, he asked, 'Is it peace, Jehu?' Jehu replied, 'What peace can there be? The harlotries of your mother Jezebel and her many sorceries are still flourishing!'

(2 Kings 9:23) 
Then Joram turned his chariot around to flee, crying out to Ahaziah, 'Treachery, Ahaziah!'

(2 Kings 9:24) 
But Jehu drew his bow with his own hand and shot Joram between his shoulders. The arrow pierced his heart, and he immediately collapsed in his chariot.

(2 Kings 9:25) 
Jehu then said to Bidkar, his captain, 'Pick him up and throw him into the field of Naboth the Jezreelite. Remember how, when you and I were riding in chariots behind Ahab his father, the Lord pronounced this sentence against him, saying:'

(2 Kings 9:26) 
'Surely I saw the blood of Naboth and the blood of his sons yesterday,' says the Lord, 'and I will repay you in this very field,' says the Lord. 'So now, take him and throw him into the field, according to the word of the Lord.'

(2 Kings 9:27) 
When Ahaziah, the king of Judah, saw this, he fled by the road of the garden house. Jehu pursued him and said, 'Strike him down too, in his chariot!'
They struck him down at the ascent of Gur, which is by Ibleam. He fled to Megiddo and died there.

(2 Kings 9:28) 
His servants carried him in his chariot to Jerusalem and buried him in his tomb with his ancestors in the City of David.

(2 Kings 9:29) 
In the eleventh year of Joram, son of Ahab, Ahaziah began to reign over Judah.

(2 Kings 9:30) 
So Jehu came to Jezreel. When Jezebel heard about his arrival, she painted her eyes with dark makeup, arranged her hair, and looked out a window.

(2 Kings 9:31) 
As Jehu entered the city gate, she called out, 'Is it peace, you Zimri, murderer of your master?'

(2 Kings 9:32) 
Jehu looked up to the window and called out, 'Who is on my side? Who?'
Two or three eunuchs looked out to him.

(2 Kings 9:33) 
He said to them, 'Throw her down!' So they threw her down. Her blood splattered on the wall and on the horses, and she was trampled underfoot.

(2 Kings 9:34) 
After Jehu went in, and had eaten and drunk, he said, 'Go and look after that cursed woman and bury her, for she was a king's daughter.'

(2 Kings 9:35) 
But when they went to bury her, they found nothing but her skull, her feet, and the palms of her hands.

(2 Kings 9:36) 
When they returned and reported this to him, Jehu said, 'This is the word of the Lord, which He spoke through His servant Elijah the Tishbite, saying: 'In the field of Jezreel, dogs will devour the flesh of Jezebel.''

(2 Kings 9:37) 
'The corpse of Jezebel will be like dung on the surface of the ground in the field of Jezreel, so that no one will be able to say: 'This is Jezebel.'' This is her fate.

(2 Kings 9:1) 
Now, Elisha the prophet called one of the young men from the school of the prophets, and said to him, 'Prepare yourself for a journey and take this flask of anointing oil in your hand, and go to Ramoth-Gilead.

(2 Kings 9:2) 
When you get there, find Jehu, the son of Jehoshaphat, the son of Nimshi. Go inside, call to him, and then bring him away from his companions, leading him into an inner room where you can speak with him privately.

(2 Kings 9:3) 
Then take the flask of oil and pour it over his head, saying, 'This is what the Lord declares: I have anointed you king over Israel.' After you have done this, open the door, flee quickly, and do not stay there.

(2 Kings 9:4) 
So the young prophet departed for Ramoth-Gilead.

(2 Kings 9:5) 
When he arrived, behold, the commanders of the army were sitting together. The prophet said, 'I have a message for you, commander.' Jehu asked, 'For which of us, among all of us here?' And he answered, 'For you, commander.'

(2 Kings 9:6) 
So Jehu got up and went into the inner room. The prophet then poured the oil over his head and declared, 'This is what the Lord, the God of Israel, says: I have anointed you king over the people of the Lord, over Israel.

(2 Kings 9:7) 
You are to strike down the house of Ahab, your master. I will avenge the blood of my servants, the prophets, and the blood of all the Lord’s servants who were murdered by Jezebel.'

(2 Kings 9:8) 
Indeed, I will destroy the entire house of Ahab. I will cut off from Ahab every male descendant, both slave and free, in Israel.

(2 Kings 9:9) 
I will make the house of Ahab like the house of Jeroboam, the son of Nebat, and like the house of Baasha, the son of Ahijah.

(2 Kings 9:10) 
And as for Jezebel, dogs will devour her in the territory of Jezreel, and no one will bury her body.

(2 Kings 9:11) 
Then the young prophet opened the door and fled, just as Elisha had commanded him.

(2 Kings 9:12) 
When Jehu came out to his master’s servants, they asked him, 'Is everything well? Why did this madman come to you?' He replied to them, 'You know the man and what he might say.'

(2 Kings 9:13) 
But they insisted, 'No, that is not true; tell us instead!' So he told them, 'He said to me exactly this: 'This is what the Lord declares: I have anointed you king over Israel.''

(2 Kings 9:14) 
Immediately, each of them quickly took off his cloak and spread it under Jehu’s feet, as if making a royal throne. Then they blew the trumpet and proclaimed, 'Jehu is now king!'

(2 Kings 9:15) 
So Jehu, the son of Jehoshaphat, the son of Nimshi, conspired against Joram. Now Joram had been defending Ramoth-Gilead, along with all of Israel, against Hazael, the king of Syria.

(2 Kings 9:16) 
King Joram had returned to Jezreel to recover from the wounds he received from the Syrians while fighting against Hazael, the king of Syria. Jehu then commanded, 'If it is agreeable to you, let no one escape from the city to go and report this news in Jezreel.'

(2 Kings 9:17) 
So Jehu mounted his chariot and headed for Jezreel, because Joram was convalescing there, and Ahaziah, the king of Judah, had come down to visit him.

(2 Kings 9:18) 
Now, the watchman was standing on the tower in Jezreel, and he saw Jehu’s company approaching in their chariots. He called out, 'I see chariots coming!' Joram said, 'Send a horseman to meet them and ask if they come in peace.'

(2 Kings 9:19) 
So a horseman went out to meet him and asked, 'The king asks, 'Do you come in peace?'' Jehu replied, 'What concern is peace to you? Turn around and follow me!' The watchman reported, 'The messenger reached them, but he is not returning.'

(2 Kings 9:20) 
Then Joram sent a second horseman, who came to them and asked, 'The king asks, 'Do you come in peace?'' And Jehu answered, 'What concern is peace to you? Turn around and follow me!'

(2 Kings 9:21) 
The watchman reported again, saying, 'He reached them, but he is not returning. The way the chariot is being driven is like the furious driving of Jehu, the son of Nimshi, for he drives with great speed.'

(2 Kings 9:22) 
Then Joram exclaimed, 'Prepare my chariot!' So they prepared his chariot. King Joram of Israel and King Ahaziah of Judah each went out in their own chariots, and they rode to meet Jehu. They encountered him in the field of Naboth the Jezreelite.

(2 Kings 9:23) 
When Joram saw Jehu, he asked, 'Do you come in peace, Jehu?' He replied, 'How can there be peace, as long as the many immoral acts and sorceries of your mother Jezebel are still thriving?'

(2 Kings 9:24) 
Joram then quickly turned his chariot to flee and shouted to Ahaziah, 'Treachery, Ahaziah! It’s an ambush!'

(2 Kings 9:25) 
But Jehu drew his bow with his full strength and shot Joram between his shoulders. The arrow pierced through his heart, and he immediately collapsed in his chariot.

(2 Kings 9:26) 
Jehu then said to Bidkar, his aide, 'Pick him up and throw him into the field of Naboth the Jezreelite. Remember when you and I were riding together in a chariot behind Ahab, your father? The Lord then laid this prophecy as a burden upon him, saying:'

(2 Kings 9:27) 
'Surely I saw the blood of Naboth and the blood of his sons yesterday, says the Lord, and I will repay you in this very field, says the Lord.' Now therefore, pick him up and throw him into the field, fulfilling the word of the Lord.

(2 Kings 9:28) 
When Ahaziah, the king of Judah, saw this, he fled by way of the garden house. Jehu pursued him and commanded, 'Strike this one down too!' And they struck him down in his chariot on the ascent of Gur, which is by Ibleam. He then escaped to Megiddo and died there.

(2 Kings 9:29) 
His servants took his body in a chariot and brought him to Jerusalem, where they buried him in his tomb with his ancestors in the City of David.

(2 Kings 9:30) 
Jehu then arrived in Jezreel. When Jezebel heard of his arrival, she painted her eyes with kohl, adorned her head, and looked out from a window.

(2 Kings 9:31) 
As Jehu entered the city gate, Jezebel called out, 'Is it peace, you Zimri, murderer of your master?' —comparing him to a previous king who assassinated his lord.

(2 Kings 9:32) 
Jehu looked up to the window and called out, 'Who is on my side? Who?' And two or three eunuchs looked down at him.

(2 Kings 9:33) 
He said to them, 'Throw her down!' So they threw her down. Her blood splattered on the wall and on the horses, and her body was trampled underfoot.

(2 Kings 9:34) 
Then Jehu went inside, ate, and drank. Afterward, he commanded, 'Go now and see to that cursed woman, and bury her, for after all, she was a king’s daughter.'

(2 Kings 9:35) 
But when they went to bury her, they found nothing but her skull, her feet, and the palms of her hands.

(2 Kings 9:36) 
So they returned and reported this to him. Jehu then declared, 'This is the word of the Lord, which He spoke through His servant Elijah the Tishbite, saying: 'In the territory of Jezreel, dogs will devour the flesh of Jezebel.'

(2 Kings 9:37) 
And the corpse of Jezebel will be like dung on the surface of the ground in the territory of Jezreel, so that no one will be able to identify her and say, 'This was Jezebel.'

"And I will make the house of Ahab like the house of Jeroboam, the son of Nebat, and like the house of Baasha, the son of Ahijah."

(2 Kings 9:10) 
"As for Jezebel, dogs will eat her flesh in the field of Jezreel, and no one will bury her." Then the prophet opened the door and fled.

(2 Kings 9:11) 
Jehu then went out to the servants of his master. They asked him, "Is everything alright? Why did that madman come to you?" He replied to them, "You know the man and what he said."

(2 Kings 9:12) 
But they insisted, "That's not true! Tell us what he really said!" So he told them, "He said to me such and such, and then he declared, 'This is what the Lord says: I have anointed you king over Israel.'"

(2 Kings 9:13) 
So they immediately rushed, and each man took his cloak, spread it under Jehu's feet like a royal carpet, and sounded the trumpet, proclaiming, "Jehu is king!"

(2 Kings 9:14) 
Thus, Jehu, the son of Jehoshaphat, the son of Nimshi, conspired against Joram. (Now, Joram had been defending Ramoth-Gilead, along with all of Israel, against Hazael, the king of Syria.)

(2 Kings 9:15) 
King Joram had returned to Jezreel to recover from the wounds he had received from the Syrians while fighting against Hazael, the king of Syria. Jehu then said, "If you agree with my plan, let no one escape from the city to go and report this news in Jezreel."

(2 Kings 9:16) 
Jehu then mounted his chariot and went to Jezreel, for Joram was recovering there, and Ahaziah, the king of Judah, had come down to visit Joram.

(2 Kings 9:17) 
The lookout who was standing on the watchtower in Jezreel saw Jehu's chariot approaching and reported, "I see a chariot coming!" Joram said, "It's still far off. Send a messenger to meet him and ask: 'Is all well?'"

(2 Kings 9:18) 
So the messenger went to meet him and said, "The king asks: 'Is all well?'" Jehu replied, "What concern is peace to you? Turn around and follow me!" The lookout reported again, saying, "The messenger reached them, but he is not returning."

(2 Kings 9:19) 
Joram then sent a second chariot with horses, and this messenger also reached them and asked, "The king asks: 'Is all well?'" Jehu again replied, "What concern is peace to you? Turn around and follow me!"

(2 Kings 9:20) 
The lookout reported again, saying, "He reached them and is not returning. The driving is like the driving of Jehu, the son of Nimshi, for he drives furiously."

(2 Kings 9:21) 
Joram said, "Harness my chariot!" So they harnessed his chariot, and King Joram of Israel and King Ahaziah of Judah each went out in their own chariots. They rode to meet Jehu and found him in the field of Naboth the Jezreelite.

(2 Kings 9:22) 
When Joram saw Jehu, he asked, "Is all well, Jehu?" But Jehu responded, "How can there be peace, as long as the many idolatries and sorceries of your mother Jezebel continue to thrive?"

(2 Kings 9:23) 
Joram immediately turned his chariot around and fled, shouting to Ahaziah, "Treason, Ahaziah!"

(2 Kings 9:24) 
Then Jehu drew his bow with his full strength and shot Joram between his shoulders. The arrow pierced his heart, and he immediately collapsed in his chariot.

(2 Kings 9:25) 
Jehu then said to Bidkar, his officer, "Pick him up and throw him into the field of Naboth the Jezreelite. Remember when you and I were riding together in a chariot behind Ahab, this man's father, that the Lord laid this burden upon him, saying:"

(2 Kings 9:26) 
"'Surely I saw the blood of Naboth and the blood of his sons yesterday, says the Lord, and I will repay you in this very field.' Therefore, pick him up now and throw him into the field, according to the word of the Lord."

(2 Kings 9:27) 
King Ahaziah of Judah, seeing this, fled by way of the garden house. But Jehu pursued him and commanded, "Strike him down also in his chariot!" So they struck him down on the ascent of Gur, which is by Ibleam. He managed to flee to Megiddo, but he died there.

(2 Kings 9:28) 
His servants then placed him in his own chariot and brought him to Jerusalem, where they buried him in his tomb with his fathers in the City of David.

(2 Kings 9:29) 
In the eleventh year of Joram, son of Ahab, Ahaziah began his reign over Judah.

(2 Kings 9:30) 
Jehu then arrived in Jezreel. When Jezebel heard of his coming, she put on her eye makeup, adorned her head, and looked out of the window.

(2 Kings 9:31) 
As Jehu entered through the gate, she called out, "Is it peace, you Zimri, who murdered his master?"

(2 Kings 9:32) 
Jehu then looked up toward the window and asked, "Who is on my side? Who?" Two or three eunuchs looked out at him.

(2 Kings 9:33) 
He commanded them, "Throw her down!" So they threw her down. Her blood splattered on the wall and on the horses, and she was trampled underfoot.

(2 Kings 9:34) 
Jehu then went inside to eat and drink. Afterward, he said, "Go, inspect the body of that cursed woman and bury her, because after all, she was a king's daughter."

(2 Kings 9:35) 
But when they went to bury her, they found nothing but her skull, her feet, and the palms of her hands.

(2 Kings 9:36) 
They returned and reported this to him. Jehu said, "This is the word of the Lord, which He spoke through His servant Elijah the Tishbite, saying: 'In the field of Jezreel, dogs will eat the flesh of Jezebel.'"

(2 Kings 9:37) 
"And the corpse of Jezebel will be like dung on the surface of the ground in the field of Jezreel, so that those who pass by will say, 'Is this really that Jezebel?'"

(2 Kings 9:1) 
Elisha the prophet called one of the prophets' disciples and said to him, 'Prepare yourself for travel, take this flask of anointing oil in your hand, and go to Ramoth-Gilead.'

(2 Kings 9:2) 
When you arrive there, look for Jehu, the son of Jehoshaphat, the grandson of Nimshi. Go in, close the door of the room securely, take him aside from his companions, and lead him into a private, inner room.

(2 Kings 9:3) 
Then take the flask of anointing oil and pour it over his head, saying, 'The Lord declares this: I have anointed you as king over Israel.' After you have done this, open the door, flee immediately, and do not wait there for anything.

(2 Kings 9:4) 
So the young man, the prophet's servant, went to Ramoth-Gilead.

(2 Kings 9:5) 
He entered the room where the army commanders were gathered. Jehu was sitting among his fellow officers. The young man said, 'I have a message for you, commander.'

(2 Kings 9:6) 
Jehu asked, 'For which one of us?' The young man replied, 'For you, commander.'

(2 Kings 9:7) 
Jehu stood up and went into the private room. There, the young prophet poured the oil over his head and declared, 'This is what the Lord God of Israel says: I have anointed you as king over the Lord's people, over Israel.'

(2 Kings 9:8) 
You must strike down the household of Ahab your master. Through your hand, I will avenge the blood of My servants, the prophets, and the blood of all the Lord's servants, against Jezebel.

(2 Kings 9:9) 
I will utterly destroy the entire household of Ahab. I will cut off from Ahab every male, both slave and free, in Israel.

(2 Kings 9:10) 
I will make the household of Ahab like the household of Jeroboam, the son of Nebat, and like the household of Baasha, the son of Ahijah.

(2 Kings 9:11) 
And as for Jezebel, dogs will devour her in the field of Jezreel, and there will be no one to bury her.' After saying this, the young prophet opened the door and fled.

(2 Kings 9:12) 
When Jehu returned to his master's officers, they asked him, 'Is everything alright? Why did that madman come to you?'

(2 Kings 9:13) 
He replied to them, 'You know the man, and you know what he said.'

(2 Kings 9:14) 
But they said, 'Don't lie to us; tell us honestly.' So he told them, 'He said such and such to me, saying: "The Lord declares this: I have anointed you as king over Israel."'

(2 Kings 9:15) 
They quickly took each man's cloak and laid it beneath Jehu, like a royal carpet on a raised platform. Then they blew the trumpet and proclaimed, 'Jehu is king!'

(2 Kings 9:16) 
So Jehu plotted against Joram, Ahab's son, who was in Jezreel. Joram, along with all Israel, had been defending Ramoth-Gilead.

(2 Kings 9:17) 
Joram had returned to Jezreel to recover from wounds inflicted by the Arameans when he fought against Hazael, the king of Aram. Jehu declared, 'If you are in agreement with me, let no one escape from the city to go and report this news in Jezreel.'

(2 Kings 9:18) 
Then Jehu mounted his chariot and rode to Jezreel, where King Joram was recuperating. Ahaziah, king of Judah, had also come down to visit Joram.

(2 Kings 9:19) 
A watchman standing on the tower in Jezreel saw Jehu approaching with his company of men and exclaimed, 'I see a chariot approaching!' Joram said, 'Send a rider on horseback to meet them and ask, "Is it peace?"'

(2 Kings 9:20) 
So a horseman rode out to meet him and asked, 'The king asks, "Is it peace?"' Jehu replied, 'What concern is peace to you? Turn around and follow me!' The watchman reported again, saying, 'The messenger reached them, but he is not returning.'

(2 Kings 9:21) 
So Joram sent out a second horseman. When he reached them, he asked, 'The king asks, "Is it peace?"' Jehu replied, 'What concern is peace to you? Turn around and follow me!'

(2 Kings 9:22) 
The watchman reported, 'He reached them as well, but he is not returning. And the driving is like the driving of Jehu, son of Nimshi—he drives like a madman.'

(2 Kings 9:23) 
Joram then commanded, 'Harness my chariot!' So they harnessed his chariot. King Joram of Israel and King Ahaziah of Judah each went out in their own chariots, riding to meet Jehu. They encountered him in the field that belonged to Naboth of Jezreel.

(2 Kings 9:24) 
When Joram saw Jehu, he asked, 'Is it peace, Jehu?' Jehu replied, 'What peace can there be, as long as the harlotries of your mother Jezebel and her many sorceries are still flourishing?'

(2 Kings 9:25) 
Joram immediately turned his chariot to flee and cried out to Ahaziah, 'Treachery, Ahaziah!'

(2 Kings 9:26) 
But Jehu drew his bow with his full strength and struck Joram between his shoulders. The arrow pierced through his heart, and he collapsed instantly in his chariot.

(2 Kings 9:27) 
Then Jehu ordered Bidkar, his officer, 'Pick him up and throw him into the field of Naboth the Jezreelite. Remember when you and I were riding in chariots behind Ahab, this man's father, how the Lord laid this burden upon him, saying:'

(2 Kings 9:28) 
'"Surely I have seen the blood of Naboth and the blood of his sons, which was shed yesterday," declares the Lord. "And I will repay you in this very field," declares the Lord. Now, therefore, pick him up and throw him into the field, according to the word of the Lord.'

(2 Kings 9:29) 
King Ahaziah of Judah saw what happened and fled by way of the garden house. Jehu pursued him and commanded, 'Strike him down in his chariot too!' So they struck him at the ascent of Gur, which is by Ibleam. He managed to escape to Megiddo, but he died there.

(2 Kings 9:30) 
His servants carried him in a chariot to Jerusalem and buried him in his tomb with his ancestors in the City of David.

(2 Kings 9:31) 
When Jehu arrived in Jezreel, Jezebel heard about his coming. She painted her eyelids with kohl, adorned her head with jewels, and looked out from a window.

(2 Kings 9:32) 
As Jehu entered the gate, she called out, 'Is it peace, you Zimri, murderer of your master?'

(2 Kings 9:33) 
Jehu looked up toward the window and asked, 'Who is on my side? Who?' Two or three eunuchs looked out at him.

(2 Kings 9:34) 
He commanded them, 'Throw her down!' So they threw her down. Some of her blood splattered on the wall and on the horses' hooves, and Jehu's chariot trampled over her.

(2 Kings 9:35) 
Then Jehu went inside, ate and drank. Afterward, he said, 'Go and see to that accursed woman's corpse and bury her, for she was a king's daughter.'

(2 Kings 9:36) 
But when they went to bury her, they found nothing but her skull, her feet, and the palms of her hands.

(2 Kings 9:37) 
When they returned and reported this to Jehu, he said, 'This is the word of the Lord, which He spoke through His servant Elijah the Tishbite, saying: "In the field of Jezreel, dogs will devour Jezebel's flesh."

(2 Kings 9:38) 
And the corpse of Jezebel will be like dung on the surface of the ground in the field of Jezreel, so that those passing by will say: "Is this truly that Jezebel?"'

(2 Kings 9:39) 
For Jezebel will not be in the earth, nor will there be a place where she can be buried. Instead, her remains will be scattered in the plain of Jezreel like dung on the surface of the ground, so completely that no one will be able to recognize her remains.

(2 Kings 9:40) 
Thus, the corpse of Jezebel will be like dung on the surface of the ground in the field of Jezreel, so that those passing by will say: 'Is this truly that Jezebel?' For she will not be in the earth, nor will there be a place where Jezebel can be buried. Instead, her remains will be scattered in the plain of Jezreel like dung on the surface of the ground, so completely that no one will be able to recognize her remains.

(2 Kings 10:1) 
Now King Ahab had seventy sons living in Samaria. So Jehu wrote letters and dispatched them to Samaria, addressing them to the city's officials, its elders, and those who were responsible for raising Ahab's sons, with this message:

(2 Kings 10:2) 
"Since your lord's sons are with you, and you have chariots, horses, a fortified city, and weapons,

(2 Kings 10:3) 
choose the best and most capable among your lord's sons, and place him on his father's throne. Then, fight for the family and household of your lord."

(2 Kings 10:4) 
But the officials were terrified, and they said: "Look, two kings—King Joram and King Ahaziah—could not stand against him. How then can we possibly resist him?"

(2 Kings 10:5) 
So the royal steward, the city governor, the elders, and the guardians of the sons sent a message back to Jehu, saying: "We are your servants, and we will do whatever you command us. We will not make anyone king. Do whatever you deem best."

(2 Kings 10:6) 
Then Jehu wrote to them a second time, saying: "If you are truly on my side and will obey me, then cut off the heads of your lord's sons, and come to meet me in Jezreel by this time tomorrow." Now, the king's seventy sons were living with the city's leading men, who were raising them.

(2 Kings 10:7) 
When the letters reached them, they seized the king's sons and killed all seventy men. Then they placed their heads in baskets and sent them to Jehu in Jezreel.

(2 Kings 10:8) 
Then a messenger arrived and reported to Jehu, saying: "They have brought the heads of the king's sons." Jehu responded: "Arrange them in two piles at the entrance of the city gate, and leave them there until morning."

(2 Kings 10:9) 
When Jehu went out the next morning, he stood before the people and declared: "You are innocent in this matter. Indeed, I conspired against my lord and killed him; that is my responsibility. But who is responsible for slaying all these seventy men?"

(2 Kings 10:10) 
Know therefore that not a single word spoken by the Lord against the house of Ahab has failed to come true. The Lord has accomplished what He declared through His servant Elijah."

(2 Kings 10:11) 
So Jehu struck down all who remained of Ahab's family and household in Jezreel, including all his leading men, his relatives, and his priests, until there was not a single person left from Ahab's line.

(2 Kings 10:12) 
Then Jehu rose up and departed, traveling to Samaria. As he came to the Shepherds' House on the way,

(2 Kings 10:13) 
he encountered the relatives of King Ahaziah of Judah and asked them: "Who are you?" They replied: "We are relatives of Ahaziah, and we have come down to greet the sons of the king and the sons of the queen."

(2 Kings 10:14) 
Jehu seized them and slaughtered forty-two men by the pit near the Shepherds' House, leaving not a single one alive.

(2 Kings 10:15) 
When Jehu departed from there, he met Jehonadab son of Rechab. After greeting him, Jehu asked: "Is your heart as loyal to me as my heart is loyal to you and God's purpose?" Jehonadab answered: "It is." Then Jehu said: "If so, give me your hand." Jehonadab extended his hand, and Jehu pulled him up into his chariot.

(2 Kings 10:16) 
Jehu then said to him: "Come with me, and witness my zeal for the Lord." So Jehu brought him into his chariot.

(2 Kings 10:17) 
Upon entering Samaria, Jehu struck down all who remained of Ahab's family and household in that city, utterly destroying them, in fulfillment of the Lord's word spoken to Elijah.

(2 Kings 10:18) 
Then Jehu gathered all the people and declared to them: "Ahab served Baal only a little, but I will serve him much more diligently."

(2 Kings 10:19) 
Therefore, summon all the prophets of Baal, all his servants, and all his priests to me now. Let no one fail to come, for I am offering a great sacrifice to Baal. Whoever is absent will not live." Jehu was doing this with cunning intent, aiming to utterly destroy the worshippers of Baal.

(2 Kings 10:20) 
And Jehu commanded: "Proclaim a solemn assembly for Baal!" So it was proclaimed throughout the land.

(2 Kings 10:21) 
Jehu also sent messengers throughout all Israel, and all the servants of Baal came. Not a single one remained who did not come. They entered the temple of Baal, and the temple of Baal was filled from one end to the other.

(2 Kings 10:22) 
Then Jehu said to the one in charge of the vestments: "Bring out the robes for all the servants of Baal." So the official brought out the robes for them.

(2 Kings 10:23) 
When Jehu and Jehonadab son of Rechab entered the temple of Baal, Jehu said to the Baal worshippers: "Look carefully and make sure there is no servant of the Lord among you, but only servants of Baal."

(2 Kings 10:24) 
Then the Baal worshippers proceeded to offer sacrifices and burnt offerings. Meanwhile, Jehu had stationed eighty men outside, warning them: "If any of the men whom I bring into your hands should escape, then your own life will be taken in exchange for his life."

(2 Kings 10:25) 
As soon as Jehu had finished offering the burnt offering, he commanded his guards and officers: "Go in and strike them down! Let no one escape!" So the guards and officers struck them with the edge of the sword. Then they cast out the bodies and proceeded to the inner sanctuary of the temple of Baal.

(2 Kings 10:26) 
They brought out the sacred pillar of Baal from the temple of Baal and burned it.

(2 Kings 10:27) 
They also broke down the sacred pillar of Baal and completely tore down the temple of Baal. They turned it into a public latrine, and it remains so to this very day.

(2 Kings 10:28) 
Thus Jehu utterly eradicated Baal worship from Israel.

(2 Kings 10:29) 
However, Jehu did not turn away from the sins of Jeroboam son of Nebat, who had caused Israel to sin, specifically from worshipping the golden calves that were in Bethel and Dan.

(2 Kings 10:30) 
Therefore, the Lord said to Jehu: "Because you have diligently carried out what was right and pleasing in My sight, and you have done everything I intended against the house of Ahab, your sons will sit on the throne of Israel for four generations."

(2 Kings 10:31) 
Yet Jehu himself was not careful to walk in the Law of the Lord, the God of Israel, with his whole heart; for he did not turn away from the sins of Jeroboam, who had caused Israel to sin.

(2 Kings 10:32) 
In those days, the Lord began to diminish Israel. King Hazael of Aram struck them throughout all the territories of Israel,

(2 Kings 10:33) 
including all the land beyond the Jordan River—Gilead, Gad, Reuben, and Manasseh—from Aroer, which is by the Arnon Valley, including Gilead and Bashan.

(2 Kings 10:34) 
Now, the rest of the acts of Jehu, all that he accomplished, and all his might, are these not recorded in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?

(2 Kings 10:35) 
Then Jehu rested with his ancestors, and they buried him in Samaria. His son Jehoahaz succeeded him as king.

(2 Kings 10:36) 
The length of Jehu's reign over Israel in Samaria was twenty-eight years.

(2 Kings 10:39)
