(2 Kings 10:1) 
Now, Ahab had seventy sons living in Samaria. So Jehu wrote letters and sent them into Samaria, to the city's most important officials, to its elders, and to those who had cared for Ahab's children since their youth, saying this:

(2 Kings 10:2) 
“As soon as you receive this letter—you who are responsible for your lord's sons, who have chariots and horses, who control fortified cities and weapons—

(2 Kings 10:3) 
choose the best and most capable among your lord's sons. Then put him on his father's throne and fight for the dynasty of your lord.”

(2 Kings 10:4) 
But they were terrified and said, “Look, two kings couldn't stand against him—referring to Jehu—so how can we possibly resist Jehu ourselves?”

(2 Kings 10:5) 
So the official in charge of the palace, along with the city's chief officials, the elders, and the guardians of Ahab's sons, sent this message back to Jehu: “We are your servants. Whatever you command, we will do. We will not set up anyone as king. You may do whatever you think is right.”

(2 Kings 10:6) 
Jehu then wrote a second letter to them, saying: “If you truly are loyal to me and are ready to obey me, then take the heads of your lord's sons and come to me in Jezreel by this time tomorrow.” Now, the king's seventy sons were living with the most important officials of the city, who were raising them.

(2 Kings 10:7) 
When the officials received Jehu's letter, they seized the king's seventy sons and slaughtered every one of them. Then they put their heads in baskets and sent them to Jehu in Jezreel.

(2 Kings 10:8) 
When a messenger came and reported to Jehu, saying, “They have brought the heads of the king's sons,” Jehu replied, “Pile them in two heaps by the entrance of the city gate, and leave them there until morning.”

(2 Kings 10:9) 
In the morning, Jehu went out, stood before all the people, and declared: “Understand this now: None of you are guilty of this conspiracy to kill Joram, the son of Ahab; however, know that nothing of all the Lord's words spoken against the dynasty of Ahab has failed to come to pass. The Lord has truly done what he promised through his servant Elijah.”

(2 Kings 10:10) 
So then Jehu struck down all those who remained of Ahab's dynasty in Jezreel, along with all of Ahab's chief officials, his close associates, and his priests, until not a single person remained from his family line.

(2 Kings 10:11) 
Then Jehu got up and traveled to Samaria. On the way, when he reached a shepherd's hut,

(2 Kings 10:12) 
he found the relatives of Ahaziah, king of Judah. He asked them, “Who are you?” They answered, “We are the relatives of King Ahaziah, and we are on our way to greet the sons of the king and the sons of the queen.”

(2 Kings 10:13) 
Jehu ordered, “Seize them alive!” And when they had seized them alive, he had them slaughtered by the roadside well—all forty-two men. He did not leave a single one of them alive.

(2 Kings 10:14) 
When Jehu left that place, he met Jehonadab son of Rechab, who was coming to meet him. Jehu greeted him and said, “Is your heart as true to me as my heart is to yours?” Jehonadab answered, “It is.” Jehu then said, “If it is, give me your hand.” So Jehonadab gave him his hand, and Jehu pulled him up into his chariot with him.

(2 Kings 10:15) 
Then Jehu said to him, “Come with me and see my zeal for the Lord.” And he took Jehonadab into his chariot.

(2 Kings 10:16) 
When Jehu arrived in Samaria, he struck down everyone who remained from Ahab's dynasty in Samaria, until he had completely annihilated them. This was in accordance with the word of the Lord that he had spoken to Elijah.

(2 Kings 10:17) 
Then Jehu gathered all the people and said to them, “Ahab served Baal a little, but I will serve him much more.”

(2 Kings 10:18) 
“Therefore, summon all the prophets of Baal, all his servants, and all his priests to me now. Let no one fail to come, for I am offering a great sacrifice to Baal. Anyone who is absent will not live.” Jehu was doing this with a cunning plan in mind, intending to utterly destroy the worshippers of Baal.

(2 Kings 10:19) 
And Jehu said, “Consecrate a solemn assembly for Baal!” So they proclaimed it.

(2 Kings 10:20) 
Jehu sent messengers throughout all Israel, and all the servants of Baal came; not one remained who did not come. They entered the temple of Baal, and the temple of Baal was filled from one end to the other.

(2 Kings 10:21) 
Then Jehu said to the attendant who was in charge of the robes, “Bring out vestments for all the worshippers of Baal.” So he brought out vestments for them.

(2 Kings 10:22) 
Jehu, along with Jehonadab son of Rechab, entered the temple of Baal. Jehu said to the worshippers of Baal, “Search carefully and make sure there is no servant of the Lord among you, but only worshippers of Baal.”

(2 Kings 10:23) 
Then they proceeded to offer sacrifices and burnt offerings. Now, Jehu had stationed eighty men outside, saying to them, “If any of these men whom I bring into your hands escape, then the life of that guard will pay for the life of the one who escaped.”

(2 Kings 10:24) 
As soon as the burnt offering was completed, Jehu commanded his guards and officers, “Go in and strike them down! Let no one escape!” So the guards and officers struck them down with the edge of the sword. They threw their bodies out and went into the inner sanctuary of the temple of Baal.

(2 Kings 10:25) 
They brought out the sacred pillar, or idol, from the temple of Baal and burned it.

(2 Kings 10:26) 
They then broke down the sacred pillar of Baal and tore down the temple of Baal itself. They turned it into a latrine, which it remains to this very day.

(2 Kings 10:27) 
Thus, Jehu eradicated Baal worship from Israel.

(2 Kings 10:28) 
Nevertheless, Jehu did not turn away from the sins of Jeroboam son of Nebat, who caused Israel to sin—namely, the worship of the golden calves that were in Bethel and Dan.

(2 Kings 10:29) 
Therefore, the Lord said to Jehu, “Because you have zealously carried out what was right in my sight, and have accomplished all that was in my heart concerning the dynasty of Ahab, your sons will sit on the throne of Israel for four generations.”

(2 Kings 10:30) 
However, Jehu himself did not carefully walk in the Law of the Lord, the God of Israel, with all his heart. For he did not turn away from the sins of Jeroboam, who caused Israel to sin.

(2 Kings 10:31) 
In those days, the Lord began to cut off parts of Israel. King Hazael of Aram struck them throughout all the territory of Israel,

(2 Kings 10:32) 
starting from the Jordan River eastward, encompassing all the land of Gilead—the territories of Gad, Reuben, and Manasseh—from Aroer, which is by the Arnon Valley, including Gilead and Bashan.

(2 Kings 10:33) 
Now, the rest of the acts of Jehu, all that he did, and all his might, are they not written in the Book of the Annals of the Kings of Israel?

(2 Kings 10:34) 
So Jehu rested with his ancestors, and they buried him in Samaria. Then his son Jehoahaz became king in his place.

(2 Kings 10:35) 
Jehu reigned over Israel in Samaria for twenty-eight years.

(2 Kings 10:36) 
As for the rest of the acts of Jehoahaz, and all that he did, and his might, are they not written in the Book of the Annals of the Kings of Israel?

(2 Kings 10:37) 
Jehoahaz rested with his ancestors, and they buried him in Samaria. Then his son Joash became king in his place, during the seventeenth year of the reign of King Joash of Judah.

(2 Kings 10:38) 
Amasias was twenty-five years old when he began to reign, and he reigned twenty-nine years in Jerusalem. His mother's name was Jehoaddin, from Jerusalem.

(2 Kings 10:39) 
He did what was right in the sight of the Lord, though not with the complete devotion of his ancestor David. He followed the example of all that his father Joash had done.

(2 Kings 10:40) 
However, he did not remove the high places—the pagan altars—so the people still offered sacrifices and burned incense there. In those days, Amaziah sent messengers to King Joash son of Jehoahaz, son of Jehu, king of Israel, saying, “Come, let us meet face to face in battle.”

(2 Kings 10:1) 
Now, Ahab had seventy sons in Samaria. So Jehu wrote letters and sent them into Samaria to the chief men of the city, to the elders, and to those who had been responsible for raising Ahab’s children. This is what he said:

(2 Kings 10:2) 
"As soon as you receive these letters—you who have the sons of your lord, and chariots, and horses, and cities, and weapons—choose the best and most pleasing of your lord’s sons. Then put him on his father’s throne and fight for your lord’s family."

(2 Kings 10:3) 
But they were terrified, and they said: "Look, two kings were not able to stand against him, so how can we resist?"

(2 Kings 10:4) 
Therefore, Jehu had already sent people to take charge of the household and the sons of Ahab. Indeed, Jehu himself had already killed all the chief men, all the elders, and those who had been responsible for raising Ahab’s children in Samaria.

(2 Kings 10:5) 
But then Jehu sent a second set of letters to them, saying: "If you are with me and obey me, then take the heads of Ahab’s sons and come to me tomorrow at this time in Jezreel." (The king’s seventy sons were living with the chief men of the city, who were raising them.)

(2 Kings 10:6) 
When these letters reached them, they seized the king’s sons and killed all seventy men. Then they put their heads in baskets and sent them to Jehu in Jezreel.

(2 Kings 10:7) 
A messenger came and reported to Jehu, saying: "They have brought the heads of the king’s sons." Jehu replied: "Make them into two piles at the entrance of the city gate, and leave them there until morning."

(2 Kings 10:8) 
When morning came, Jehu went out and stood on the steps near the city gate. He said to all the people there: "You yourselves are innocent in this matter. Look, I conspired against my lord and killed him. But who then murdered all of these men?"

(2 Kings 10:9) 
"Understand now that not one word spoken by the Lord against Ahab’s house has fallen to the ground without being fulfilled. The Lord has done what He spoke through His servant Elijah."

(2 Kings 10:10) 
So Jehu then killed all those who remained of Ahab’s family in Jezreel—all of his chief men, his close acquaintances, and his priests—until he left not a single one alive.

(2 Kings 10:11) 
And Jehu rose up and left, going toward Samaria. When he came to the shepherd’s house on the road,

(2 Kings 10:12) 
He found the relatives of Ahaziah, the king of Judah, there and asked them: "Who are you?" They replied: "We are Ahaziah’s relatives, and we have come down to greet the sons of the king and the sons of the queen."

(2 Kings 10:13) 
Jehu said: "Capture them alive!" So, when they had captured them alive, they slaughtered them—forty-two men—by the well near the house. Not a single one of them was left alive.

(2 Kings 10:14) 
When Jehu had gone from there, he met Jehonadab, the son of Rechab, who was coming to meet him. Jehu greeted him and said to him: "Is your heart as true to mine as my heart is to yours?" Jehonadab replied: "It is true, indeed! If it is, then give me your hand." So Jehu gave him his hand, and Jehu lifted him up into his chariot.

(2 Kings 10:15) 
And Jehu said to him: "Come with me, and see my zeal for the Lord." So he had Jehonadab sit in his chariot with him.

(2 Kings 10:16) 
When Jehu arrived in Samaria, he killed all who remained of Ahab’s family in Samaria, until not one was left. This was according to the word of the Lord which He had spoken to Elijah.

(2 Kings 10:17) 
Then Jehu took a priest of Baal and said to them: "Summon all the servants of Baal for me—all of his priests and all of his prophets. No one is to be absent, for I am offering a great sacrifice to Baal. Whoever fails to come will not live." Jehu was doing this cunningly, intending to destroy the worshippers of Baal.

(2 Kings 10:18) 
And Jehu announced this throughout all Samaria.

(2 Kings 10:19) 
And Jehu announced throughout all Israel, saying: "Consecrate a solemn day for Baal!" He proclaimed it, and all the servants of Baal gathered together. Not a single one remained who did not come.

(2 Kings 10:20) 
And they entered the temple of Baal, and the temple of Baal was filled from one end to the other.

(2 Kings 10:21) 
And Jehu said to those who were in charge of the vestments: "Bring out robes for all the servants of Baal." So they brought out the robes for them.

(2 Kings 10:22) 
Then Jehu, along with Jehonadab, the son of Rechab, entered the temple of Baal. He said to the worshippers of Baal: "Search carefully and make sure that none of the Lord’s servants are among you, but only the servants of Baal."

(2 Kings 10:23) 
And they went in to offer sacrifices and burnt offerings. But Jehu had placed one hundred men outside, telling them: "Whoever allows any of the men whom I deliver into your hands to escape, his life will pay for that man’s life."

(2 Kings 10:24) 
And it came to pass that when the offering of the burnt offering was completed, Jehu commanded his guards and his commanders: "Go in and strike them down! Let no one escape!" So they struck them down with the edge of the sword, threw out their bodies, and then went into the inner city of the temple of Baal.

(2 Kings 10:25) 
And they brought out the statue from the temple of Baal and burned it.

(2 Kings 10:26) 
And they smashed the statue of Baal into pieces and utterly destroyed its temple, turning it into latrines, right up to the present day.

(2 Kings 10:27) 
So Jehu completely eradicated Baal worship from Israel.

(2 Kings 10:28) 
Nevertheless, Jehu did not turn away from the sins of Jeroboam, the son of Nebat, who had caused Israel to sin. He did not abandon the golden calves that were in Bethel and Dan.

(2 Kings 10:29) 
And the Lord said to Jehu: "Because you have diligently done what was right and pleasing in My eyes, and have carried out everything that was in My heart against the house of Ahab, your sons will sit upon the throne of Israel for four generations."

(2 Kings 10:30) 
However, Jehu did not carefully observe walking in the law of the Lord God of Israel with all his heart. For he did not turn away from the sins of Jeroboam, who had caused Israel to sin.

(2 Kings 10:31) 
In those days, the Lord began to be disgusted with Israel. He allowed Hazael to strike them in all the territories of Israel,

(2 Kings 10:32) 
From the Jordan River eastward, he struck all the land of Gilead, and Gad, and Reuben, and Manasseh—from Aroer, which is by the torrent of Arnon, including Gilead, and Bashan.

(2 Kings 10:33) 
Now, the rest of the acts of Jehu, and all that he did, and his mighty deeds—are these not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?

(2 Kings 10:34) 
So Jehu rested with his forefathers, and they buried him in Samaria. And his son Jehoahaz reigned in his place.

(2 Kings 10:35) 
Now, the days that Jehu reigned over Israel were twenty-eight years in Samaria.

(2 Kings 10:36) 
And Jehu rested with his forefathers, and they buried him in Samaria. And his son Jehoahaz reigned in his place.

(2 Kings 11:1) 
Athalia, the mother of Ochozias, saw that her son was dead. She then rose up and ordered the killing of all the royal offspring.

(2 Kings 11:2) 
However, Iosaba, daughter of King Ioram and sister of Ochozias, took Ioas, the son of Ochozias. She secretly removed him from among the king’s sons who were being slaughtered. She gave him to his nurse in the treasury chamber, and they hid him from Athalia to prevent his murder.

(2 Kings 11:3) 
Ioas was hidden with her in the Temple of the Lord for six years. During this time, Athalia reigned over the land.

(2 Kings 11:4) 
In the seventh year, Ioiada sent for the centurions and soldiers, bringing them to him in the Temple of the Lord. He made a solemn covenant with them, imposing an oath on them in the Temple of the Lord, and then revealed the king’s son to them.

(2 Kings 11:5) 
He commanded them, saying: “This is the instruction you must follow: A third of you are to enter on the Sabbath and guard the royal palace.”

(2 Kings 11:6) 
“A third of you will stand guard at the Sur Gate. And a third of you will be at the gate beyond the armor-bearers’ chariots. You are to maintain watch over the palace and prevent any attack.”

(2 Kings 11:7) 
“The other two parts of your company, all those whose Sabbath shift is ending, are to guard the Temple of the Lord around the king.”

(2 Kings 11:8) 
“You are to surround him, with your weapons in your hands. If anyone enters the Temple precincts without permission, they are to be killed. You will be with the king both when he enters and when he leaves.”

(2 Kings 11:9) 
The centurions carried out all that Ioiada the priest had commanded them. Each one gathered his men—those whose Sabbath shift was beginning and those whose shift was ending—and they came to Ioiada the priest.

(2 Kings 11:10) 
The priest then gave them the weapons and shields of King David, which had been stored in the Temple of the Lord.

(2 Kings 11:11) 
Each man stood with his weapons in hand, forming a line from the right side of the Temple to the left side of the altar and the Temple itself, surrounding the king.

(2 Kings 11:12) 
Ioiada brought out the king’s son and placed the royal crown upon him, along with a copy of the Law to signify his covenant with God. They made him king and anointed him. Then, clapping their hands, they shouted: “Long live the king!”

(2 Kings 11:13) 
Athalia, meanwhile, heard the sound of the people running and praising the new king. She went to the people in the Temple of the Lord.

(2 Kings 11:14) 
She saw the king standing on the royal platform, as was customary, with the singers and trumpeters near him, and all the people of the land rejoicing and blowing trumpets. She tore her garments and cried out: “Conspiracy! Conspiracy!”

(2 Kings 11:15) 
But Ioiada the priest commanded the centurions and those in charge of the army, saying: “Lead her outside the Temple precincts. Anyone who follows her is to be killed by the sword.” The priest had given this order because he said: “She must not be killed in the Temple of the Lord.”

(2 Kings 11:16) 
So they seized her, and when she reached the path of the Horse Gate, near the royal palace, they killed her there.

(2 Kings 11:17) 
Ioiada then made a covenant between the Lord and the king and the people, establishing that they would be the Lord’s people. He also made a covenant between the king and the people, defining their mutual obligations.

(2 Kings 11:18) 
All the people of the land went to the temple of Baal and destroyed it. They utterly shattered its altars and idols. They also killed Mathan, the priest of Baal, in front of the altars. Then the priest stationed guards in the Temple of the Lord.

(2 Kings 11:19) 
He then took the centurions, the Carians, the royal guards, and all the people of the land. They led the king from the Temple of the Lord and entered the palace through the Gate of the Guards. Ioas then took his seat on the royal throne.

(2 Kings 11:20) 
All the people of the land rejoiced, and the city became peaceful. Athalia had been killed by the sword at the royal palace.

(2 Kings 11:21) 
Ioas was seven years old when he began to reign.

(2 Kings 11:22) 
In the seventh year of Iehu’s reign, Ioas began to reign. He reigned for forty years in Ierusalem. His mother’s name was Sebia, from Bersabee.

(2 Kings 11:23) 
Ioas did what was right in the eyes of the Lord all the days that Ioiada the priest guided him.

(2 Kings 11:24) 
Nevertheless, he did not remove the high places of worship. The people still continued to sacrifice and burn incense there.

(2 Kings 11:25) 
Ioas said to the priests: “All the consecrated money that is brought to the Temple of the Lord by passersby—including money offered as atonement for a soul or dedicated by a personal vow, and whatever money people freely and willingly bring to the Temple of the Lord—

(2 Kings 11:26) 
let each priest receive it from his designated collectors, and with it, let them repair the deterioration of the Temple whenever they find anything broken or in disrepair.”

(2 Kings 11:27) 
But by the twenty-third year of King Ioas, the priests still had not repaired the deterioration of the Temple.

(2 Kings 11:28) 
So King Ioas summoned Ioiada the high priest and the other priests, saying to them: “Why have you not repaired the deterioration of the Temple? From now on, you are not to receive money from your collectors, but instead, you must hand it over directly for the Temple’s restoration.”

(2 Kings 11:29) 
Thus, the priests were forbidden from then on to receive money from the people and from overseeing the repair of the Temple’s deterioration themselves.

(2 Kings 11:30) 
Ioiada the high priest took a single chest, cut a hole in its lid, and placed it beside the altar, on the right side of those entering the Temple of the Lord. The priests who guarded the doors would put all the money brought to the Temple of the Lord into it.

(2 Kings 11:31) 
Whenever they saw that the chest was full, the king’s scribe and the high priest would go up. They would empty it and count the money that had been collected in the Temple of the Lord.

(2 Kings 11:32) 
They would then give the money, according to its counted sum and measure, into the hands of those overseeing the work, and to the carpenters, builders, and stonemasons who were to repair the Temple’s deterioration.

(2 Kings 11:33) 
It was also given to those who bought wood and cut stones to repair the damage to the Temple of the Lord, and for all other expenses required for the work of restoring the Temple.

(2 Kings 11:34) 
Nevertheless, silver bowls, pitchers, cups, trumpets, or any gold and silver vessels were not made in the Temple of the Lord from the money that was brought in.

(2 Kings 11:35) 
Instead, the money was given solely to those performing the work, so that they could use it to repair the deterioration of the Temple.

(2 Kings 11:36) 
No accounting was required from the men who were given the money to distribute to the workmen and carpenters, because they acted with complete trustworthiness.

(2 Kings 11:37) 
However, the money from the trespass offerings and the money from the sin offerings was not put into the Temple treasury; it belonged to the priests.

(2 Kings 11:38) 
At that time, Azahel, the king of Syria, advanced and fought against Geth, capturing it. He then turned his attention towards Ierusalem, intending to attack it.

(2 Kings 11:39) 
For this reason, Ioas, king of Iuda, took all the consecrated items that Iosaphat, Ioram, and Ochozias—his ancestors and kings of Iuda—had dedicated, along with his own offerings. He also took all the silver that could be found in the treasury of the Temple of the Lord and in the royal treasury. He sent all this to King Azahel of Syria, who then turned away from Ierusalem.

(2 Kings 11:40) 
The rest of the acts of Ioas, and all that he did, are they not indeed written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Iuda?

(2 Kings 11:1) 
When Athalia, the mother of Ochozias, saw that her son was dead, she rose up and killed all the royal offspring.

(2 Kings 11:2) 
However, Josaba—daughter of King Joram and sister of Ochozias—took Joas, the son of Ochozias, and secretly rescued him from among the other royal children who were being murdered. She hid him and his nurse in the bedroom, away from Athalia, and so he was not killed.

(2 Kings 11:3) 
So Joas was hidden with her in the Lord's Temple for six years, while Athalia reigned over the land.

(2 Kings 11:4) 
But in the seventh year, Joiada sent for the centurions and soldiers and brought them to him in the Lord's Temple. There he made a covenant with them, and after administering an oath in the Lord's Temple, he showed them the king's son.

(2 Kings 11:5) 
And he commanded them, saying, 'This is what you shall do: a third of you will come on the Sabbath and guard the king's palace.'

(2 Kings 11:6) 
Another third will guard the Sur Gate. And the final third will guard the inner gate, where the shield-bearers usually run their course. You will take turns guarding the Temple complex.

(2 Kings 11:7) 
And two other groups of you, all who typically go off duty on the Sabbath, are to guard the Lord's Temple around the king.

(2 Kings 11:8) 
Surround the king, with each man having his weapons in hand. Anyone who tries to break through your ranks is to be killed. You are to stay with the king both when he enters and when he exits.

(2 Kings 11:9) 
So the centurions did everything that Joiada the high priest had commanded them. Each centurion gathered his men, both those whose shift was beginning on the Sabbath and those whose shift was ending, and they came to Joiada the high priest.

(2 Kings 11:10) 
Then the high priest gave them the spears and the weapons of King David that were stored in the Lord's Temple.

(2 Kings 11:11) 
Then each man, with weapons in hand, took his position around the king, from the right side of the Temple all the way to the left side, encompassing both the altar and the Temple itself.

(2 Kings 11:12) 
Then Joiada brought out the king's son and placed the royal crown upon him, along with the Testimony (the law of the covenant). They proclaimed him king and anointed him. Then, clapping their hands, they all shouted, 'Long live the King!'

(2 Kings 11:13) 
When Athalia heard the shouts of the people running about, she came to the people in the Lord's Temple.

(2 Kings 11:14) 
She saw the new king standing on the platform according to custom, with the singers and trumpeters beside him. All the people of the land were rejoicing and blowing trumpets. So she tore her clothes and cried out, 'Treason! Treason!'

(2 Kings 11:15) 
Joiada then commanded the centurions who were in charge of the army, saying, 'Bring her out beyond the Temple precincts, and anyone who follows her is to be killed with the sword.' For the high priest had declared, 'Let her not be killed in the Lord's Temple.'

(2 Kings 11:16) 
So they seized her and led her out through the entrance for horses, next to the palace, and there she was put to death.

(2 Kings 11:17) 
Then Joiada made a covenant between the Lord, the king, and the people, establishing them as the Lord's own people. He also made a covenant between the king and the people.

(2 Kings 11:18) 
Then all the people of the land went to the temple of Baal and utterly demolished it. They smashed its altars and images into tiny pieces. They also killed Mathan, the priest of Baal, right in front of the altars.

(2 Kings 11:19) 
Joiada then appointed officers over the Lord's Temple, placing them under the authority of the priests and Levites, each performing his service in his assigned role within the Lord's house. This was to oversee the burnt offerings and peace offerings, according to the commandment of David, as it is written in the Book of Moses, and to perform these duties with joy and singing.

(2 Kings 11:20) 
Then Joiada, accompanied by the centurions, the mighty men, the leaders of the people, and all the common people of the land, led the new king from the Lord's Temple. They entered the palace through the Horse Gate, and the king took his seat upon the royal throne.

(2 Kings 11:21) 
All the people of the land rejoiced, and the city finally found peace. Athalia had been killed by the sword at the king's palace.

(2 Kings 11:1) 
Athaliah, who was the mother of Ahaziah, saw that her son was dead. So she rose up and killed all the royal offspring.

(2 Kings 11:2) 
But Jehosheba, who was King Jehoram's daughter and Ahaziah's sister, took Ahaziah's son, Joash. She secretly took him from among the king's children who were being killed. She gave him to his nurse in a hidden bedroom, so that he would not be killed by Athaliah.

(2 Kings 11:3) 
He remained hidden with her in the house of the Lord for six years. During this time, Athaliah reigned over the land as queen.

(2 Kings 11:4) 
In the seventh year, Jehoiada sent for the centurions and the soldiers. He brought them to him in the Temple of the Lord. He made a covenant with them there and swore them to an oath in the Temple of the Lord. Then he showed them the king's son, Joash.

(2 Kings 11:5) 
He commanded them, saying, "This is what you are to do: One-third of you, those who are entering on duty for the Sabbath, shall guard the royal palace."

(2 Kings 11:6) 
"Another third of you shall be at the Sur Gate. And the final third shall be at the gate behind the guardhouse. You will all keep watch over the palace building."

(2 Kings 11:7) 
"The other two divisions of you, all who are going off duty on the Sabbath, shall guard the Temple of the Lord around the king."

(2 Kings 11:8) 
"You shall surround the king, with each man having his weapons in his hands. If anyone tries to enter the inner courts, he shall be killed. You are to remain with the king as he enters and leaves."

(2 Kings 11:9) 
So the centurions did everything that Jehoiada the priest had commanded them. Each one took his men, those who were entering duty on the Sabbath, along with those who were going off duty from the Sabbath, and they came to Jehoiada the priest.

(2 Kings 11:10) 
The priest then gave them spears and the weapons of King David, which were kept in the Temple of the Lord.

(2 Kings 11:11) 
The men stood, each with his weapons in his hands. They formed a line from the right side of the Temple to the left side, by the altar, the Temple itself, and all around the king.

(2 Kings 11:12) 
Then Jehoiada brought out the king's son. He placed the royal crown on him and presented him with the testimony, which was the covenant scroll. They made him king and anointed him with oil. They clapped their hands and shouted, "Long live the king!"

(2 Kings 11:13) 
When Athaliah heard the noise of the people running and praising the king, she entered the Temple of the Lord where the people were.

(2 Kings 11:14) 
She saw the king standing by the pillar, as was the custom, with the singers and trumpeters near him. All the people of the land were rejoicing and blowing trumpets. So she tore her clothes and cried out, "Treason! Treason!"

(2 Kings 11:15) 
Jehoiada commanded the centurions who were in charge of the army. He told them, "Bring her out beyond the Temple courts. And whoever follows her, let him be killed by the sword." For the priest had said, "She must not be killed in the Temple of the Lord."

(2 Kings 11:16) 
So they seized her. She went out through the Horse Gate, which was near the royal palace, and she was killed there.

(2 Kings 11:17) 
Then Jehoiada made a covenant between the Lord, the king, and the people, so that they would be the Lord's people. He also established a covenant between the king and the people.

(2 Kings 11:18) 
All the people of the land went to the temple of Baal and destroyed it. They smashed its altars and its idols into pieces, completely destroying them. They also killed Mattan, the priest of Baal, in front of his altar. Then the priest Jehoiada appointed guards over the Temple of the Lord.

(2 Kings 11:19) 
Jehoiada took the centurions, the Carites (a foreign mercenary guard), the royal guards, and all the people of the land. They brought the king down from the Temple of the Lord. They entered the palace by way of the royal guard's gate, and he sat on the throne of the kings.

(2 Kings 11:20) 
All the people of the land rejoiced, and the city was quiet and at peace. Athaliah, however, had been killed by the sword in the royal palace.

(2 Kings 11:21) 
Joash was seven years old when he began to reign.

(2 Kings 11:22) 
In the seventh year of Jehu's reign, Joash became king. He reigned for forty years in Jerusalem. His mother's name was Zibiah, from Beersheba.

(2 Kings 11:23) 
Joash did what was right in the sight of the Lord all the days that Jehoiada the priest instructed him.

(2 Kings 11:24) 
Nevertheless, he did not remove the high places—these were the local places of worship outside Jerusalem. The people still sacrificed and burned incense on these high places.

(2 Kings 11:25) 
Joash said to the priests, "All the money that is brought into the Temple of the Lord for sacred purposes by those who pass through—the money paid for a person's life, and any money that people freely and willingly bring to the Temple of the Lord—"

(2 Kings 11:26) 
"Let the priests receive it, each from his own district, and let them repair the damages of the Temple building wherever they find a breach or a gap."

(2 Kings 11:27) 
However, by the twenty-third year of King Joash's reign, the priests had still not repaired the damages of the Temple.

(2 Kings 11:28) 
So King Joash called for Jehoiada the chief priest and the other priests. He asked them, "Why are you not repairing the damages of the Temple? From now on, you shall not receive money from the people for yourselves. Instead, you must hand it over directly for the Temple repairs."

(2 Kings 11:29) 
The priests were then forbidden to receive money from the people for their own use and were tasked only with repairing the breaches of the Temple.

(2 Kings 11:30) 
Jehoiada the chief priest took one chest and bored a hole in its lid. He placed it beside the altar, on the right side as one entered the Temple of the Lord. The priests who guarded the entrance would put into it all the money that was brought to the Temple of the Lord.

(2 Kings 11:31) 
When they saw that there was a large amount of money in the chest, the king's secretary and the chief priest would go up. They would empty it and count the money that was found in the Temple of the Lord.

(2 Kings 11:32) 
They would then give the counted money to the supervisors of the masons, the builders, and the stonecutters, who were restoring the Temple of the Lord.

(2 Kings 11:33) 
They gave it to those who cut stones and to the quarrymen. It was also used to buy wood and cut stones, so that the entire Temple of the Lord could be restored wherever there were damages. This money was spent specifically for the restoration of the Temple.

(2 Kings 11:34) 
However, no silver basins, snuffers, bowls, trumpets, or any other vessels of gold or silver were made for the Temple of the Lord from the money brought into the Temple.

(2 Kings 11:35) 
Instead, that money was given to those who performed the work, so that they could use it to restore the Temple of the Lord.

(2 Kings 11:36) 
No accounting was required from the men who received the money to distribute to the workmen and the laborers, because they were considered trustworthy.

(2 Kings 11:37) 
The money from trespass offerings and sin offerings was not brought into the Temple of the Lord, because that money belonged to the priests.

(2 Kings 11:38) 
At that time, Hazael, the king of Syria, came up and fought against Gath and captured it. Then he set his sights on marching against Jerusalem.

(2 Kings 11:39) 
Because of this threat, King Joash of Judah took all the sacred gifts that his fathers—Jehoshaphat, Jehoram, and Ahaziah, the kings of Judah—had consecrated. He also took his own consecrated gifts, and all the silver that could be found in the treasuries of the Temple of the Lord and in the royal palace treasury. He sent all these to King Hazael of Syria. In exchange for these treasures, Hazael turned his army away from Jerusalem.

(2 Kings 11:40) 
Now, as for the rest of the acts of Joash, and all that he did, are these not written in the book of the chronicles of the kings of Judah?

(2 Kings 11:1) 
Athalia, the mother of Ahaziah, heard that her son was dead. She then rose up and ordered the killing of all who were of the royal lineage, to eliminate all potential heirs to the throne.

(2 Kings 11:2) 
But Jehosheba, the daughter of King Joram and sister of Ahaziah, rescued Ahaziah's son, Joash, by secretly taking him from among the other royal children who were being murdered. She gave him to his nurse in a hidden room away from Athalia, and so he was not killed.

(2 Kings 11:3) 
Joash remained hidden with her in the house of the Lord, the Temple, for six years, all while Athalia was ruling over the land.

(2 Kings 11:4) 
Then, in the seventh year of Athalia's reign, Jehoiada the high priest sent for the captains of hundreds and the soldiers. He brought them to himself in the Temple of the Lord, made a solemn covenant with them, and after making them swear an oath in the Temple, he showed them the king’s son, Joash.

(2 Kings 11:5) 
Jehoiada then commanded them, saying: “These are your instructions: a third of your men, those who are coming on duty for the Sabbath, shall go into the palace and guard the king’s residence.

(2 Kings 11:6) 
Another third of you will stand guard at the Sur Gate, and the final third will be at the gate behind the guards' barracks. You must keep watch over the Temple to ensure it is not breached.”

(2 Kings 11:7) 
“As for the other two parts of your men, all who are going off duty on the Sabbath, they shall guard the Lord's Temple and surround the king.

(2 Kings 11:8) 
You shall form a protective circle around the king, with your weapons ready in your hands. If anyone attempts to enter your lines, they are to be killed. You are to remain with the king, protecting him whenever he enters or leaves.”

(2 Kings 11:9) 
The captains of hundreds carried out all the orders given to them by Jehoiada the priest. Each officer took command of his incoming men, those who were starting their Sabbath duty, and his outgoing men, those who were finishing their Sabbath duty, and they all assembled before Jehoiada the priest.

(2 Kings 11:10) 
Then Jehoiada the priest equipped them, giving them spears and the weapons of King David that had been kept in the Lord's Temple treasury.

(2 Kings 11:11) 
Each man took his position with weapons in hand, forming a perimeter from the right side of the Temple all the way to the left side of the altar and the main Temple building, surrounding the king.

(2 Kings 11:12) 
Then Jehoiada brought out the king's son, Joash, and placed the royal crown upon him. He also presented him with a copy of God’s Law, symbolizing his covenant with God and his duty to rule justly. They then proclaimed him king and anointed him with oil. The people clapped their hands and shouted, “Long live the king!”

(2 Kings 11:13) 
Athalia heard the noise of the people running and praising the new king. She went to where the people were, entering into the Lord's Temple.

(2 Kings 11:14) 
There she saw the young king standing on the royal platform, as was the custom. The Temple singers were there, with trumpeters nearby, and all the people of the land were rejoicing and sounding their trumpets. Athalia tore her royal robes in distress and cried out, “Conspiracy! Treason!”

(2 Kings 11:15) 
Jehoiada the priest then gave orders to the captains of the army: “Lead her out from the Temple grounds, and anyone who follows her is to be killed by the sword.” The priest had given this instruction because he did not want her to be put to death in the sacred house of the Lord.

(2 Kings 11:16) 
So they seized her and led her out through the Horse Gate, which led to the royal palace, and there she was executed.

(2 Kings 11:17) 
So Jehoiada formally established a covenant between the Lord, the new king, and the people, confirming that the nation would again wholeheartedly belong to the Lord.

(2 Kings 11:18) 
Then all the people of the land went to the temple of Baal and utterly destroyed it, along with its altars and idols, which they thoroughly smashed. They also killed Mattan, the priest of Baal, right in front of his altars. Jehoiada the priest then placed guards over the Lord's Temple.

(2 Kings 11:19) 
Jehoiada then led the captains, the Carite guards, the royal footmen, and all the people of the land, bringing the king from the Temple of the Lord. They entered the palace through the main guard gate, and Joash then sat upon the royal throne, taking his rightful place as king.

(2 Kings 11:20) 
All the people of the land rejoiced, and the city finally found peace and quiet. Athalia had been put to death by the sword near the king's palace, ending her reign of terror.

(2 Kings 11:21) 
Joash was seven years old when he began his reign as king.

(2 Kings 12:1) 
In the seventh year of Jehu's reign, Joas began to reign as king. He reigned for forty years in Jerusalem, the capital city. His mother's name was Sebia, and she was from the city of Bersabee.

(2 Kings 12:2) 
And Joas did what was right in the sight of the Lord during all the days that Jojada the high priest instructed and guided him.

(2 Kings 12:3) 
Nevertheless, King Joas did not tear down the high places of worship outside of Jerusalem, so the people continued to offer sacrifices and burn incense in these unauthorized shrines.

(2 Kings 12:4) 
King Joas then said to the priests: "Collect all the money from the holy offerings that is brought into the Lord's Temple. This includes money from visitors, from those who pay the redemption tax for their lives, and whatever people willingly and freely bring to the Lord's Temple from their hearts."

(2 Kings 12:5) 
"The priests are to receive this money, each from his own assigned collection point. Then they are to use it to repair any damage they find in the Temple structure, wherever they see a need for restoration."

(2 Kings 12:6) 
However, up to the twenty-third year of King Joas's reign, the priests still had not completed the repairs on the Temple structure.

(2 Kings 12:7) 
So King Joas called for Jojada the high priest and the other priests and demanded of them: "Why have you not repaired the damages of the Temple? From now on, you are not to keep this money for yourselves. Instead, you must give it directly for the repairs of the Temple."

(2 Kings 12:8) 
Therefore, the priests were forbidden from accepting money from the people for their own use, and they were also no longer solely responsible for directing the repairs of the Temple.

(2 Kings 12:9) 
Then Jojada the high priest took a single chest and drilled a hole in its lid. He placed it beside the altar, to the right of those entering the Lord's Temple. And the priests who guarded the entrance deposited all the money that was brought to the Lord's Temple directly into this chest.

(2 Kings 12:10) 
Whenever the Temple officials saw that a large amount of money had accumulated in the chest, the king's secretary and the high priest would go up. They would empty the chest and count the money that had been collected for the Lord's Temple.

(2 Kings 12:11) 
They then gave the counted money directly into the hands of those who supervised the work, and to the carpenters and the masons they had hired, who were responsible for repairing the Temple.

(2 Kings 12:12) 
They also paid the timber merchants and stonecutters for purchasing stone and timber, and for all other expenses related to restoring the damages of the Temple.

(2 Kings 12:13) 
Nevertheless, out of the money brought into the Lord's Temple, no silver basins, tongs, bowls, trumpets, or any other vessels of gold or silver were made for use in the Temple rituals.

(2 Kings 12:14) 
Instead, the money was given only to those who were doing the work, so that they could use it to repair the damages of the Temple.

(2 Kings 12:15) 
They did not require an accounting from the men who received the money to pay the workers, because they entrusted it to them in good faith.

(2 Kings 12:16) 
However, the money from sin offerings and guilt offerings was not brought into the Lord's Temple chest, because that money belonged to the priests for their sustenance.

(2 Kings 12:17) 
At that time, Hazael, the king of Syria, marched up and fought against the city of Geth and captured it. Then he set his sights on marching up against Jerusalem.

(2 Kings 12:18) 
Because of this threat, Joas, the king of Judah, took all the sacred gifts that his fathers, the kings of Judah—Josaphat, Joram, and Ochozias—had dedicated to the Lord, along with his own offerings, and all the gold that could be found in the treasuries of the Lord's Temple and in the king's palace. He sent all of this as a tribute to Hazael, the king of Syria, and Hazael then turned away from attacking Jerusalem.

(2 Kings 12:19) 
Are not the rest of the deeds of Joas, and all that he accomplished, recorded in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Judah?

(2 Kings 12:20) 
However, his own servants rose up and conspired against him. They struck down Joas in the house of Mello, which is on the road that goes down to Sella.

(2 Kings 12:21) 
Josachar, the son of Semaath, and Jozabad, the son of Somer, his own servants, struck him down, and he died. They buried him with his ancestors in the City of David. His son Amasias then reigned in his place.

(2 Kings 12:1) 
In the seventh year of Jehu's reign, Joash became king. He reigned for forty years in Jerusalem. His mother's name was Zibiah, from Beersheba.

(2 Kings 12:2) 
Joash did what was right in the sight of the Lord throughout all the days that Jehoiada the priest instructed him.

(2 Kings 12:3) 
Nevertheless, he did not remove the high places. The people continued to sacrifice and burn incense there.

(2 Kings 12:4) 
Joash said to the priests: "All the money that is brought into the temple of the Lord from those who pass through—money consecrated to God, that is given as a vow, or that anyone willingly offers—and brought into the temple of the Lord:"

(2 Kings 12:5) 
"Let the priests receive it according to their assigned duty, and let them repair the damages of the temple, wherever they find anything broken."

(2 Kings 12:6) 
But up until the twenty-third year of King Joash, the priests had not repaired the damages of the temple.

(2 Kings 12:7) 
So King Joash called Jehoiada the high priest and the other priests, saying to them: "Why have you not repaired the damages of the temple? Therefore, do not receive any more money according to your assigned duty, but give it for the repair of the temple."

(2 Kings 12:8) 
And the priests were forbidden from receiving any more money from the people or repairing the damages of the temple themselves.

(2 Kings 12:9) 
Then Jehoiada the high priest took a single chest and drilled a hole in its lid. He placed it beside the altar, on the right side of those entering the House of the Lord. And the priests who guarded the entrances deposited all the money that was brought to the temple of the Lord into it.

(2 Kings 12:10) 
Whenever they saw that there was a large amount of money in the chest, the king's secretary and the high priest would go up to it, empty it out, and count the money that was found in the temple of the Lord.

(2 Kings 12:11) 
Then they would give it, carefully counted and measured, into the hands of those who supervised the builders of the House of the Lord. These supervisors, in turn, spent it on the masons and the carpenters who worked on the temple of the Lord.

(2 Kings 12:12) 
They also spent it on those who repaired the cracks, and on purchasing stones and timbers to fully restore the damages of the temple of the Lord, whatever needed repair.

(2 Kings 12:13) 
However, no silver basins, snuffers, bowls, trumpets, or any gold or silver vessels were made from that particular money that was brought into the temple of the Lord.

(2 Kings 12:14) 
Instead, that money was given to those who performed the work, so that they could repair the damages of the temple of the Lord with it.

(2 Kings 12:15) 
And no accounting was required from the men who received the money to distribute it to the builders, because they acted with integrity.

(2 Kings 12:16) 
However, money from trespass offerings and sin offerings was not brought into the temple of the Lord, but belonged to the priests.

(2 Kings 12:17) 
At that time, Hazael, the king of Syria, came up and fought against Gath and captured it. Then he set his sights on marching up against Jerusalem.

(2 Kings 12:18) 
For this reason, Joash, the king of Judah, took all the sacred gifts that his fathers, King Jehoshaphat, Jehoram, and Ahaziah, had consecrated, along with what he himself had offered. He also took all the silver that could be found in the treasuries of the temple of the Lord and in the king's treasuries, and he sent it to Hazael, the king of Syria. As a result, Hazael withdrew from Jerusalem.

(2 Kings 12:19) 
As for the rest of the deeds of Joash, and all that he did, are these not written in the book of the chronicles of the kings of Judah?

(2 Kings 12:20) 
But his servants conspired against him and struck him down in the House of Millo, on the road down to Silla.

(2 Kings 12:21) 
Indeed, Jozachar, the son of Shimeath, and Jozabad, the son of Shomer, his servants, struck him, and he died. They buried him with his fathers in the City of David, and his son Amaziah reigned in his place.

(2 Kings 12:1) 
In the seventh year of Jehu's reign, Joash became king. He ruled in Jerusalem for forty years. His mother's name was Zibiah, and she was from Beersheba.

(2 Kings 12:2) 
King Joash did what was right in the eyes of the Lord all the days that Jehoiada the High Priest guided and taught him.

(2 Kings 12:3) 
Nevertheless, the king did not remove the high places of worship. The people continued to offer sacrifices and burn incense in these high places.

(2 Kings 12:4) 
King Joash then spoke to the priests: "All the consecrated funds that are brought into the Temple of the Lord by those who pass through, and the money offered as a redemption for a soul, and whatever people willingly and freely bring into the Temple of the Lord, out of their own free will—"

(2 Kings 12:5) 
"...—the priests are to receive these funds according to their assigned duties, and they must use them to repair the structural damage of the Temple, specifically anything they find that is broken or dilapidated."

(2 Kings 12:6) 
However, up until the twenty-third year of King Joash's reign, the priests had not yet repaired the structural damage of the Temple.

(2 Kings 12:7) 
So King Joash called for Jehoiada the High Priest and the other priests, asking them: "Why are you not repairing the damage to the Temple? From now on, you are not to personally receive the money, but instead, you must hand it over specifically for the purpose of repairing and restoring the Temple's damage."

(2 Kings 12:8) 
Therefore, the priests were forbidden from then on to collect money directly from the people for themselves, or to manage the repairs of the Temple on their own.

(2 Kings 12:9) 
So Jehoiada the High Priest took one chest, drilled a hole in its lid, and placed it beside the altar, on the right side as one enters the House of the Lord. The priests who guarded the entrance then put all the money that was brought into the Temple of the Lord into this chest.

(2 Kings 12:10) 
When they saw that a large amount of money had accumulated in the chest, the king's scribe and the High Priest would go up, empty out the chest, and count the money that was found in the House of the Lord.

(2 Kings 12:11) 
They would then give the counted money to those who were in charge of the craftsmen, the skilled laborers, and the builders of the House of the Lord. These were the ones responsible for repairing the structural work of the Temple.

(2 Kings 12:12) 
This money was given to the carpenters, the masons, and those who quarried stones. It was also used to purchase wood and cut stones from the quarries for repairing the structural work of the House of the Lord, and for all other materials needed for the Temple's restoration.

(2 Kings 12:13) 
However, from the money that was brought into the Temple, no silver basins, tongs, bowls, trumpets, or any other golden or silver vessels were made for the Temple of the Lord.

(2 Kings 12:14) 
Instead, the money was given to the workers so that they could use it to repair the Temple of the Lord.

(2 Kings 12:15) 
And no accounting was required from the men who received the money to distribute it to the craftsmen and skilled laborers, for they acted with faithfulness and integrity.

(2 Kings 12:16) 
However, money from trespass offerings and money from sin offerings was not brought into the Temple of the Lord, because these specific funds belonged to the priests as their rightful portion.

(2 Kings 12:17) 
At that time, Hazael, the king of Syria, attacked and fought against Gath, capturing it. He then set his sights on Jerusalem, preparing to conquer it next.

(2 Kings 12:18) 
Because of this threat, King Joash of Judah took all the sacred gifts that his fathers—Kings Jehoshaphat, Jehoram, and Ahaziah of Judah—had dedicated, along with his own offerings. He also took all the silver that could be found in the treasuries of the House of the Lord and in the king's treasury. He sent all of this to King Hazael of Syria, and by doing so, he diverted the attack away from Jerusalem.

(2 Kings 12:19) 
Now, concerning the rest of the acts of Joash, and all that he accomplished, are these not indeed written in the Book of the Annals of the Kings of Judah?

(2 Kings 12:20) 
However, his own servants rose up and conspired against him, striking down King Joash at Beth Millo, on the road descending to Silla.

(2 Kings 12:21) 
Indeed, his servants Jozachar, son of Shimeath, and Jehozabad, son of Shomer, were the ones who struck him, and he died. They buried him with his ancestors in the City of David. Then his son Amaziah became king in his place.

(2 Kings 12:1) 
In the seventh year of Jehu's reign, Joash became king. He reigned for forty years in Jerusalem. His mother's name was Zibiah, and she was from Beersheba.

(2 Kings 12:2) 
Joash did what was right in the sight of the Lord all the days that Jehoiada the priest instructed him.

(2 Kings 12:3) 
However, he did not remove the high places of pagan worship. The people still continued to offer sacrifices and burn incense in these high places.

(2 Kings 12:4) 
Joash then said to the priests: 'All the money offered as sacred gifts that is brought into the Temple of the Lord by those passing through, and from individual men, according to the assessed value of their souls, and all the money that is voluntarily and willingly brought into the Temple of the Lord—'

(2 Kings 12:5) 
'—let the priests receive it according to their regular practice, and use it to repair the Temple's damage, wherever ruin is found.'

(2 Kings 12:6) 
However, up to the twenty-third year of King Joash's reign, the priests had not yet repaired the Temple's damage.

(2 Kings 12:7) 
So King Joash called for Jehoiada the high priest and the other priests, saying to them: 'Why have you not repaired the Temple's damage? From now on, you are not to receive money according to your regular portion, but you must give it for the restoration of the Temple.'

(2 Kings 12:8) 
Consequently, the priests were forbidden from receiving any more money from the people for their own use, and they were instead charged with repairing the Temple.

(2 Kings 12:9) 
Then Jehoiada the high priest took a single chest, cut a hole in its lid, and placed it beside the altar, to the right of those entering the Lord's house. The priests who guarded the doors would place all the money that was brought into the Lord's Temple into this chest.

(2 Kings 12:10) 
Whenever they saw that there was a large amount of silver in the chest, the king's scribe and the high priest would go up, empty it, and count the money that was found in the Lord's Temple.

(2 Kings 12:11) 
They would then give the counted money to those who were in charge of the work, and to the carpenters and masons who were repairing the Lord's house,

(2 Kings 12:12) 
and to those who cut stones, and to those who carried materials. This was also for buying timber and cut stones, and for performing all other repairs needed for the Lord's Temple.

(2 Kings 12:13) 
However, no golden or silver ornaments, no bowls, no basins, no trumpets, nor any golden or silver vessels were made for the Lord's Temple from the money that was brought in.

(2 Kings 12:14) 
Instead, the money was given to the workmen so that the Lord's Temple could be repaired with it.

(2 Kings 12:15) 
The men who received the money to distribute to the workmen were not required to give an account for it, because they acted with integrity and trustworthiness.

(2 Kings 12:16) 
But the money for guilt offerings and the money for sin offerings was not brought into the Lord's Temple, because that money belonged to the priests as their portion.

(2 Kings 12:17) 
At that time, Hazael, the king of Syria, went up and fought against Gath and captured it. He then set his sights on marching against Jerusalem.

(2 Kings 12:18) 
Because of this threat, Joash, the king of Judah, took all the sacred gifts that his fathers, King Jehoshaphat, King Jehoram, and King Ahaziah, had consecrated, along with his own offerings, and all the silver that could be found in the treasuries of the Lord's Temple and in the king's palace. He sent all of this to Hazael, the king of Syria, and Hazael then turned away from Jerusalem.

(2 Kings 12:19) 
As for the rest of the acts of Joash, and all that he did, are these not written in the Book of the Annals of the Kings of Judah?

(2 Kings 12:20) 
However, his own servants rose up and formed a conspiracy among themselves. They struck down Joash in the house of Millo, which is on the way down to Silla.

(2 Kings 12:21) 
Jozachar, the son of Shimeath, and Jehozabad, the son of Shomer, his own servants, struck him dead. He was buried with his forefathers in the city of David, and his son Amaziah became king in his place.

(2 Kings 13:1) 
In the twenty-third year of Joash, the son of Ahaziah, who was king of Judah, Jehoahaz, the son of Jehu, began to reign over Israel in Samaria. He reigned for sixteen years.

(2 Kings 13:2) 
And he did evil in the sight of the Lord. He followed the sins of Jeroboam, the son of Nebat, who had caused Israel to sin, and he did not turn away from those sins.

(2 Kings 13:3) 
So the Lord was angry with Israel and delivered them into the power of Hazael, the king of Syria, and into the power of Ben-Hadad, the son of Hazael, for all those days.

(2 Kings 13:4) 
But Jehoahaz pleaded with the Lord, and the Lord heard him, for He saw the suffering of Israel because the king of Syria had greatly oppressed them.

(2 Kings 13:5) 
And the Lord gave Israel a deliverer, and he freed them from the power of Syria, so the children of Israel lived in their own homes as they had before—in peace and security.

(2 Kings 13:6) 
Nevertheless, they did not turn away from the sins of the house of Jeroboam, who had caused Israel to sin, but they persisted in those sins. Moreover, the Asherah pole also remained standing in Samaria.

(2 Kings 13:7) 
And the Lord had left to Jehoahaz no more of the people than fifty horsemen, ten chariots, and ten thousand foot soldiers, for the king of Syria had destroyed them and made them like dust when threshing grain.

(2 Kings 13:8) 
Now the rest of the acts of Jehoahaz, and all that he did, and his strength, are these not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?

(2 Kings 13:9) 
So Jehoahaz slept with his fathers, and they buried him in Samaria. And Joash, his son, reigned in his place.

(2 Kings 13:10) 
In the thirty-seventh year of Joash, the king of Judah, Joash, the son of Jehoahaz, began to reign over Israel in Samaria, and he reigned for sixteen years.

(2 Kings 13:11) 
And he did what was evil in the sight of the Lord. He did not turn away from all the sins of Jeroboam, the son of Nebat, who had caused Israel to sin, but he persisted in them.

(2 Kings 13:12) 
Now the rest of the acts of Joash, and all that he did, and his strength, and how he fought against Amaziah, the king of Judah, are these not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?

(2 Kings 13:13) 
So Joash slept with his fathers, and Jeroboam sat on his throne. And Joash was buried in Samaria with the kings of Israel.

(2 Kings 13:14) 
Now Elisha was suffering from the illness of which he was to die. And Joash, the king of Israel, went down to him and wept before him, saying, 'My father, my father! You are the very strength and defense of Israel!'

(2 Kings 13:15) 
And Elisha said to him, 'Bring a bow and arrows.' So he brought a bow and arrows to him.

(2 Kings 13:16) 
He then said to the king of Israel, 'Put your hand on the bow.' And when the king had put his hand on it, Elisha put his own hands over the king's hands.

(2 Kings 13:17) 
And Elisha said, 'Open the eastern window.' And when he had opened it, Elisha said, 'Shoot the arrow!' And he shot it. Then Elisha said, 'This is the arrow of the Lord’s deliverance, the arrow of deliverance against Syria! You will strike down Syria at Aphek until you have utterly destroyed them!'

(2 Kings 13:18) 
And again Elisha said, 'Take the arrows.' And when he had taken them, he said to the king of Israel, 'Strike the ground with the arrows.' And he struck the ground three times, and then he stopped.

(2 Kings 13:19) 
And the man of God was angry with him and said, 'If you had struck the ground five or six or seven times, you would have struck down Syria until its complete destruction. But now you will strike Syria only three times!'

(2 Kings 13:20) 
So Elisha died, and they buried him. Now, bands of Moabite raiders would invade the land in the spring of that year.

(2 Kings 13:21) 
And as some men were burying a man, they saw the raiders and quickly threw the corpse into Elisha’s tomb. And when the corpse touched the bones of Elisha, the man was revived and stood up on his feet.

(2 Kings 13:22) 
Now Hazael, the king of Syria, had oppressed Israel throughout all the days of Jehoahaz.

(2 Kings 13:23) 
But the Lord was merciful to them and turned to them because of His covenant which He had made with Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob. He was unwilling to destroy them or utterly cast them from His presence, even to this present time.

(2 Kings 13:24) 
So Hazael, the king of Syria, died, and Ben-Hadad, his son, reigned in his place.

(2 Kings 13:25) 
And Joash, the son of Jehoahaz, took back from the power of Ben-Hadad, the son of Hazael, the cities which Hazael had taken from the power of Jehoahaz, his father, in battle. Joash defeated him three times and restored the cities to Israel.

(2 Kings 13:1) 
In the twenty-third year of the reign of Joash, son of Ahaziah, king of Judah, Jehoahaz, the son of Jehu, began his seventeen-year reign over Israel in Samaria.

(2 Kings 13:2) 
He did what was evil in the sight of the Lord. He continued to commit the sins of Jeroboam, son of Nebat, who caused Israel to sin. He did not turn away from those sins.

(2 Kings 13:3) 
The Lord's anger burned hot against Israel. He handed them over to the power of Hazael, the king of Syria, and later to Ben-Hadad, Hazael’s son, for the entire reign of these kings.

(2 Kings 13:4) 
Jehoahaz then pleaded before the Lord, and the Lord heard him, for the Lord saw the oppression of Israel, because the king of Syria was crushing them.

(2 Kings 13:5) 
And the Lord gave Israel a deliverer, and they were rescued from the power of the king of Syria. The Israelites then lived in their homes in peace, as they had in previous times.

(2 Kings 13:6) 
However, they did not turn away from the sins of Jeroboam's family line, who caused Israel to sin. Instead, they continued to practice those very sins. Moreover, the Asherah pole—a false idol—remained standing in Samaria.

(2 Kings 13:7) 
Jehoahaz had almost no fighting force left from his army, except for fifty cavalrymen, ten chariots, and ten thousand infantrymen. This was because the king of Syria had decimated them, he had ground them down like dust on the threshing floor.

(2 Kings 13:8) 
Now the rest of the acts of Jehoahaz, and all that he did, and his strength—are these not recorded in the book of the chronicles of the kings of Israel?

(2 Kings 13:9) 
Jehoahaz rested in death with his ancestors, and they buried him in Samaria. His son Joash began to reign in his place.

(2 Kings 13:10) 
In the thirty-seventh year of Joash's reign over Judah, Joash, the son of Jehoahaz, began his sixteen-year reign over Israel in Samaria.

(2 Kings 13:11) 
He did what was evil in the sight of the Lord. He did not turn away from any of the sins of Jeroboam, son of Nebat, who had caused Israel to sin, but he continued to practice those very sins.

(2 Kings 13:12) 
Now the rest of the acts of Joash, and all that he did, and his strength, including how he fought against Amaziah, the king of Judah—are these not recorded in the book of the chronicles of the kings of Israel?

(2 Kings 13:13) 
Joash rested in death with his ancestors, and Jeroboam then took his place on the throne. Moreover, Joash was buried in Samaria, among the kings of Israel.

(2 Kings 13:14) 
Now Elisha was suffering from the illness that would ultimately cause his death. King Joash of Israel went to visit him and wept before him, crying out: "My father, my father! You are the very strength of Israel, its chariots and horsemen!"

(2 Kings 13:15) 
Elisha said to him, "Bring a bow and arrows." And when the king had brought him a bow and arrows,

(2 Kings 13:16) 
Elisha said to the king of Israel, "Place your hand on the bow." And when the king had placed his hand on the bow, Elisha placed his own hands over the king's hands.

(2 Kings 13:17) 
Then Elisha said, "Open the window facing east." And the king opened it. Elisha told him, "Shoot." And he shot the arrow. Elisha declared: "This is the Lord's arrow of salvation, an arrow of victory against Syria! You will strike down Syria at Aphek until they are utterly defeated."

(2 Kings 13:18) 
Then Elisha said, "Now pick up the arrows." And the king picked them up. Again, Elisha told him, "Strike the ground with them." So the king struck the ground three times, and then he stopped.

(2 Kings 13:19) 
And the man of God became angry with him and said, "If you had struck the ground five or six times, you would have completely defeated Syria. But now, you will defeat Syria only three times."

(2 Kings 13:20) 
So Elisha died, and he was buried. Now, every year, Moabite raiding parties would invade the land.

(2 Kings 13:21) 
Once, as some men were burying a dead man, they suddenly saw a raiding party approaching and quickly threw the dead body into Elisha's tomb. As soon as the body touched Elisha's bones, the man was restored to life and stood up on his feet.

(2 Kings 13:22) 
Throughout the entire reign of Jehoahaz, Hazael, the king of Syria, had oppressed Israel.

(2 Kings 13:23) 
But the Lord had compassion on them and He turned back to them because of His covenant, which He had established with Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob. He was unwilling to destroy them or to utterly cast them away from His presence, right up to the present day.

(2 Kings 13:24) 
Then Hazael, the king of Syria, died, and his son Ben-Hadad began to reign in his place.

(2 Kings 13:25) 
Now Joash, the son of Jehoahaz, recaptured the cities that Ben-Hadad, son of Hazael, had taken from his father, Jehoahaz. Joash defeated Ben-Hadad three times and restored the cities of Israel to its control.

(2 Kings 13:1) 
In the twenty-third year of Joas, son of Ochozia, the king of Judah, Joachaz, son of Jehu, began to reign over Israel in Samaria. He reigned for sixteen years.

(2 Kings 13:2) 
He did evil in the Lord's presence. He continued the sins of Jeroboam, son of Nabat, who had led Israel into sin, and he never turned away from them.

(2 Kings 13:3) 
The Lord's wrath burned against Israel, and He handed them over to Hazael, king of Syria, and to Hazael's son, Benadad, for many days.

(2 Kings 13:4) 
However, Joachaz implored the Lord for help, and the Lord heard him, because He had seen the distress of Israel and how the king of Syria had afflicted them.

(2 Kings 13:5) 
So the Lord provided Israel with a deliverer, and He freed them from the hand of the king of Syria. The people of Israel were released from Syrian control and were able to live in their homes peacefully again, just as they had before the war.

(2 Kings 13:6) 
Nevertheless, they did not turn away from the sins of Jeroboam's house—the ones who had led Israel into sin. Instead, they continued in them. Even the Asherah pole, dedicated to false gods, remained standing in Samaria.

(2 Kings 13:7) 
For Joachaz, there were only fifty horsemen, ten chariots, and ten thousand foot soldiers left in his army. The king of Syria had destroyed all the rest, crushing them like dust under the threshing sledge.

(2 Kings 13:8) 
Now, the rest of the history of Joachaz—all that he did, and how bravely he acted—is it not all written in the book of the chronicles of the kings of Israel?

(2 Kings 13:9) 
Joachaz died and was buried in Samaria. Then his son, Joas, reigned in his place.

(2 Kings 13:10) 
In the thirty-seventh year of Joas, the king of Judah, Joas, son of Joachaz, began to reign over Israel in Samaria. He reigned for sixteen years.

(2 Kings 13:11) 
He also did evil in the sight of the Lord. He did not turn away from any of the sins of Jeroboam, son of Nabat, who had led Israel into sin, but he continued to practice them.

(2 Kings 13:12) 
Now, the rest of the history of Joas—all that he did, and his might in fighting against Amasias, the king of Judah—is it not all written in the book of the chronicles of the kings of Israel?

(2 Kings 13:13) 
Joas died, and Jeroboam, his son, sat on his throne. Joas was buried in Samaria, among the kings of Israel.

(2 Kings 13:14) 
Now Eliseus became sick with the illness from which he would die. Joas, the king of Israel, went down to visit him and wept before him, saying, 'My father, my father! You are like the chariot and horsemen of Israel!'

(2 Kings 13:15) 
Eliseus said to him, 'Bring a bow and arrows.' So the king brought him a bow and arrows.

(2 Kings 13:16) 
Then Eliseus said to the king of Israel, 'Put your hand on the bow.' The king did so, and Eliseus placed his own hands over the king's hands.

(2 Kings 13:17) 
Eliseus said, 'Open the window to the east.' When the king opened it, Eliseus commanded, 'Shoot the arrow!' The king shot the arrow. Then Eliseus declared, 'This is the Lord's arrow of salvation and deliverance against Syria! You will strike Syria at Aphec until you completely destroy them!'

(2 Kings 13:18) 
Then Eliseus said, 'Take the arrows.' When the king had taken them, Eliseus said to him again, 'Strike the ground!' The king struck the ground three times and then stopped.

(2 Kings 13:19) 
The man of God was angry with him and said, 'If you had struck five, six, or even seven times, you would have utterly destroyed Syria! But now, you will strike Syria only three times.'

(2 Kings 13:20) 
So Eliseus died, and they buried him. In that same year, Moabite raiding parties invaded the land.

(2 Kings 13:21) 
As some men were burying a dead body, they suddenly saw the Moabite raiding parties approaching. So, they quickly threw the corpse into Eliseus's tomb. When the body touched Eliseus's bones, the man came back to life and stood on his feet!

(2 Kings 13:22) 
Throughout the entire reign of Joachaz, Hazael, the king of Syria, had oppressed Israel.

(2 Kings 13:23) 
However, the Lord had compassion on them. He turned to them because of His covenant with Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob. He did not wish to destroy them or utterly cast them out from His presence, even to this very day.

(2 Kings 13:24) 
Then Hazael, the king of Syria, died, and his son Benadad reigned in his place.

(2 Kings 13:25) 
Furthermore, Joas, son of Joachaz, recaptured the cities from Benadad, son of Hazael—the very cities Benadad's father had seized from Joachaz, his own father, in battle. Joas defeated Benadad three times, thus restoring those cities to Israel.

(2 Kings 13:1) 
In the twenty-third year of the reign of Joash, the son of Ahaziah, king of Judah, Jehoahaz, the son of Jehu, began his reign over Israel in Samaria, and he ruled for seventeen years.

(2 Kings 13:2) 
And he did what was evil in the sight of the Lord. He followed the sins of Jeroboam, the son of Nebat, who had made Israel commit sin; Jehoahaz did not turn away from those sins.

(2 Kings 13:3) 
Therefore, the Lord was angry with Israel. He handed them over to the power of Hazael, the king of Syria, and into the power of Ben-Hadad, Hazael's son, throughout those days.

(2 Kings 13:4) 
But Jehoahaz pleaded before the Lord. And the Lord heard him, because He saw the distress of Israel; for the king of Syria had oppressed them.

(2 Kings 13:5) 
So the Lord gave Israel a deliverer, and they were freed from the power of the king of Syria. Then the children of Israel were able to live in their homes, as they had in times past.

(2 Kings 13:6) 
Nevertheless, they did not turn away from the sins of the house of Jeroboam, who had made Israel commit sin; instead, they continued in them. Indeed, the Asherah pole remained standing in Samaria.

(2 Kings 13:7) 
For Jehoahaz, there remained no more of the army than fifty horsemen, ten chariots, and ten thousand foot soldiers. This was because the king of Syria had destroyed everyone else, crushing them like dust under the threshing sledges.

(2 Kings 13:8) 
Now, as for the rest of the acts of Jehoahaz, and everything he did, and his valiant deeds—are these not written in the book of the chronicles of the kings of Israel?

(2 Kings 13:9) 
So Jehoahaz rested with his fathers, and they buried him in Samaria. Then his son Jehoash became king in his place.

(2 Kings 13:10) 
In the thirty-seventh year of Joash, king of Judah, Jehoash, the son of Jehoahaz, began to reign over Israel in Samaria, and he ruled for sixteen years.

(2 Kings 13:11) 
And he did what was evil in the sight of the Lord. He did not turn away from any of the sins of Jeroboam, the son of Nebat, who had made Israel commit sin, but walked in them.

(2 Kings 13:12) 
Now, as for the rest of the acts of Jehoash, and everything he did, and his might in how he fought against Amaziah, king of Judah—are these not written in the book of the chronicles of the kings of Israel?

(2 Kings 13:13) 
So Jehoash rested with his fathers, and Jeroboam sat on his throne. Jehoash was buried in Samaria with the kings of Israel.

(2 Kings 13:14) 
Now Elisha became sick with the illness by which he eventually died. Then Jehoash, the king of Israel, went down to him and wept over him, saying: 'My father, my father! The chariots of Israel and its horsemen!'

(2 Kings 13:15) 
Elisha then said to him, 'Bring a bow and arrows.' When Jehoash had brought him a bow and arrows,

(2 Kings 13:16) 
Elisha said to the king of Israel, 'Place your hand upon the bow.' And Jehoash placed his hand upon it, and Elisha placed his hands over the king's hands.

(2 Kings 13:17) 
And Elisha said, 'Open the window toward the east.' When Jehoash had opened it, Elisha said, 'Shoot the arrow!' And he shot it. Then Elisha declared, 'This is the arrow of the Lord's deliverance! It is the arrow of deliverance against Syria! For you will strike Syria in Aphek until you completely destroy them.'

(2 Kings 13:18) 
And Elisha said, 'Take the arrows.' When Jehoash had taken them, Elisha again said to him, 'Strike the ground.' And he struck it three times, and then he stopped.

(2 Kings 13:19) 
Then the man of God was angry with him and said, 'If you had struck five or six times, you would have struck Syria until their complete destruction. But now, you will strike Syria only three times.'

(2 Kings 13:20) 
So Elisha died, and they buried him. And raiding parties from Moab invaded the land in that very year.

(2 Kings 13:21) 
Now it happened that some men were burying a dead person when they saw the raiding parties. So they threw the corpse into Elisha's tomb. When the dead man touched Elisha's bones, he revived and stood up on his feet.

(2 Kings 13:22) 
Indeed, throughout all the days of King Jehoahaz, Hazael, the king of Syria, had oppressed Israel.

(2 Kings 13:23) 
But the Lord had mercy on them and turned back to them because of His covenant which He had made with Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob. He did not wish to destroy them, nor to cast them utterly away from His sight, even until the present day.

(2 Kings 13:24) 
Then Hazael, the king of Syria, died, and his son Ben-Hadad reigned in his place.

(2 Kings 13:25) 
Moreover, Jehoash, the son of Jehoahaz, then recovered the cities from the hand of Ben-Hadad, the son of Hazael. These were the cities that Ben-Hadad had taken from the hand of Jehoahaz, Jehoash's father, by right of war, throughout all those days. Jehoash struck him three times, and so restored the cities to Israel.

(2 Kings 14:1) 
In the second year of Joas, the son of Joachaz and King of Israel, Amasias, the son of Joas and King of Judah, began his reign.

(2 Kings 14:2) 
He was twenty-five years old when he began to reign, and he reigned for twenty-nine years in Jerusalem. The name of his mother was Joadan, who was from Jerusalem.

(2 Kings 14:3) 
Amasias did what was right in the sight of the Lord, however, he did not do it with the same wholeheartedness as David, his father. He followed all the ways that Joas, his father, had done before him.

(2 Kings 14:4) 
Yet the high places of idolatry were not removed; the people still offered sacrifices and burned incense on those high places dedicated to false gods.

(2 Kings 14:5) 
After he had established his royal authority and secured the kingdom in his own hands, Amasias struck down his servants who had assassinated Joas, his royal father.

(2 Kings 14:6) 
But the sons of those assassins he did not put to death. He acted according to what is written in the book of the Law of Moses, as the Lord commanded, saying: 'Fathers shall not be put to death for their sons, nor shall sons be put to death for their fathers; rather, each person shall die for their own sin alone.'

(2 Kings 14:7) 
Amasias himself struck down Edom in the Valley of Salt, killing ten thousand men. He captured the city of Sela in battle, and he called its name Jecthel, which remains its name to this very day.

(2 Kings 14:8) 
Then Amasias sent messengers to Joas, the son of Joachaz and grandson of Jehu, who was King of Israel. Amasias' message was: 'Come, let us look each other in the face,' meaning, 'Let us meet in battle.'

(2 Kings 14:9) 
Joas, the King of Israel, sent this reply to Amasias, the King of Judah: 'The thistle in the field sent a message to the cedar in Lebanon, saying, "Give your daughter to my son to be his wife." But a wild beast passed by and trampled the thistle underfoot.'

(2 Kings 14:10) 
Joas continued, 'You have indeed struck down and conquered Edom, and your heart has been lifted up in pride because of it. Rejoice in your victory, but stay in your own house and enjoy your triumph. Why do you provoke evil, so that you fall, and Judah with you?'

(2 Kings 14:11) 
But Amasias did not listen to this warning. So Joas, the King of Israel, went up with his army. And he, along with Amasias, the King of Judah, met each other in battle at Beth Shemesh, a town in Judah.

(2 Kings 14:12) 
Judah was defeated by Israel, and every man of Judah fled back to his own tent, abandoning the battle.

(2 Kings 14:13) 
Joas, the King of Israel, captured Amasias, the King of Judah — the son of Joas, and grandson of Ochozias — at Beth Shemesh. Joas then brought Amasias as his prisoner to Jerusalem. There, Joas broke down the wall of Jerusalem, from the Gate of Ephraim to the Corner Gate, a distance of four hundred cubits — a significant humiliation and weakening of Judah's defenses.

(2 Kings 14:14)
